# **289 – At the Theodore Residence**

“I apologize for making such an unreasonable request right after your return from your journey.”

“Not at all. I thought it would be nice to celebrate your return. I believe having some liveliness is a good thing.”

I welcomed Princess Adriana and her party, guiding everyone through the entrance hall. Naturally, since they were all important figures, they were accompanied by knight escorts. Mildred and Mercedes. The escorts assigned by Verdgar had likely chosen people I was acquainted with.

“I’m glad to see you safe, Ambassador.”

“Thank you.”

I exchanged greetings with Mildred and the others. And then—another important figure emerged from the carriage. King Melvin and King Eberhart.

“My apologies for today, Theodore-dono.”

“…Indeed. Consider this an incognito visit, so let’s dispense with formalities today. Since this is rather sudden, please refrain from excessive courtesy. I believe your home alone is worthy of hospitality.”

It seemed King Eberhart was also interested in my house after hearing about it. That led to both King Melvin and King Eberhart deciding to come as well.

“Thank you. Well then—please come this way.”

I nodded and guided them further inside.

“I had expected as much… but you reshaped the building materials using magic and enhanced them to construct this, didn’t you?”

Old Sigmund groaned as he examined the walls and ceiling.

“As expected, I can’t find any seams… It’s like a joke of a building.”

“Indeed… Seeing this, one can understand how you managed to defeat the demons.”

Old Sigmund and Valentina nodded as if they had reached an understanding.

Miriam had previously shared her thoughts on the finished magic construction… but these two were analyzing it from a more magician-like perspective.

“The interior is lovely too. Did you do this as well?”

Princess Adriana asked.

“For the interior, I referred to architecture-related books and everyone’s opinions.”

“I see… It’s a wonderful home.”

“You honor me.”

When I guided them to the game room, exclamations of admiration escaped from someone.

“Hmm. There are so many unusual things that my eyes don’t know where to look.”

“I knew about the items in the royal castle and hot springs… but there were too many eyes around to touch them.”

…In this manner, the two princesses had shining eyes.

“I believe everyone has different preferences, so please feel free to try whatever interests you first.”

When I said this, everyone began examining whatever caught their fancy.

Elliot, Old Sigmund, Valentina, along with King Melvin and King Eberhart chose billiards. Tephra, Princess Stephania, and Princess Adriana seemed to have decided to start by looking at darts.

As for Alfred and the workshop group… they were remarkably composed, likely because they handled these items themselves. They decided to leisurely enjoy card games. Grace and the others were similar, sitting at tables to play cards.

Mildred and Mercedes were strictly on escort duty this time… but perhaps because they didn’t need to be too tense, their expressions appeared quite calm.

“I saw the soldiers at the royal castle happily playing darts… but I couldn’t possibly join them. Just like with the hot springs, there were too many people watching, you see.”

“I see… That makes sense.”

So Princess Stephania had been restraining herself.

“I’d like to visit the hot springs too… It’s a place blessed by Tephra-sama, isn’t it?”

“Indeed. Theodore prepared a ritual site to welcome me. That place has the effect of granting power to spirits and fairies.”

Tephra said happily while throwing darts. Hearing her words, King Melvin spoke up.

“…Hmm. Come to think of it, since nothing bad happened I didn’t contact you about it… but something slightly unusual occurred regarding the ritual site.”

“Did something happen?”

“You saw the fairies when we went flower viewing before, correct? It seems they’ve drifted over and settled at the ritual site. A flower garden has formed around the gazebo there.”

I noticed Seraphina showing a happy expression at King Melvin’s words.

…Well now. Just like that mountain slope, the ritual site must be a comfortable place for fairies, I suppose. Fairies are a type of spirit. It must indeed be comfortable for them.

“I don’t dislike seeing spirits and fairies getting along with humans. I’d like to welcome those beings as well.”

“If the fairies’ actions are harmless, then it’s fine.”

…Though the area around the ritual site is becoming increasingly otherworldly.

“I haven’t heard of any problems occurring so far. The shrine maidens are usually at the ritual site, and they seem to be managing well.”

“That’s good to hear.”

Regarding the hot spring facility, it seemed they’d been closing early in the evening during my absence to focus on inspections and maintenance, concerned that there might be issues they couldn’t handle.

“—In that case, would it be possible to reserve it for private use at night?”

“That it would. The night of the full moon is approaching as well. How about attending the theater, then relaxing at the hot springs while we discuss matters?”

The night of the full moon. That would mean Irmhild’s performance. Irmhild placed a hand on her chest as if to say “leave it to me” and smiled.

With the location and timing for discussions decided, everyone began enjoying the games in the game room.

“Hmm. You made this with magic too, didn’t you?”

“…Could it be that you also thought of it and were the first to create it?”

“Yeah. Both Theodore.”

Sheila, who had been explaining how to play billiards to Valentina, nodded.

Elliot, with a slightly strained smile, took his stance with the cue and struck the cue ball, the sound of billiard balls colliding echoing through the game room.

“This is quite… what should I say, a crisp sound.”

“That’s right. It’s a nice sound. Hmm… The feel when striking and the sound when the balls drop are both pleasant too.”

Valentina nodded at Elliot’s words.

“Hmm. I heard you’re selling these. I’d like to have one in Silvatoria as well. My long convalescence has made my body sluggish. Such convenient pastimes would be quite useful.”

Just then, Claire and Cyrille brought shaved ice and carbonated drinks. Old Sigmund’s eyes widened at seeing them using the Humanization Spell.

“…My, my. I had prepared myself to some extent… but I’m still astonished.”

“You honor us.”

Claire and the others smiled and bowed to Old Sigmund, who was giving a wry smile.

“Drinks and ice sweets are unusual items too. Could it be that these as well…?”

“Yeah.”

When Sheila nodded, Old Sigmund’s mouth twitched.

“What in the world led to this situation? Well, if I were to be surprised every time you come up with something new and create it, it would be too much for me to handle… but having servants like Arachne, Centaurs, and Sirens isn’t something that can simply be called unusual.”

“If I were to explain the circumstances, it would take too long and we might go off track. Would it be acceptable to discuss this another day?”

When I glanced over, Claudia was giving a wry smile. King Melvin showed a similar reaction.

“Indeed. Verdgar has adopted a policy of accepting friendly monsters as much as possible. The background leading to that is as Theodore says. Starting on that topic now would likely lead us nowhere.”

Since we’re forming a united front against the demons, there are aspects we must disclose to King Eberhart and the others, especially Old Sigmund… but well, today is also a celebration of our return, so I’d prefer to avoid topics that would lead to work discussions.

“…Hmm. Indeed. For today, I won’t inquire deeply into the circumstances and simply enjoy myself.”

Old Sigmund said this and took a sip of the carbonated drink… his eyes widening for a moment before he finished it and grinned.

“Interesting. I like this.”

“You can make this with magic tools too, and we sell them.”

“Um. Al—fred, right? I’ll buy all of it.”

“Please get some for me too.”

Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana made quite generous statements to Alfred.

If this means more customers for Silvatoria, it should be welcomed. Delivery should be possible using Teleportation Magic though…

“Thank you for your purchase.”

Alfred answered with a wry smile at Princess Stephania’s words.

“This will be your guest room.”

The banquet was in full swing. While everyone was playing games, night had deepened considerably, so Old Sigmund and Valentina decided to stay overnight.

The royal family members would be returning to the royal castle, but they expressed interest in seeing the guest rooms, which is why I’m showing them around.

“You can cool or heat the room with magic tools. Nothing left to be desired, eh?”

“Silvatoria, as a Magic Kingdom, must learn from this as well.”

“My, my. Absolutely.”

Old Sigmund and King Eberhart nodded in agreement.

“You can climb up there. What an interesting structure.”

“This is lovely. Can you place bedding up there too?”

And as I expected—Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana seemed to really like the loft. I’m glad they’re enjoying themselves to the fullest.

+++

# **290 – Memory of Battle**

“I apologize for the intrusion with so many people today.”

“Not at all. Well then, good night.”

“Indeed. Farewell.”

“Thank you for today.”

I saw King Melvin and Princess Stephania off to the entrance. After exchanging greetings, they boarded their carriage.

“Well then, Ambassador-dono. We shall take our leave as well.”

“Yes. Please be careful on your journey.”

I also exchanged words with Mildred and Mercedes. And so, King Melvin and the others returned to the Royal Castle.

It was a quiet night. Perhaps it was the lingering memory of all the earlier commotion, but it felt especially so. As the sound of horse hooves and carriage wheels faded into the distance, only the moonlit night streets remained behind.

Now then, Elliot, Old Sigmund, and Valentina were staying overnight. First, I should show Elliot and the others to their guest rooms.

“You can adjust the temperature—raise it or lower it—with this Magic Tool,” I explained once more the functions and usage of the Magic Tool in the guest room to those staying over.

“Understood.”

“When the bath is ready, a servant will come to call you. It shouldn’t take too long, so please relax in the meantime.”

“Thank you. Then, we’ll take it easy for a while.”

Elliot nodded.

“Good night, Elliot brother.”

“Good night, Ashley. Well then, Theodore-dono.”

“Yes. Good night.”

After exchanging pre-sleep greetings, Elliot closed the door with a gentle smile.

Next, I showed Valentina to her room.

“I haven’t left the student alliance much, so I think Theodore-kun’s home feels safe.”

Valentina said this with a smile.

Indeed, that’s true. Valentina must have been a child when the memory seal was placed, and I imagine she’s been through a lot, being tossed about… yet she doesn’t show a single unpleasant expression.

I hear she’s inherited several magics as part of the elders’ clan… That’s probably why she couldn’t remain an outsider.

The fact that she’s striving to assist Old Sigmund right after awakening suggests she has a much stronger will than her soft demeanor implies. I think it’s fitting that she was close with Mother.

“…During your stay in Termwills, please feel free to stay at this house without hesitation. If anything comes up, let me know. As for the bath, I believe it can be prepared quickly.”

“Thank you. It’s a nice room, so I think I can rest well.”

Valentina’s words made me smile wryly, feeling a bit tickled.

“Thank you. Well then, good night.”

“Yes, good night.”

After exchanging greetings with Valentina, I went to Old Sigmund’s room.

“My apologies for the trouble.”

“Not at all, Grandfather.”

Old Sigmund also smiled, but then his expression suddenly turned serious.

“…About your father…”

“Yes.”

I had informed him that Father would arrive tomorrow or the day after. It wasn’t hard to imagine that Old Sigmund had complex feelings toward Father. He probably wanted to blame him for not being able to save Mother, and likely felt self-reproach as well.

As for me… I don’t want to see their relationship worsen. Even if there’s no clear answer as to what could have been done better… from my position, I can say it wasn’t Father’s fault, nor the elders’.

“I think… at that time six years ago, no one else could have done anything about it. Sometimes I think, if only I could have used Circulating Ki back then, if I could have fought.”

“…That itself is an unreasonable expectation. Even you now are beyond what was hoped for. No… perhaps it’s because of that that you are as you are now.”

The current me. I don’t know why I became like this, but I can definitely say that the reason I dive into labyrinths and try to accumulate my own strength lies there.

“What do you… think? But I’ve always wanted to become stronger. I still do. I’m happy that I have enough power to fight demons.”

“…I see.”

“Yes. When Father returned from Termwills, he was deeply saddened. So I don’t think of blaming him.”

I remember that expression of Father’s, and how he shed tears at the gravesite… that figure.

“…I’ll keep that in mind.”

“Of course, it’s not your fault or the elders’ either.”

At my words, Old Sigmund showed a slightly surprised expression.

Yes… Without that incident, the current me and Grace wouldn’t exist.

“Please, don’t blame yourself.”

Old Sigmund looked at me for a while, then nodded quietly.

“…Understood. But let me ask you one thing. About… what Patricia fought against…”

The story of the King of Deathly Slumber attacking Verdgar is somewhat famous… but by that time, the elders were probably cut off from outside information.

“It was a demon who spread a disease called the King of Deathly Slumber. …Do you know of it?”

“Deathly Slumber… a disease-spreading demon.”

High fever, coma, and weakness. A slow but certain bringer of death. That’s why his epithet is Deathly Slumber.

“Demons… when given epithets by humans, they apparently enjoy using them as their own titles. They know that infamy becomes their sustenance.”

“Indeed. Once a powerful demon rampages, their activities tend to calm down because of it. Hence, humans try to pass down the tales. But that one is different. The demon who spreads the sleeping death disease has been known since ancient times, but he doesn’t reveal his name. I hear he’s an evil being who doesn’t proclaim his own name and delights in killing.”

That’s right. So his name remains unknown, and he’s simply called the King of Deathly Slumber.

An ancient demon who doesn’t proclaim his name to humans, killing whimsically when hungry. That’s why he’s called a king with fear.

“After rampaging in neighboring countries, he suddenly appeared within Verdgar… spreading disease everywhere… eventually crossing the Barony of Silun and coming to Gartner County. He avoided Termwills probably because, for him, it would become sustenance later.”

“…That would be so.”

The greater the fear, lament, and sorrow of the people left behind, the more it becomes the demon’s sustenance. So I think he avoided Termwills. If the urban population had survived, their emotions would have entirely become his nourishment.

In fact, in other countries, he didn’t cause damage in urban areas, and even in attacked places, he seemed to leave survivors to pass down tales of the King of Deathly Slumber.

Throughout history, battles with demons have been long, but the reason humans haven’t been destroyed despite demons having overwhelmingly superior power probably lies there.

“And Patricia defeated him, did she?”

“Yes. There was someone who fled from the Barony of Silun. Mother heard the circumstances from that person… and confronted him.”

Upon hearing the story of the person who fled from the Barony of Silun, Mother intercepted him. The adventurers present in Gartner County also cooperated in fighting the King of Deathly Slumber.

Mother flew with alchemically crafted wings. Using Teleportation Magic, Sealing Technique, every technique at her disposal, she fought the demon in the skies above the county. The intersection of light and darkness. Bursting sparks. A giant Magic Circle. Countless Magic Slaves. Fire and lightning. Explosions and roars.

I… watched it all, together with Grace.

She beheaded the demon with a blade of light extending from her staff—I’ll never forget that scene. The demon turning to dust and scattering, and Mother, having been exposed to miasma at close range, falling onto the snow—

When I recounted that battle and its outcome, Old Sigmund let out a deep breath.

“…She was brave, wasn’t she? Patricia.”

“—Yes.”

Old Sigmund narrowed his eyes, smiled sadly, and nodded.

“…Then, I won’t blame your father. Patricia splendidly protected you and your fiancée Grace, didn’t she? She upheld our clan’s and our ancestors’ will, protecting what was important through to the end. As a father, he should be proud of such a daughter. To blame someone for the result would only tarnish Patricia’s feelings.”

“That… might be true.”

I returned a smile to Old Sigmund.

“You must be tired too, and I made you listen to a long story. My apologies.”

“Not at all. But I think I’ll take it easy and rest today as well.”

“Indeed. Well then, until tomorrow.”

“Yes. See you tomorrow.”

The door to Old Sigmund’s room closed.

“Theo…”

Grace’s voice.

“Sorry. Did I say something that brought back memories?”

When I answered, Grace hugged me tightly.

“No. It’s a painful memory, but I don’t want to forget it. It makes me happy… to know there are people who are proud of her.”

“…Yeah. That’s right.”

Grace and I embraced for a while. Then we slowly separated.

“Lady Lisa’s story of that battle has also been a constant support for me.”

“Yeah. Ashley.”

I drew Ashley close. Ashley pressed her cheek against my chest, clinging to me.

“Theodore. Cheer up, okay?”

She said in a bell-like voice. I hugged Marlene, who was looking up at me, and answered.

“…Yeah. I’m fine.”

Ashley and Marlene. I felt their warmth and heartbeat. When I separated from them, this time Claudia pulled me close, embracing my head.

“—I remember a little about when she came to the Full Moon Labyrinth.”

Claudia said this while holding me.

“…You saw Mother?”

“Probably. At that time, I didn’t know her name, and we didn’t exchange words. But thinking back now, I believe so.”

I recall in Adventurer Guild Master Auria’s story, there was talk of Mother going to the Full Moon Labyrinth to rescue adventurers.

“When I sensed something wrong and went to check, she was fighting monsters. I understood she came to help those who had lost their way, so I also suppressed the monsters for a little while.”

“I see… Thank you.”

When I thanked her, Claudia smiled and loosened her grip.

Then, I drew Rosemary close. Rosemary showed a slightly flustered reaction but then relaxed into it, wrapping her arms around my neck.

“…I’m not in a position to say anything particularly admirable. But as one born into royalty, if I may say so, I think she’s a person worthy of respect.”

As royalty, huh. I think that’s the highest praise coming from Rosemary.

“Is that so? Regardless of methods, if Marie became queen, I think she would have fulfilled her duties properly.”

“Really? I’m glad you say that, Theodore.”

Rosemary seemed to give a small laugh.

By the time she slowly pulled away, she was already hiding her mouth with her feather fan, so I couldn’t see her expression.

“…Well then, let’s rest easy too.”

Turning around, I smiled and nodded at Sheila, Irmhild, and Seraphina, and they returned the smiles.

+++

# **291 – The Workshop and the Sage**

Morning—. I slipped out of my bedroom more leisurely than usual, tidied up my appearance, and headed toward the newly expanded main dining hall with everyone. Since we had guests staying over, it was decided we’d have breakfast together today.

“Good morning.”

“Good morning.”

When I greeted Cecilia in the morning, she cheerfully returned the greeting. The main dining hall already seemed to have the food served, with a delicious aroma wafting through the air.

The source of the smell was probably onion soup. There were also sandwiches, salad, sausages, and omelets—all visually vibrant.

“Good morning.”

Elliot, Tephra, Old Sigmund, and Valentina arrived at the dining hall one after another.

“Good morning. Did you sleep well last night?”

“Well, yes. It was quiet and comfortable.”

“I slept soundly until morning.”

So said Elliot and Valentina.

“The bath was quite splendid as well. It was a good soak.”

“I’m glad to hear that.”

I smiled back at Old Sigmund.

“Perhaps because Seraphina has settled here, it feels quite comfortable for me as well.”

So said Tephra.

“Cleaning yesterday was fun since I got to chat with Tephra about various things.”

Seraphina, perched on my shoulder, said cheerfully. Hmm. Perhaps spirits become more active at night… But if they’re getting along well, that’s what matters most.

Well then. Now that everyone’s gathered, it’s time for breakfast.

“What are the plans for today?”

Rosemary asked.

“A few miscellaneous tasks. Going to the workshop to discuss magic tool creation with Alfred, sending Marquis Zilbolt back to his territory. And probably performing the familiar contract ceremony for Marlene’s familiar.”

I should get these things done before Father and Kennel arrive.

“…Magic tools, huh. So you’re making your magic tools with that boy.”

“Yes. Alfred is a magic engineer. I write the spell formulas, and Alfred turns them into magic tools. Metalworking and such is handled by Viola the blacksmith—that’s the flow.”

“So when we provide technical cooperation, it would be in coordination with him. We’ve been told to cooperate with Theodore-kun’s friend, the magic engineer.”

Valentina said.

“I think that’s how it will be. We’re developing various things, and since he’s trustworthy, the flow would be that anything we’d be troubled to have leaked goes through Alfred.”

“In that case, it would be good for us to accompany you and properly introduce ourselves.”

Matters related to the airship would likely be handled at the workshop. Since Alfred said he works at the workshop, I’ll head there after breakfast.

Marquis Zilbolt is staying at the royal castle with his wife Belinda and their daughter Romina. With one incident resolved and the marquis family’s honor restored, they’ve returned safely and apparently wanted some time together as a family. Marquis Zilbolt will return to Silvatoria, but it seems Romina will be studying abroad at Peresford Academy.

Since the marquis is supposed to return today… well, I’ll have him contact me when it’s convenient for him.

“I see. So we embed this gem into the giant arrow.”

I went to the workshop and reintroduced Old Sigmund and Valentina to Alfred and the other workshop members.

After properly introducing everyone to each other again, I showed Alfred the items I received as rewards from the Vinesdora royal castle’s treasure room.

“Viola, what do you think?”

“Hmm, hmm. I don’t think it will take that much work. If they attract each other when activated… how about making a new gauntlet or bracelet and embedding the other gem there?”

Viola looked at the gems and said that.

“Ah. That would be wonderful. If you can incorporate it into equipment, I won’t have to take it out when using it. And if it were just a gem, I’d be worried about dropping it or something.”

Irmhild laughed cheerfully and clasped her hands in front of her chest.

“What about this gauntlet? Can you adjust it?”

So said Sheila. The Thunder Gauntlet that Sheila chose also needed some adjustments to fit her properly.

“Um… yes. This should be fine. I just need to rework some of the metal fittings and replace the strap, so could I take Sheila-san’s measurements?”

“Mm. That’s our Viola.”

“Fufufu.”

Viola seemed pleased by Sheila’s comment and let out a soft laugh.

“My bracelet fits just right. I don’t think it needs any adjustments.”

Grace said while wearing her bracelet.

“Since this functions entirely as a magic tool, if the size didn’t fit, adjustments would have been difficult. It’s quite a good item.”

“Thank you.”

Grace and Viola exchanged such conversation.

“Marlene, what did you receive? That bird?”

When Alfred asked, Marlene brought forward the bird statue that was following slightly behind her, smiling.

I should provide additional explanation about the bird.

“It’s a bird-type… magical creature, I suppose. It seems it can become a familiar, and we plan to perform the contract ceremony later.”

“They say bird familiars are convenient.”

“It has the form of a raptor… shall we make a gauntlet for Marlene-sama as well?”

“Like a falconer?”

“Yes.”

Perhaps pleased by Viola’s words, Marlene nodded repeatedly. Viola broke into a smile at Marlene’s reaction.

“So we have the giant arrow processing and three gauntlet jobs. Grace’s bracelet seems fine since the size is perfect… But we have a big job coming up too, so I’ll proceed with Ignis’s inspection. The armor and skeleton both seem fine though.”

Rosemary said while touching Ignis’s shoulder.

“A big job, huh. Yeah. As a technician, being involved in that is exciting.”

Alfred said happily.

The big job… meaning the airship. It hasn’t been decided yet whether we’ll build a new one or modify an existing ship…

“Since our full cooperation is already decided. We’ve already received permission from His Majesty Eberhart and His Majesty Melvin to proceed as we see fit.”

I see. It seems they settled those matters at the royal castle last night.

I’ll be responsible for creating the ship’s body using that magical power conversion armor. Alfred will process the completed armor plates. We need to create circuits to guide magical power to the magic tools that provide propulsion.

But I’ll need to prepare the armor plates in a state where they can be processed using special magic. Since they absorb impacts and magic, unless I use spell formulas to make them maintainable, proper processing won’t be possible. Maintaining the armor’s fixed state will also be my responsibility.

There are several other points to work out regarding the airship.

“I heard about improving the airship’s efficiency—do you have any ideas?”

“Yes, I have a few things in mind. For example—”

I created a simple model of an airship using wood magic. The main body followed the ship shape like previous airshps, but the airplane-like wings extending from both sides were slightly different.

I controlled the air using wind magic. When I adjusted the airflow above and below the wings separately, the model floated in the air.

Old Sigmund and Valentina stared wide-eyed. Not just the two of them, but Rosemary, Alfred, Ashley, and Elliot—those knowledgeable about magic—seemed to realize that it wasn’t floating because I was using Levitation.

“This is… not Levitation, is it?”

“No. It’s the same principle as a fore-and-aft sail on a sailing ship. Fore-and-aft sails convert wind power into forward motion… but this directly manipulates the wind to create upward lifting force.”

“I see, fore-and-aft sails…”

In other words, it’s lift. I’m using wind magic to manipulate air pressure to make it float. By incorporating wind magic above and below the wings to lift it up, I can assist the force that makes the airship float.

Also, by manipulating this lift, it should be possible to turn left and right. The heart of the airship maintains overall balance… but I might need to synchronize it with that.

“Next would be strengthening propulsion, I suppose. I’m thinking about using a combination of fire and wind magic to take in air from the front and release it from the back to accelerate…”

Well, too much acceleration would just increase danger, so moderate performance would be fine.

When I glanced at Old Sigmund, he wore a stunned expression, but he shook his head slightly and spoke as if collecting himself.

“…Compound magic, huh. To make it into a magic tool, we’ll need high-quality magic stones.”

“The technology to imbue magic stones with specific elements… does Verdgar have that?”

Valentina asked.

“You can do that?”

“Yes. It’s one of the spell formulas I’ve inherited. So if we have large magic stones, I think we can be quite flexible.”

Saying that, Valentina smiled.

Hmm… That’s good. Being able to create things like the fire magic stone extracted from the Flame Demon at will… seems like it would expand what we can do in various ways. We just need to procure originally high-quality magic stones. That’s where labyrinths really shine.

+++

# **292 – The Return of the Marquis**

While we were discussing various matters about the airship, a message came through the communication device. It was from Mercedes. According to a message from Marquis Zilbolt, he was asking if he could visit now.

I had told him he could decide when to return via teleportation and to let me know when the time came, but it seemed he couldn’t leave his territory unattended for too long, so I had received word that he would be returning today. Even so, he probably wanted to make some time to spend with Romina.

It appeared Marquis Zilbolt was being escorted by the knight order, so in any case, he would likely be accompanied to my house.

Therefore, I replied that I was in the workshop and asked if they could guide the Marquis there. While waiting for Marquis Zilbolt, I continued discussing the airship.

“Having piloted the airship this far… I’ve come to realize there are indeed many blind spots,” I remarked.

Old Sigmund nodded as if he had similar thoughts.

“Indeed. The fact that we can’t see below at all is problematic.”

“For this issue, I’ve thought of several methods. First, we could have wyverns or crew members equipped with aerial combat gear accompany the ship. There’s also the simple method of installing windows on the hull bottom…”

Having wyverns accompany the ship would be similar to the relationship between an aircraft carrier and its planes. This would also make use of the airship’s carrying capacity, and having escorts for the airship should solve the blind spot problem to some extent.

“I see… From the way you speak, it seems you have other ideas as well…”

“I was thinking of either making the ship itself a magical creature… or incorporating magical creatures as components.”

For example, gargoyles or golems. Like Rosemary’s dolls. Rosemary showed a thoughtful expression at my words.

“So you mean incorporating magical creatures as components to eliminate blind spots?” she said.

Rosemary’s simple-type dolls had the ability to combine with other dolls to form larger ones. This would probably be her area of expertise.

“Exactly. We could incorporate magical creatures with vision into the hull and link them with crystal balls through contract magic.”

“Like a familiar contract?”

“Yes. Though we’d need to modify the spell formula for the contract magic somewhat…”

When I looked at Alfred as I said this, he smiled and nodded as if he understood perfectly.

“I’ve researched various contract magic that connects objects to objects. I think we can apply that knowledge,” he said.

Due to the communication device development, we already had the know-how for implementing contract magic into magic tools.

Anyway, by linking vision to crystal balls, we would be able to see places that would normally be out of sight as images. It would be like a car’s backup monitor.

“Next would be… armaments designed to counter demons. I don’t think ordinary projectiles would hit demons that fly around.”

“…That would likely be true. What Zadias had installed on his ship probably wouldn’t be effective against demons either.”

Old Sigmund nodded. I turned to Valentina and asked,

“Earlier you mentioned that magic stones can be given specific directionality. Would that work with somewhat special things like the Moon Goddess’s Blessing or Cursed Melody?”

“…I haven’t tried it… but I think it might be possible?”

Valentina answered after thinking for a moment.

“I’m thinking of mounting magic tools that can give such things directionality and project them. The idea is to disrupt the flight control of demons that come within the airship’s range, then have accompanying dragon knights or combat personnel intercept them.”

The concept is similar to acoustic weapons. I believe they were non-lethal weapons intended for riot control, but disrupting control in aerial combat and then attacking with wyvern corps seems quite effective.

There’s also the convenience of simply projecting to be effective. If we can make the gun mounts rotate up, down, left, and right, evasion would be difficult. From the enemy’s perspective, easy approaches to the airship would be blocked.

“Hmm… What needs to be made is becoming clearer…”

“Yes. Next would be estimating the required amount of materials, and for magic stones and other shortages, we could procure them from the labyrinth, I suppose.”

Just then, a knock sounded. Talcott appeared at the door, followed by Cindy, the object of Talcott’s one-sided affection.

“What is it?” Alfred asked.

“It seems we have visitors. Dame Mercedia and members of the Zilbolt Marquis household have arrived,” Talcott replied.

Since Talcott also serves as Alfred’s bodyguard, he doubles as security for the workshop. Announcing visitors is also part of his duties.

Cindy sometimes helps in the workshop, and today she seemed to be keeping Talcott company while he was on guard duty. It appears their relationship is progressing relatively well.

“Understood. Our discussion has reached a good stopping point anyway, so please show them in.”

“Understood.”

“I’ll prepare some tea,” Cindy said.

Talcott bowed and returned. Cindy seemed to have decided to prepare tea.

Shortly after, guided by Talcott, Mercedes and three members of the Zilbolt Marquis household arrived.

“Hello.”

“Yes. Hello, Ambassador-dono. And everyone else.”

We exchanged greetings with the arriving group.

“Are you ready now?” I asked.

“Yes. We were able to spend some leisurely time together as a family,” Marquis Zilbolt said with a smile.

After drinking tea and relaxing for a while, we moved to the ritual site. Teleporting from the ritual site apparently significantly reduces Claudia’s consumption. This is because we can borrow power from both the spell formula and Tephra.

“Ahaha, it’s true! Everyone’s here!”

As Seraphina spread her arms and flew forward, fairies appeared from among the flowers, drawn out with smiling faces. Seraphina happily spun around in the air, chasing the fairies and being chased by them.

The ritual site… had become a place where colorful flowers bloomed in profusion. Combined with being filled with unique magical power, it was quite an unreal scene.

The fairies also flew around us, went to greet Tephra and Claudia… They felt much friendlier than before.

“Hmm. This is good. Truly good.”

As for Tephra, the master of the ritual site, she was in quite a good mood. She seemed favorable to the fairies settling here. She was letting them sit on her shoulders and fingers.

“Now then, Romina. Do your best.”

“Yes. To make up for having been protected by Father until now, I want to study hard and broaden my knowledge.”

Nearby, Marquis Zilbolt, Lady Belinda, and Romina were exchanging words. Since we left the Zilbolt Marquis territory, we don’t know the situation there, so we plan to accompany Marquis Zilbolt to confirm his safety.

“It’s unfortunate that you have to return, busy as you are, when the theater performance is just a few days away,” Alfred said, watching them.

“…If the consumption for teleportation magic to the Marquis territory is small, could we invite the two of them on the day?”

“Yes. That shouldn’t be a problem,” Claudia said, narrowing her eyes.

In that case, why not invite all three members of the Marquis household? I tried conveying this idea to the three of them.

“That would be delightful… but wouldn’t it be a burden?”

“Frequent use would be problematic, but the consumption doesn’t seem to be large, and considering this is for the victory celebration…”

“Is that so…? Then we’ll gratefully accept your kind offer.”

At these words, Romina showed a happy expression.

“Then I’ll send you off. I think we’ll appear in the air, so please use Levitation.”

“Understood.”

The Marquis used Levitation on himself and Lady Belinda, then put his arm around his wife’s shoulder. The lady also cheerfully leaned against the Marquis. They really seemed like a devoted couple.

“Well then, we’ll be off for a bit.”

“Hmm. We’ll wait here then,” Old Sigmund nodded.

“This way.”

Following Claudia, we moved to the air above the ritual site’s accommodation facilities. As soon as the Magic Circle deployed, we were enveloped in light—and when I opened my eyes, the scenery and temperature had completely changed.

Marquis Zilbolt’s castle was visible below us.

As we descended into the castle’s courtyard, retainers came running with surprised expressions. Among them were the Knight Order Commander and the magician from the Marquis territory whom we had met before. They were the pillars of the Marquis territory.

“Oh, Marquis… and Lady Belinda too. Have you returned?”

“Yes. Is everything normal?”

“Yes! Those influenced by Zadias are quietly staying in the prison cells.”

Marquis Zilbolt nodded and informed them that Zadias had been defeated.

“Zadias was defeated by Theodore-dono here, and His Majesty Eberhart has disinherited him. He’ll never see the light of day again.”

“Oh…”

The Knight Order Commander and the magician closed their eyes as if looking up to heaven with deep emotion. King Eberhart had also restored Marquis Zilbolt’s honor. For them too, this must have been a welcome outcome.

+++

# **293 – Remembrance**

“Thank you so much, Theodore-dono, and everyone else.”

“Please give our regards to Her Highness Stephania as well.”

“Understood. I will certainly convey them.”

The Knight Order Commander and the magician expressed their gratitude with deep bows.

“I truly wish we could welcome you with the entire territory’s hospitality,” said Lady Belinda with regret.

“We still have many matters to attend to over there… Well, I’m also curious about the hot springs of Mt. Tephra, so we’ll visit again when we have time.”

“Please do come. We shall prepare a proper welcoming feast then.”

“If it’s hot springs you seek, there are excellent spots in the mountains. I shall guide you,” offered Marquis Zilbolt with a smile.

“Yes, we’d love that.”

“If any problems arise, the shrine maidens can offer prayers to the Moon Goddess, and we’ll be able to detect it. Though going through Tephra works too,” Claudia added.

“Understood.”

Marquis Zilbolt nodded at Claudia’s words. Since they had given Tephra a communication device, they should be able to detect any abnormalities in the mountains.

“What about you, Tephra?”

“I shall wander the mountains for a while. After relaxing a bit, I’ll come visit you all.”

“Got it. Just contact us, and we’ll come pick you up at the ritual site.”

“Mm. Farewell for now.”

Tephra nodded contentedly and flew off toward the mountains.

“Well then—we should head back too.”

“Yes. We look forward to the theater invitation.”

After exchanging such farewells with Marquis Zilbolt, we returned to the ritual site via Claudia’s teleportation magic.

“—Welcome back.”

“Yeah, we’re home.”

Alfred and the others were drinking tea in the gazebo.

Old Sigmund glanced at Claudia for a moment, but since we had informed him that we would discuss matters with King Melvin present as well, he didn’t press for details.

Given that he only knew of teleportation magic as theoretical knowledge, he was probably curious about Claudia’s background. Her refined demeanor and the hints of high status she exuded made it understandable.

“My apologies for the delayed explanation.”

“Hmm. No matter. There are many matters regarding Silvatoria that require discretion, after all. Verdgar, too, being an ancient land, must have its share of complexities.”

Old Sigmund said this with a wry smile.

Now then. The dragon palanquin carrying Father and the others should arrive sometime tonight.

We need to finish what must be done before then. After seeing off Marquis Zilbolt, the next task is Marlene’s familiar contract.

“Marlene. Sorry to keep you waiting.”

When I called out to her, Marlene smiled, led the falcon over, and hurried closer with quick steps.

“Marie. The catalyst.”

“Right.”

She retrieved the ritual catalysts, silver plates, and other items from the magic bag.

We proceeded with the contract ceremony using the altar in the ritual site. Unlike when we summoned Lavigne, we knew from the start that the falcon, being a magical creature, was docile, so there was no need to construct a barrier. We filled a silver plate with water, reflecting the celestial map on the ceiling as we advanced the ritual.

“Marlene. Do you remember the steps?”

Marlene held the ritual rapier and nodded firmly. Standing across the altar from the falcon… she let a drop of blood fall into the water. Closing her eyes once, she took a deep breath, then gazed straight at the falcon as a clear chant spun from her lips.

“Here, I declare my name… and grant you a name, to forge an eternal covenant.”

The chant was slightly awkward, but the words were firm. Dipping her fingertips into the water mirror, Marlene continued the incantation.

“My name is Marlene Vulcadil Fobrester. Your name shall be… Eclair.”

The moment she spoke the name, the falcon—Eclair—let out a cry.

Hmm. It seems the contract was successfully formed.

Eclair flew around Marlene joyfully, then landed as if to greet her, bowing her head to Marlene.

“Well done, Marlene.”

When Claudia spoke with a gentle expression, Marlene turned toward her, beaming happily, and hugged Claudia.

“Nice to meet you, Eclair,” said Grace.

Eclair came before Grace and, like a gentleman placing a hand on his waist to bow, moved her wings in a bow.

She then hopped lightly from spot to spot, greeting each person present one by one. She came before me too and bowed. …She seems quite intelligent.

“Alright. Eclair has a proper name now… Shall we return to the gazebo and relax?”

As I collected the ritual tools, I suggested this to everyone, and they nodded, leaving the ritual site.

“Theodore-sama.”

Then, Ashley approached to speak.

“Hm? What is it?”

“Just now, I received a message from the butler via the communication device. I believe the content is something you should be informed of.”

I see. Let me take a look at Ashley’s communication device. It read:

『Lord Elliot’s fiancée is here. She wishes to accompany us—is that acceptable?』

…Ah. I see. That must be a matter from when the previous Baron Silun—Ashley’s father—was still alive… If Elliot was meant to be the heir, it wouldn’t be strange for him to have a fiancée.

“I haven’t been told much about Lord Elliot’s fiancée by the butler, and my own memories are vague… But if we’re to discuss the Barony of Silun, it’s something we cannot avoid.”

“Indeed. We can’t avoid talking about it.”

Given that Kennel referred to her as his fiancée in the present tense, it seems the person is still unmarried.

Since Elliot was presumed dead in a shipwreck, Kennel probably didn’t convey the details to Ashley. That was likely Kennel’s own form of consideration, but now that Elliot is alive, it’s not necessarily invalid.

“Elliot, do you have a moment?”

I informed him of the situation as well. When I told him that Kennel was asking to bring his fiancée along, he showed a slightly surprised reaction but quickly regained his composure and said,

“Then… could you please inform Kennel to bring her along?”

“Understood.”

I nodded. Ashley relayed that message to Kennel via the communication device.

“If it’s not too much trouble, could you tell me what kind of person she is?”

“…Well, her name is Camilla. She’s the daughter of a retired knight… Apparently, while my father was traveling within the territory, he was attacked by monsters in a nearby forest and was aided by Camilla’s father. As a token of gratitude, he invited them to a banquet, and during that event, they hit it off, leading to the arrangement of her becoming my fiancée.”

“I see…”

So she’s likely the daughter of a local notable? What happened after that… Elliot says he doesn’t know. If we had informed him about the communication device earlier, he might have contacted and confirmed with Kennel…

Of course, due to confidentiality, there were parts we couldn’t reveal until returning to Termwills.

“I’m acquainted with Camilla’s father as well. He grew disillusioned with the capital, retired from the knight order, and chose to seclude himself in the countryside… He doesn’t seem like the type to be obsessed with power,” Elliot added.

Hmm… Judging from Elliot’s assessment of her character… if we properly discuss matters with Camilla’s father, the barony situation should be manageable. They’re probably aware that Ashley has succeeded as the lord. In that case, it would be best to settle things clearly to prevent anyone from using her to stir up trouble.

Since it also involves Elliot’s future position, it will likely require discussions with King Melvin present as well.

“Then, I’ll inform His Majesty Melvin about this matter as well.”

“My apologies for the trouble.”

Saying this, Elliot bowed his head quietly.

“Are you acquainted with Miss Camilla as well?”

“Yes. We often played together when we were young. She’s two years older than me… To me, she felt more like an older sister than a fiancée… I see. So she hasn’t married… If I caused her any sadness, I feel truly sorry for that.”

I see. If she was older than Elliot, then from Camilla’s perspective, Elliot might not have been like a younger brother but recognized properly as a male fiancé.

Elliot didn’t return… and six years passed.

If that has left lingering effects, it explains why Ashley barely remembers Camilla and why Kennel never brought her up.

Because she would see Elliot’s resemblance in Ashley… Camilla probably wanted to keep her distance from the Silun baronial family.

…Yes. Since this stems from the King of Deathly Slumber, I too hope this matter can be settled where it ought to be.

+++

# **294 – Reunion at Dusk**

A short while after Ashley replied to Kennel, my communication device received a call this time. It was from Father. He wrote that he’d arrive at Termwills by evening.

I’d thought they would stay overnight in the Barony of Silun before coming… but since they’d contacted us in advance, they must have prepared everything in the Barony of Silun as well.

Still, it’s a bit of a forced march, but perhaps both Father and Kennel are feeling somewhat impatient.

“Father says he’s coming. Should we go meet them partway?”

Even though it’s a dragon palanquin, since they’ll be traveling at night, we should provide an escort of sorts… It would be more reassuring if we went to meet them.

…Yeah. Let’s take the dragon palanquin too, and all go to meet them. It probably doesn’t warrant sending an airship. That would attract too much unwanted attention.

“Let’s prepare the dragon palanquin. Lindwurm is in the house’s inner courtyard, right? We need to go meet them.”

“Understood.”

“Then, please allow me to accompany you on Saphir as well.”

Saying this, Elliot also stood up. Of course, there was no reason to refuse. Elliot probably wants to meet them as soon as possible too.

“Well then… we’ll be going for a bit. Father does have a mansion in Termwills, but I don’t think he’s contacted that place yet… So he’ll probably come to my house instead.”

When I said this, Old Sigmund nodded.

“Hmm… I’d like to think quietly for a while, so I’ll wait in Termwills. You be careful too, young man.”

“Yes. I’ll leave Caduceus here with you.”

Caduceus, who had taken the form of a cat, was being held by Valentina.

Now then. First, I need to go home. Lindwurm… has been playing with the Carbuncles in my house’s inner courtyard. While taking Lindwurm with us, I’ll tell Cecilia and the others to prepare for hospitality.

After contacting Father and the others via the communication device, we depart from Termwills. If we head along the road toward the Barony of Silun, we should be able to meet up. As long as we periodically exchange our general location and rest timing with Father via the communication device, we shouldn’t miss each other somewhere along the way.

Since I’m serving as escort this time, I’m not riding in the dragon palanquin but instead moving while mounted on Lindwurm. Elliot is also riding Saphir, flying alongside the dragon palanquin.

Balor, who has bird-like legs, is perched on my shoulder. I don’t know what he thinks about moving on Lindwurm, but he keeps blinking his eyes while looking around at the scenery.

As we move through the sky above the road, Elliot spoke.

“When Camilla was little… she was the kind of girl who would swing a sword around.”

His voice sounded nostalgic. Probably because she comes from a knight’s family.

“Could it be that you learned to handle a sword because of her influence too?”

“That’s right. I also trained together with Camilla. Even after being told I had talent for magic at my study abroad destination. As a lord, I sometimes wonder if I should have focused solely on water magic. Thinking about it that way, you could say Camilla protected my life.”

…Yeah. Because she trained with the sword since childhood, she was probably able to fight valiantly on the ship.

There is the part about her catching the attention of Zadias and Ragnar because of that, but all of that is because Elliot spent his childhood with Camilla.

As we advanced while talking with Elliot and letting the wyverns and Saphir rest… around the time the evening sun began coloring the surroundings, I saw a dragon palanquin approaching from afar.

Using Light Magic to magnify the view… it’s definitely Father’s dragon palanquin. The Gartner County family crest is painted on it.

“…That Technique is quite convenient.”

“I’m discussing with Alfred about turning it into a magic tool. It would probably be useful even if equipped on an airship.”

With this Technique, you can grasp the other party’s appearance from a greater distance.

As we approach the dragon palanquin, Father shows his face from the other side.

“Hello, Father.”

“Theodore. I’m glad we could meet up.”

“It’s been a long time.”

“Hmm. I’m just glad you look well.”

I exchange words with Father like this.

“Is Camilla-san with you too?”

“Hmm. And it appears Lord Elliot is accompanying you as well.”

Father said this after looking at Elliot mounted on Saphir. As Father who’s also acquainted with Ashley, he seemed to recognize Elliot at a glance.

“Pleased to meet you, Count Gartner.”

“Likewise, Lord Elliot.”

Elliot’s expression is somewhat stiff. He definitely seems nervous.

“…It’s unsettling being up in the sky. I’d like to lower the dragon palanquin and talk, if that’s alright?”

Showing some concern about the inside of the dragon palanquin, Father said.

Camilla and Kennel are probably behind him too… but they probably can’t push Father aside to show their faces from the window.

I scan the area, looking for a suitable place to land the dragon palanquin.

“Understood. We can probably land the dragon palanquin over there. Lindwurm.”

I say, having Lindwurm guide the wyverns pulling the dragon palanquin.

When Lindwurm calls out, the two dragon palanquins slowly descend to an open area beside the road.

Elliot and I land on the ground first, followed by the dragon palanquin carrying Grace and the others, then the dragon palanquin carrying Father and his group in that order.

Then the dragon palanquin’s door opens—and a woman emerges from inside.

She appears to be in her early twenties, or perhaps even younger. From Elliot’s stories, I’d imagined her to be an active person… but she’s slender with a somewhat unhealthy pale complexion.

“Camilla.”

Elliot calls her name. Called by her name, Camilla opens her eyes wide and stares intently at Elliot’s face.

“…Elliot… Truly—”

With an emotionally overwhelmed expression, tears welling in the corners of her eyes, Camilla runs to Elliot and clings to him as if throwing herself into his chest.

“I’m so glad…! Truly, so glad…! Welcome back…!”

“…I’m home. I’m sorry. I took so long to return.”

Elliot says while holding Camilla. After embracing for a while, they separate, though it’s unclear who moved first. As the evening sun dyes the surroundings red, the two face each other holding hands.

“You’ve… grown taller.”

Looking up at Elliot, Camilla shows an expression that looks like she might burst into tears any moment, yet still happy—a mixture of various emotions.

“…Yeah. When we last met, you were the taller one.”

“You have a scar on your face…”

Camilla frowns as she touches Elliot’s cheek.

“I feel bad toward you, Camilla, for having gotten such an injury.”

Though Camilla had teary eyes, she gave a wry smile and shook her head.

“You came back… alive. That’s what makes me happy. Does it… hurt?”

“No.”

For Elliot, who lived wearing a mask… this scar seems to be the sole proof that he and Benedict are the same person.

He said that the human relationships he built in Silvatoria might be useful for both Verdgar and Silvatoria in the future. So he’ll leave it as is. Elliot had said that. Still… he might have been anxious about showing it to Camilla.

“I got injured while fighting… It seems I hit my head at that time. After that, I’d lost my memory all this time.”

“I see… So that’s what happened.”

“I made you… suffer because of me.”

“Father also got injured six years ago and stayed home ever since… So I… couldn’t bear the thought of going to someone else, and I stopped going out much.”

“I’m sorry for making you wait.”

“No.”

It seems that her feelings for Elliot, combined with worry for her father, made Camilla put down her sword. That’s probably why she gives the impression of not being very active.

When I glance over, I see Kennel watching that scene while wiping tears with a handkerchief. Next to him, a man who appears to be Camilla’s father is also standing, squinting as if looking at something dazzling.

Ashley too… while tears moisten her eyes, she smiles gently, with Grace and the others staying close to her.

When our eyes meet, they smile at me. I quietly return the smile.

“I’m home, Kennel.”

Elliot calls out to Kennel, who had been watching the two from a slight distance.

“Welcome—back, Lord Elliot.”

Kennel bows deeply with tears in his eyes.

Once Camilla and Kennel have calmed down, Elliot speaks.

“Lord Theodore over there is the one who saved me. He restored my memories.”

At these words, the gazes of Camilla and her father, along with Kennel’s, gather on me.

“For bringing Elliot to us—I don’t know what to say. I can’t find the words… to express my gratitude.”

Camilla says. I quietly bow in return.

…Yeah. Since it was so sudden, I was worried about how things would turn out… but it seems there’s nothing to worry about regarding their relationship.

Bathed in the final glow of the setting sun, the two stood quietly side by side.

+++

# **295 – Father and Grandfather**

In the dragon palanquin were Father, Kennel, Camilla and her father, plus the minimum necessary servants. And there were others who had boarded as well – Daryl and Kathryn.

“Theodore-sama.”

When Daryl called out to me and our eyes met, the two of them bowed their heads to me quietly.

“Good day to you both.”

“It’s been a while.”

Regarding Kathryn going out – I had given my consent when Father asked for my opinion.

According to Father’s communication, since Mother’s blood relatives had come to Termwills, Kathryn said she wanted to go and bow her head to them. As for Daryl, he might be accompanying Kathryn…

There are parts about Mother’s background that I haven’t explained in detail and can’t explain… but Kathryn wanting to apologize might mean that her feelings have changed even more since then.

While we were exchanging greetings, the sun set and the surroundings rapidly grew dark.

Noticing the change around us, Camilla nodded to Elliot. I suppose that means it’s alright now.

“Then let’s go. I’ll escort you.”

Once everyone had boarded the dragon palanquin, I began escorting it alongside Elliot.

We would escort them to Termwills while using Night Vision Magic to survey our surroundings.

“Father, I’d like to discuss our plans after arriving in Termwills.”

Flying beside Father’s dragon palanquin, I spoke through the window.

“Hmm.”

“I’ve renovated the house and hired people. Dinner preparations are underway, and it’s possible for everyone to stay over. I think heading straight to the annex would be too rushed.”

“Renovation… Understood. I’ll inform the servants that we’ll be heading to the annex tomorrow or later.”

When Father visited Termwills last time, he saw my house briefly… well, its appearance might have changed quite a bit.

“We were… planning to find lodging in town,”

said Camilla.

“Right now, Lord Elliot is staying with us as well. The main building we use and the guest wing are separate… so if it’s not an inconvenience, please feel free to stay. Dinner preparations are also underway.”

When I said that, Camilla and her father smiled.

“Thank you very much. We’ll gladly accept your kind offer.”

“…Before dinner, might I be able to meet with Lord Siegmund? I’d like to meet with him alone first.”

Father inquired. Regardless of what Kathryn thought, Father probably felt the responsibility lay with himself.

“Understood. I’ll prepare a place to talk here.”

“My apologies, Theo.”

I contacted Cecilia and Mihaela via communication device and made arrangements so that we could talk immediately upon arriving home.

The journey to Termwills went smoothly. After greeting the watchtower, I guided them directly to my house.

“Renovation… It’s become almost unrecognizable…”

“I’d say we bought the neighboring house and incorporated it. The interior of that wing preserves the old house.”

Seeing my house from above, Father looked puzzled as he spoke, so I explained about the house while landing the dragon palanquin in the courtyard.

“Well then, Lindwurm. Until tomorrow.”

After everyone had disembarked, I said that, and Lindwurm let out a cry before withdrawing with the dragon palanquin back to the Royal Castle. Then Cecilia arrived.

“Welcome home, Master.”

“Is everything ready?”

“Yes. Everything is perfectly prepared.”

Cecilia nodded quietly.

“Then… Father. This way.”

I had Old Sigmund waiting in the reception room. Father nodded and followed behind me.

“Everyone else, this way please. There’s still some time before dinner, so please wait a little while.”

Cecilia guided Kennel, Kathryn and the others into the house. Well… I’ll leave that to her. Kathryn seemed quite tense and didn’t appear to be in any state to relax…

Entering the house from the courtyard, I guided Father to the reception room near the entrance hall.

“Grandfather, are you there?”

“Hmm…”

When I knocked on the door, Old Sigmund’s response came from inside. When we entered, Old Sigmund stood up and cleared his throat.

“Pleased to make your acquaintance. I am Henry Verdim Gartner.”

Seeing Old Sigmund, Father introduced himself with a deep bow.

“…I have come from Silvatoria. I am Siegmund Willcloud. Patricia… she went by Lisa here. I am Lisa’s father.”

Both voices… held tension.

“There is one other person who came, someone Patricia treated like a younger sister and cherished. Would it be alright if I explained the circumstances of this matter only to that person?”

“Of course.”

Saying that, Father slowly knelt on the floor and bowed his head to Old Sigmund.

“Truly – I am sorry. Today’s situation is entirely the result of my own inadequacies. I cannot face either Patricia or you.”

Receiving those words, Old Sigmund remained silent for a while, but eventually closed his eyes, let out a breath, and spoke gravely.

“Please raise your head, Count. A father should not show such a appearance before his son.”

“…But…”

“I say it is fine.”

Old Sigmund’s words. After a silence, Father spoke.

“…I… couldn’t I have done something more before things turned out that way, for Lisa… for Patricia… couldn’t I have done more for her… That day, I cannot forgive myself more than anything else for not even being able to raise my sword against the demon. Why… couldn’t I have been there…”

Hearing Father’s words, I too closed my eyes. Father’s monologue and remorse. These were words he hadn’t even revealed to me.

But I knew. I understood that Father was regretful.

Silence fell. Just as Old Sigmund was about to speak, a knock sounded.

“Please, I beg you… let me speak too. Regarding that person, I too bear responsibility.”

It was Kathryn’s voice.

“Kathryn bears no responsibility… All responsibility lies with me.”

Father said that, but Old Sigmund quietly replied.

“I understand your desire to protect your wife. I don’t consider it either of your responsibilities, but let’s hear what she has to say.”

Kathryn entered the room and, like Father, bowed her head to Old Sigmund. And so they spoke about House Gartner and House Broderick.

“In the end, it was… myself and my father who broke the promise.”

…It was about an arranged marriage from the time of the previous Marquis Broderick.

Mother met Father during her adventurer days… then the arranged marriage agreement between the previous Count and the previous Marquis was exchanged. And so Father ended up marrying Kathryn.

The promise. It was probably about welcoming Mother into the Count’s residence later.

“I… from the beginning, found that person dazzling and frightening. I was afraid to acknowledge that she possessed everything I lacked…”

Dazzling and frightening… This might be the first time I’ve heard from Kathryn’s own mouth how she felt about Mother.

That Mother was dazzling. So she clung to her status. Clinging to her status, she worked to prevent someone who wasn’t nobility from entering the residence. That… must be what breaking the promise meant.

After that, the previous Marquis Broderick tried to manipulate Kathryn.

Wanting to escape the guilt of betraying Father and her self-reproach toward Mother… I suppose it was because of that weakness that she became distorted.

“So… regarding that person, I bear responsibility… I… not only that, but I even treated Theodore terribly…”

“But… you now regret that, do you not? …Regretting that if only you had done things differently, being unable to forgive yourself – I am the same.”

In response to Kathryn’s words, Old Sigmund shook his head, then looked up to the heavens and laughed self-deprecatingly.

“Had we welcomed Patricia into the residence as wife rather than concubine… or perhaps she would have been in Termwills. If so, she might not have known about the demon’s attack, or if not… she would have fought the King of Deathly Slumber with you all in tow… but that’s not how it turned out.”

Even if Father had been there, it probably wouldn’t have changed anything. Even if Kathryn had kept the promise, there’s no way to know if that day’s battle wouldn’t have occurred.

“If I said I bear no resentment, that would be a lie. However… after speaking with Theodore, I thought that blaming someone for Patricia, who fought demons and protected her loved ones, would be disregarding that girl’s heart.”

After saying that, Old Sigmund narrowed his eyes.

“Therefore, I do not blame you two. Both of you, please raise your heads and stand.”

At Old Sigmund’s words, Father and Kathryn hesitantly stood up.

“I shall ask no more. I have indeed heard your words. Those words alone are sufficient for me.”

Perhaps because he too carries regrets? Looking into Old Sigmund’s eyes, Father and Kathryn nodded.

Father and the others left… then headed to where Valentina was waiting in a nearby room.

To explain the circumstances of this matter from Old Sigmund’s and my own mouths. When I conveyed their words, Valentina quietly spoke.

“…I understand. If Lord Siegmund and Theodore-kun don’t blame them, then neither will I say this or that. If we’re speaking of regrets, I have them too.”

…That’s right. I’m the same too, but… Maybe I should change the direction of the conversation a bit.

“I know one of Mother’s friends from her adventurer days… apparently that person complained to Father about Mother once.”

“Is that so?”

“Yes. That person also said it was meaningless since she could tell he was already regretful.”

“…I see. It’s almost as if she said it on my behalf.”

Valentina gave a small, wry smile.

I tried contacting Rosetta herself via communication device. When I told her about Valentina, she replied asking if she could come now. Of course that’s fine. I heard dinner was being prepared with some extra time.

“That person too… will probably appear during tonight’s dinner.”

“Will she tell us stories about Patricia too?”

“That’s right. Shall we share memories and such later?”

“To learn what each other doesn’t know, is that it?”

“–Yes.”

Mother didn’t dislike lively gatherings either, and having stories blossom about the past… would surely make her happy.

# **296 – The Memories of the Sages**

“It’s been a while, Henry-sama.”

“Mihaela. I’m glad to see you’re doing well.”

“Thanks to you. Theodore-sama also reached out to me… I’m currently staying with Theodore-sama while supervising Cecilia.”

As we moved to the dining hall, Father and Mihaela exchanged greetings.

“Hmm. Come to think of it, Mihaela and I have known each other for quite some time now.”

“That’s right. I’ve been in service since the time of the previous Count. Although Theodore-sama is supposed to be keeping his distance publicly… yes. I was relieved to hear about the circumstances.”

Father gave a wry smile at Mihaela’s words.

“Lady Rosetta has arrived.”

Just then, Cecilia appeared. After being told to show her to the dining hall, Rosetta appeared shortly after.

“Good evening. I’m glad to see you’ve returned safely.”

“Yes, good evening, Rosetta-san.”

“Good evening, Teacher.”

Ashley and the others exchanged greetings in this manner.

“Henry. It’s been a while.”

“Ah, Rosetta. You look well too, that’s what matters most.”

“I never neglect my training. You, however… might have gotten a bit rusty, haven’t you?”

“I’ve been busy. I can’t keep up like when I used to hunt monsters with Lisa and you.”

Monster hunting, huh. Since monsters do come from the forest to the Count’s territory as well. Father has also mastered martial arts as a noble’s accomplishment. He said he was good at jousting and mounted archery, so he might not be very compatible with labyrinths. Even if he ultimately stays in the rear, Father said that when the lord stands at the front lines at least once to inspire them, the soldiers’ morale greatly increases.

“Theodore-kun, who is she?”

Valentina noticed Rosetta and called out to her.

“Yes. This is Rosetta Attenborough-san, a lecturer at Peresford Academy. Rosetta-san, this is Siegmund Willcloud, a magician from Silvatoria who is my grandfather, and Valentina-san who was close with my mother.”

“Nice to meet you. I’m Rosetta Attenborough.”

“I’m Siegmund Willcloud.”

“I’m Valentina Dornath.”

I introduced the people meeting for the first time in this way.

As dinner preparations progressed, a wonderful aroma filled the dining hall. Today’s dishes featured plenty of seafood. Apparently, due to the effects of the Sealed Door of the Magic Light Water Vein being opened, there has been continuous abundant fishing. Steamed clams in sake, bright red shrimp… quite appetizing dishes were being laid out.

“…Is something wrong?”

When I glanced at Daryl, he looked somewhat troubled. When I asked, he gave me a subtle expression.

“Well, it’s just that… Theodore-sama’s grandfather seems to have quite a dignified air about him…”

I see… Not so much troubled as nervous, I suppose. He seemed to have sensed something from Old Sigmund’s attire and demeanor.

I heard that during the previous Count’s lifetime, Daryl and Byron were both disciplined by a strict grandfather. He probably has an aversion to people who carry an air of authority as elders. Moreover, given our history too.

“…While he is indeed from Silvatoria nobility… he may look dignified, but he’s quite approachable. Regarding your matter with me, it’s already been resolved and he has no intention of bringing it up again.”

“Ah, ah.”

When I said this in a low voice, Daryl gave a small nod. Daryl was hardly involved in the matter concerning my mother. And our issue… was really nothing more than a childish quarrel.

While Daryl and I were having that conversation, dinner preparations had been completed before I knew it. Well then, let’s eat.

“—Lady Lisa said… ‘I’m going to hunt monsters here, so everyone please cooperate.’ While she had the villagers use bows and spears to keep the Goblins at bay after transforming the village into a fortress-like structure with fences made using Wood Magic, she took on the Ogre and the Goblin chieftain.”

During dinner, Grace was sharing fond memories.

…How nostalgic. That remains vaguely in my memory too. If I recall correctly… it was when we traveled south. The Goblin chieftain who could use magic had used Charm magic on the Ogre to bring it to their side, and they attacked.

The Charm magic used by chieftains is relatively effective against creatures like Ogres that live prioritizing instinct above all. Therefore, groups of Goblins led by exceptional chieftains sometimes have unexpected monsters as bodyguards, which dramatically increases their danger level.

Usually, it’s about Orc-level, but that group that had brought in an Ogre would have caused considerable damage if left alone. Well, even though it’s called Charm magic, it’s not particularly advanced. Against humans and such, it seems reason overcomes the charm’s effect, making it less effective.

“If I remember correctly—the Goblin chieftain tried to cast magic, but Grace threw a brick from a rooftop and took him down.”

“That was reckless of you.”

“Lady Lisa was drawing their attention… so I thought even if I failed, I could just run away immediately.”

At Rosetta’s words, Grace smiled, placing a hand on her chest.

“And then… how did you defeat the Ogre?”

“Since the chieftain was defeated, there were no more long-range attacks. I used Levitation to bring it high up into the sky.”

Once you use Levitation, no matter how Tough the Ogre is, it can’t resist. Without the chieftain’s support attacks, you could leisurely fly through the air using Levitation without even needing the secret technique of wings.

“You dropped it, then.”

“Lisa used to do that sometimes against large enemies that couldn’t fly. She said it saved magical power.”

Rosetta gave a wry smile.

“Hmm. I did teach her to effectively use small magics, but…”

“At that time, she dropped the Ogre onto the Goblins… and then made rocks fall from above too.”

Ogres have regeneration abilities too, so she probably wanted to be extra thorough.

“Since Lisa went to the Count’s territory, opportunities to meet decreased… but it seems she hasn’t changed.”

“…What do you mean, even in the labyrinth?”

“Yes. Since she seemed to have reserves left, as someone accompanying her, it was reassuring that she could act calmly.”

Old Sigmund and Valentina seemed interested in Grace and Rosetta’s stories, nodding along.

“Lisa—Patricia was indeed skilled with magic. Though it was a flaw that strange tastes sometimes emerged when she made tools.”

“Ah. That’s true. I had her make weapons for me too, so I understand.”

“But she holds back with small children, you know. I wonder if it’s because I got scared?”

Rosetta and Valentina nodded as if convinced… but she probably held back with me and Grace too, I think.

“What kind of things did she make?”

Seraphina asked. Marlene also seemed interested, looking this way.

“…Hmm. Like this.”

I used Earth Magic to create a skeleton. Though it’s not particularly imposing and has a somewhat stylized form, the general direction should be clear.

“I don’t dislike it.”

When Sheila said this while looking at it, Marlene also nodded repeatedly. Claudia and Irmhild, however, wore wry smiles.

After dinner, everyone moved to the game room, playing games and talking… we spent a relaxing time.

Daryl seemed to have taken a liking to darts, though his skill still has room for improvement. He was trying different things, adjusting his form.

“Theodore-dono.”

While I was playing billiards with Grace and Rosemary at a good stopping point, Donato, Camilla’s father, came to speak with me.

“What is it?”

“I’d like to ask about your plans from tomorrow onward, if that’s alright?”

Ah. Regarding Elliot and Camilla… even if their own feelings aren’t an issue, he’s probably concerned about the surrounding circumstances. Donato seems to have grown tired of the power struggles in the capital and settled in the Barony of Silun… it would be better to discuss things thoroughly beforehand. Let’s proceed with the discussion involving Ashley and Elliot, Kennel… and Camilla and Donato too.

“Very well. First, regarding the Barony of Silun…”

“As long as Ashley is the lord, I have no intention of changing that situation. From what I’ve heard, she’s quite popular among adventurers, and I hear things are running smoothly with Ashley as lord.”

When Elliot looked toward Kennel, Kennel nodded and replied.

“That’s right. Indeed… there are adventurers who were helped by Ashley-sama, and some even come all the way from Termwills. The territory is quite stable.”

“Though I might seem unreliable now… I want to become a lord that Father and Mother, and Elliot-niisama can be proud of.”

Ashley said, looking directly at Donato. Donato narrowed his eyes as he looked at Ashley.

“…I might disappoint you by not becoming lord, but…”

“No.”

Donato shook his head.

“I can’t imagine entrusting Camilla to anyone but you. Whether you’re the lord or not is irrelevant. Please, take good care of my daughter.”

“Father…”

“I promise. I will definitely make her happy.”

In response to Donato’s words, Elliot nodded, looking straight into his eyes.

Hmm. The remaining issue is Elliot’s uncertain position… but presenting some positive aspects here should help reassure them.

“His Majesty Melvin said he wouldn’t treat Sir Elliot’s future position poorly. He also said he would take his relationship with Ashley into consideration.”

I briefly glanced at Rosemary, and she nodded as if understanding, then made a thoughtful gesture while hiding her mouth with her feather fan. She was analyzing King Melvin’s intentions.

“Both his sword and magic skills are more than sufficient. His lineage isn’t a problem either. Probably… he’ll either be granted a knighthood and assigned to a knight order, or placed in a position where he can utilize the connections he built in Silvatoria. I think he’ll be kept in the capital for now—but later, there’s a high possibility he’ll be assigned to the north.”

“I see…”

Donato nodded, looking impressed. Camilla also had a serious expression since this conversation concerned her own future too.

“We’re scheduled to have a meeting with His Majesty about this matter on the next full moon. If both of you could attend as well, it might be more likely to turn out according to your wishes. Please stay until then.”

There’s still some time until the full moon, and there’s also the matter of procuring materials for the airship. In the meantime, we’ll proceed with conquering the labyrinth.

# **297 – Rest and Departure**

Since Father and the others had departed from the Count’s territory early in the morning and traveled here, they decided to take a bath and rest early. They probably also felt mentally fatigued from having to speak with Old Sigmund. Camilla was the same. Having learned from Kennel that Elliot was in Termwills, she seemed unable to relax.

So it appeared the guests decided to relax a bit in the game room after dinner, then take a bath and rest slowly.

“It’s been a while since we’ve had time to relax like this, so I’m happy for moments like these,” Grace said with a smile as she offered me a lap pillow. Her slender fingers gently combed through my hair. I closed my eyes at the ticklish yet comfortable sensation.

“Between maintaining magic tools and preparing for travel… there were so many things to do that it was hard to settle down during the journey.”

Though I had been practicing Circulating Ki… taking proper time to relax was another matter entirely.

“It seems things are settling down with Elliot-sama and Camilla-sama too… I can finally feel at ease.”

Ashley pressed her cheek against mine from beside me. I intertwined my hand with hers, palm to palm, and began Circulating Ki with both of them.

Inside… a warm sensation spread from the center of my body to the tips of my limbs, creating a comfortable feeling.

I slightly opened my eyes and touched a strand of Grace’s lustrous golden hair. I combed through it with my fingers as she had been doing. The smooth texture transmitted to my hand and the scent tickling my nostrils was pleasant.

While still holding Ashley’s hand, I brought it up to her cheek… then released it once to touch her cheek. Her pale hand came to rest on the back of mine. I could feel the fine texture of her skin clinging to my fingertips.

“Hehe… that tickles.”

“…Theodore-sama’s hand is warm.”

Both of them appeared much more relaxed than during our travels.

I supposed part of it was because their worries about Mother and Elliot had been resolved.

After practicing Circulating Ki with them for a while, I headed to the bath. Today’s rotation had Grace and Ashley in the living room, Rosemary in the bath, and Marlene and Claudia in the bedroom.

As for Rosemary, she was standing in front of the changing room with her arms crossed, opening and closing her feather fan.

“…Um. Could you go in first?”

“Understood.”

…It wasn’t like I intended to watch her change. I changed into my bath robe in the changing room and entered the bath.

While checking the water temperature and pouring water over myself with a bucket, I heard the rustle of clothing from the changing room as Rosemary entered with her hair tied up. As usual, she was wearing the Shrine Maiden’s training uniform from the Temple… but it had slits to allow easier movement when wet, revealing glimpses of her white thighs.

Combined with her good figure, it made it rather difficult to know where to look…

“You’re going to wash my back, right? I’d be happy if you could turn around,” Rosemary said, averting her face when I looked at her. She seemed somewhat unsure where to put her hands… covering her chest area and the slits, perhaps feeling unsettled without her feather fan.

“Is this good?”

“Yes.”

Understanding her discomfort, I obediently turned my back as requested, and her voice seemed to regain some composure. The sound of water filled the room as she filled buckets and wrung out towels, then began washing my back with a washcloth. After rinsing the soap from my back, she washed my hair as well.

Though she seemed somewhat unpracticed, she was thorough. Being involved in medicine preparation probably made her dexterous too.

“I’ll wash Marie’s back and hair too.”

“Oh? Well then, I’ll take you up on that.”

Since her hair was up, her slender nape was exposed, but showing her back didn’t seem to embarrass Rosemary too much.

The back of her garment was largely open. I washed it with a washcloth and poured water over it.

Next, her hair. I untied it, brushed it, then rinsed it with lukewarm water.
