Taking some Savona Tree shampoo, I lathered it up and began washing Rosemary’s hair. I wanted to be as careful as possible since damaging her hair would defeat the purpose. I washed her hair, then gently massaged her scalp as I cleaned it.

“You’re quite skilled. I’d say you’re not inferior to the Royal Castle’s maids…” Rosemary murmured in an impressed tone.

“If you say so. I’m not very confident though.”

“Yes. Not bad at all.”

I was somewhat imitating how hair is washed at barbers or salons. Using the pads of my fingers to massage rather than my nails. Well, since it’s self-taught, if it works well then that’s good enough.

After rinsing her hair, we each washed our bodies and entered the bath. Rosemary was crossing her arms to hide her chest where the fabric clung, but this only ended up emphasizing her cleavage instead. Well… I decided not to mention it.

Since maintaining distance would make Circulating Ki impossible, she leaned against me closely.

Taking deep breaths to avoid getting lightheaded, I calmed my mind and began Circulating Ki. Performing Circulating Ki in the bath had particularly high effectiveness – it felt like fatigue was literally dissolving into the hot water.

“Though it might be strange for me to say this… I’m glad you were able to reconcile,” Rosemary said quietly.

“Mmm… Yeah. But Marie, you’ve reconciled with Albert and Marlene too.”

So that was probably why those words came out.

“That’s true,” Rosemary said with a wry smile.

After warming ourselves to the core through Circulating Ki, we got out of the bath.

Since she told me to go ahead, I changed in the dressing room, called out to the bathroom, and left.

When I headed to the bedroom, Marlene and Claudia were waiting while playing cards with Sheila and the others. Though we wouldn’t actually get into bed until everyone was together, after Grace and Ashley finished their bath.

Seeing them changed into nightwear and enjoying cards was heartwarming as always, creating a sleepover-like atmosphere.

“Is the room temperature alright like this? I can adjust it if it’s too hot,” Claudia asked.

“Yeah. I think it’s fine. I’m going to do some deciphering of notes too, and it wouldn’t be good for my body to get too cold during that.”

“Okay. Understood.”

Since summer heat still lingered and we had just bathed, the room temperature was lowered just enough to prevent chills. It was quite comfortable for after bathing.

Rosemary returned to the main bedroom. Then Grace and Ashley. We each spent time as we pleased until bedtime… then when the time felt right, we all got into bed together.

Today, Marlene and Claudia were on either side of me. Next to Marlene were Ashley, Grace, and Rosemary in that order.

As for Marlene who ended up beside me… she happily clung to my chest area. Accepting this, I stroked her hair and she looked up with a beaming smile.

Seeing this, Claudia narrowed her eyes and showed a gentle expression. She lay down beside me, quietly drawing close. She pressed her cheek against me as if listening to my heartbeat, closing her eyes.

While practicing Circulating Ki, we turned off the lights.

“Not long ago… I never thought we’d have times this peaceful. Sometimes I find it strange when I think about it,” Claudia murmured to no one in particular.

…Yeah. From Claudia’s perspective, leaving the Labyrinth to go out or sleeping together with someone… probably weren’t things she could have imagined.

“…Let’s do our best at the Blazing Fortress starting tomorrow.”

“…Yes,” Claudia answered from within my embrace.

Grace and the others seemed to quietly agree as well. The quiet, peaceful time before sleep. The comfort of Circulating Ki. The delicate, soft feel of Marlene and Claudia. The scent of soap after bathing. Wrapped in these sensations, I fell asleep.

――The next day. Thanks to getting sufficient sleep, I woke up feeling refreshed. With Father and Ashley’s matters… and having found paths toward resolving various issues, my worries had diminished too.

At any rate, I think we were able to rest thoroughly and replenish our energy before heading to the Blazing Fortress. My Magical Power was in good condition too.

Checking everyone’s plans during breakfast, it turned out Father and the others would stay at the villa for several days. They planned to visit the theater and hot spring town before returning.

Since Elliot was with Camilla, Donato, and Kennel, he would spend today relaxing with them.

We decided to have Ambrum, disguised as a servant, accompany us so he could detect any problems that might occur while we were in the Labyrinth.

Since Ambrum wasn’t suited for direct combat, bringing him into the Labyrinth would be difficult, so having him serve as a liaison would work perfectly.

Old Sigmund and Valentina said they were going to the workshop. We agreed to meet at the workshop after returning from the Labyrinth.

“Well then――shall we go?”

“Yes,” everyone nodded when I called out.

After finishing breakfast, we equipped ourselves with Blazing Fortress countermeasures and left the house.

Let’s review the precautions for the Blazing Fortress on our way to the Moon Temple.

Since we had been away in Silvatoria, the Labyrinth felt unfamiliar again. Though we had countermeasure Equipment and Tephra’s Blessing among other things, it remained a challenging area regardless. Let’s psych ourselves up to avoid getting injured.

+++

# **298 – The Black Dog and the Summoner**

We teleported from the labyrinth entrance’s stone monument to the Blazing Fortress.

The normally suffocating heat felt bearable thanks to Tephra’s Blessing. What a relief. With this, we should be able to proceed with the conquest at a steady pace.

Continuing from last time, we would be advancing from the hall beyond the castle gate after defeating the gatekeeper.

Descending the stairs leading from the hall brought us to a maze. Eventually, it would lead to the castle’s inner courtyard, from where we could finally breach the main keep.

In short, to reach the fortress interior, we needed to traverse the underground maze. The maze’s route was unpredictable due to its structural changes. Today, I hoped to make it through this maze.

“Alright, let’s go. If you sense anything unusual, deploy your Shields immediately.”

“Mm. Understood.”

Sheila, being the Scout, nodded of course, and everyone else followed suit.

Descending the spiral staircase and opening the door revealed a corridor constructed of stone.

It’s fairly spacious. Immediately after descending the stairs, I could see a narrow passage continuing on the left side.

Just as we were about to begin our exploration—Lavigne groaned while staring deep into the passage. From the darkness, countless red glows were approaching us.

“Those are… Hellhounds.”

The glows were the eyes of living creatures. Spewing fire from their mouths as they came toward us… they were four-legged beasts. Their appearance resembled black dogs. Their faces were contorted, baring fangs—a visage of utmost ferocity.

“I’m going.”

Grace, Sheila, Ignis, and I dashed out to intercept.

I took the lead and charged in. As I passed a certain point in the passage, a stone block embedded in the right side of the corridor began to glow faintly red, catching the corner of my eye.

“Passage right! Bomb Rock!”

Simultaneously, Irmhild’s voice rang out.

Irmhild’s voice came from the direction of the Bomb Rock. Seraphina had transferred the sound to where Irmhild was pointing. The next moment, an axe was thrown from Grace’s hand.

The axe, roaring through the air, struck the Bomb Rock directly. The sound of shattering stone and the clinking of the retracting chain echoed.

Even when attacked, the Bomb Rock didn’t explode. Partly because Grace shattered it in one blow, but also because these monsters only burst when they reach their limit, scattering explosive force and fragments.

The troublesome part is how they camouflage themselves as building materials or natural objects, making them indistinguishable until they activate. Still, it ended in a dud. If we can discover and handle them before they explode, that’s the ideal way to deal with them.

Ignoring the shattered Bomb Rock, we confronted the Hellhounds coming from the front. As I leaped forward to charge, a Hellhound also pounced. I assumed a stance as if swinging Ouroboros, which glowed with Spark Light, and the Hellhound made a gesture as if trying to bite and stop Ouroboros. Another one behind it. It seemed one would hold down the weapon while the other attacked.

But that’s naive. Using Shield and Levitation, I performed an emergency stop, halting mid-air. Immediately, I rebounded downward, and from directly beneath the Hellhound that snapped its fangs in vain, I thrust Ouroboros upward into its belly.

“Icicle Lance!”

An ice spear shot out from the tip of the Dragon Staff, pinning the Hellhound in mid-air. The next one, missing its timing to breathe fire, was slashed aside by Nemea’s claws as they passed each other.

Grace, Sheila, and Ignis also plunged into the pack.

Protected by Fire Rat fur and Tephra’s Blessing, Grace charged through the flames unfazed. Radiating Fighting Spirit from her axe, a purple lightning-like afterimage passed, leaving only Hellhounds split cleanly in two.

From wall to ceiling, ceiling to pillar. Sheila moved three-dimensionally, changing trajectory mid-air. Her movements, grazing past their noses, left only the futile sound of snapping fangs. Flames scorched empty space.

Unexpected Sticky Thread and Lightning Strikes from unforeseen directions. The Hellhounds, having missed their attacks or had their movements hindered, were left full of openings. Ignis charged in, and with a roar from its War Hammer, sent them flying.

Even so, the Hellhounds’ movements remained coordinated. Ignoring their comrades being taken down by us Vanguards, a group of Hellhounds dashed toward the Rearguard. Clearly, movements controlled by someone.

While it might seem like there was a large gap between the Vanguard and Rearguard, full of openings—there was a reason the Midguard itself was absent.

The moment the leading Hellhound stepped into that space, its body was torn apart, spraying blood as it screamed in agony. A line of light ran from pillar to pillar in the corridor. It was a Trap using Magic Threads, set by deploying Magic Slaves.

“Too bad.”

Rosemary, watching from a distance, smiled faintly behind her feather fan.

Seeing their comrade caught in the trap, the Hellhounds immediately halted. The dogs’ reactions weren’t bad… but being in that space itself was like stepping into a trap.

“Now!”

With Ashley’s voice, Marlene’s Saucer, hovering above the corridor, cut off their retreat. As they were cornered, Ashley and Lavigne’s ice bullets, Irmhild’s Light Arrows, and Seraphina’s Sound Bullets rained down upon them. With sufficient distance, stray shots wouldn’t hit the Vanguard.

Dullahan, Caduceus, and Lavigne remained on standby as escorts for the Rearguard. Claudia, as usual, prepared for retreat using Teleportation Magic.

Eclair also joined the shooting. Flapping her wings, electrified feathers flew out. Even if the feathers themselves were dodged, something like a side lightning strike occurred—Lightning Strikes burst from the feathers, shocking the targets, which were then shot through by Irmhild’s arrows. It was a rather troublesome attack where merely avoiding the feathers was meaningless, and one had to counter the Lightning Strikes themselves.

The dogs that charged the Rearguard were annihilated in an instant—but from the darkness deep in the passage, a second wave of Hellhounds came surging forth. Quite a number. Combined with the initial pack of Hellhounds, this was an abnormal quantity.

Normally, this would be the situation to retreat to the narrow passage on the left of the corridor and fight while avoiding encirclement… but I didn’t like it. If that was the enemy’s plan, we should assume traps were set in that passage. Even if we advanced toward the passage side, we still had to deal with the Hellhound pack coming from behind.

“Go!”

While dealing with Hellhounds pouncing from left and right, I enveloped Balor, perched on my shoulder, with a sufficient amount of Magical Power and sent it charging deep into the passage.

While controlling Balor, I smashed a Hellhound’s skull with Ouroboros and impaled another with ice. Martial arts and magic execution. Nemea and Capella. Simultaneous control of Balor—.

While we were scattering the Hellhounds, Balor flew on. As long as it was enveloped in my Magical Power, a visual link with Balor was possible. Soaring over the dogs’ heads, passing the corner—I saw a group sitting in seiza, deploying a Magic Array.

Ash-gray skin. Egg-smooth heads. White eyes without pupils, faces without noses. Humanoid monsters clad in tattered cloth were fervently continuing their incantations.

Demon Summoners. Magician-type monsters possessing summoning abilities. So, they were the ones endlessly summoning the Hellhound packs.

Distance, position confirmed. From one end of the passage to the other. Balor, transformed into a Light Bullet, closed in on the Demon Summoners. Relying on momentum, I made it shoot through the Summoners’ chests. Continuously, two, three, four bodies. After piercing all the coordinates where the Summoners should have been, Balor opened its eyes to find the Summoners, chests pierced, lying scattered.

Simultaneously, the Hellhound pack shuddered and stopped moving. Probably sensing an abnormality after the Summoners’ control was suddenly cut off.

Massive openings. No reason to let that slide. It didn’t take much time for the Hellhound pack to be annihilated.

“How is it?”

I asked Sheila while she proceeded with looting.

Carefully examining the narrow passage on the left side, Sheila shook her head.

“Full of traps. For example, that floor stone there. Step on it, and spears or arrows… or a mechanism that releases poisonous smoke from that hole in the wall.”

Where Sheila pointed, there was a slightly protruding floor stone and a hole in the wall.

…Quite nasty. I had no intention of verifying the traps’ nature. Since there was another passage in the direction where the Demon Summoners were, it seemed better to proceed that way.

“No point deliberately taking a passage meant to drive us into traps. Even if we got through, there’s a high chance of an ambush. Let’s head in the direction of the Demon Summoners.”

“Understood.”

Sheila nodded, stopped peering into the passage, and joined the looting operation. The Blazing Fortress… even when looting, we couldn’t let our guard down. Because Bomb Rocks might be lurking.

“I wish we knew a way to identify Bomb Rocks before they activate,” said Irmhild.

I understood the sentiment, but I shook my head. Being stone monsters, they had no scent and made no sound. Irmhild could detect them relatively quickly through temperature changes… but that might only be possible thanks to Tephra’s Blessing. I had thought Irmhild’s detection ability would be halved in the Blazing Fortress due to the high temperature, but this was a pleasant miscalculation.

Well, since they emit light just before exploding, if we knew they were there even amidst chaotic battles, deploying a Shield would be possible.

“For now, we can only try not to miss the signs before explosion. For looting too, divide roles between watchers and workers, and be careful not to overlook changes in the walls, floor, and ceiling. Pay special attention to behind monster corpses, among other places.”

“Understood.”

Irmhild nodded with a serious expression, approached the looting team, and began scanning vigilantly without letting her guard down.

Now, about the looting. From Hellhounds, we could obtain pelts. From Bomb Rocks, we could sometimes recover Magic Stones of medium quality or, rarely, Gems.

From Demon Summoners, besides Magic Stones, we could seize their used Magic Staffs and such as spoils of war.

Hellhound pelts had high Resistance to fire and were strong against Slash Attacks, so they should fetch a good price. The Demon Summoners’ staffs, while unnecessary for me, seemed to be quite decent items. Considering building an Airship, I wanted to collect as many Magic Stones as possible.

For the combat time invested, it was a quite profitable battle.

+++

# **299 – The Shadow of the Distant Knight**

The Boundary Labyrinth was originally something that spread out underground. The place we’re currently in is a maze within the labyrinth, and since it’s further underground than the fortress, I’m not quite sure what to call it… but since it was called the Fortress Underground Maze in BFO, I’ll go with that.

Anyway, as the name “maze” rather than “labyrinth” suggests, I remember it not being that large-scale. After all, it’s just one floor within the Blazing Fortress.

However, its nature seems to be among the more troublesome types. When you touch the walls or ceiling, you can feel they’re heated up as if baked by midsummer sunlight.

It’s not so hot that you can’t touch them… but without countermeasures, it would be like being in a steam bath.

“Thanks to Tephra, it’s not too hot,” said Seraphina, smiling from her perch on Irmhild’s shoulder.

“That’s right. It helps that we can extend our exploration time too.”

…Thanks to the blessing, it seems we can manage without using cooling magic tools for now. It saves magical power, and we won’t have our vitality or concentration drained by the heat. As a result, we can extend our exploration time.

The party formation has me and Sheila, who’s serving as scout, taking the lead. Slightly behind them, Irmhild and Seraphina follow to detect Bomb Rocks.

Further back in order are Grace, Ashley, Marlene, Claudia, and Rosemary.

Lavigne follows behind Rosemary. Lavigne’s role is to detect scents, footsteps, and other presences from the rear. Ignis serves as the rearguard, with Eclair perched on its shoulder constantly monitoring the back as we advance.

We’ve hidden Caduceus near the center of the formation. Position-wise, that would be between Marlene and Claudia.

As we proceed down the passageway… it seems we’re coming to a wider corridor. Across the passageway is a small room… I can see a treasure chest in the back of the small room—but.

There don’t appear to be any enemies within our line of sight, but first I’ll send two Aqua Golems ahead to eliminate any ambush opportunities from corners. No surprise attacks from left or right.

I step into the passageway along with Sheila. A faint metallic sound. Sheila and I reacted almost simultaneously.

“—Above!”

Sheila leaped forward while shifting form, protecting her back with her shield as she turned and fired a Sticky Thread in the direction she faced. I deployed a shield overhead and prepared to receive the attack right where I stood.

Two Living Armors wielding spears jumped down from above. I could see there was space in the area right above the passageway exit where they could conceal themselves for ambushes.

I caught the spear tip with my shield at a diagonal angle, letting it slide down right in front of me. The other one got entangled in Sheila’s Sticky Thread and was pulled away with brute force.

“Move aside.”

I swept away the Living Armor that had stabbed its spear into the floor with Ouroboros from behind. The moment the strike landed, Spark Light burst out, crushing its back and sending it flying. The Living Armor, with both arms raised, crashed into a pillar with a loud clatter.

…Oh? It seems there was a Bomb Rock camouflaged as part of the pillar it hit. Apparently it reacted to the Living Armor’s impact, glowing and exploding without checking its target. The Living Armor’s parts scattered in all directions.

Thanks to the distance, only the Living Armor’s helmet came rolling over to us. Saved us some trouble.

The Living Armor Sheila was dealing with had also been finished off by the time I turned around. It seemed she had pulled it close with Sticky Thread and sliced it in two from the waist with her Pearl Sword imbued with Fighting Spirit.

The fact that she deployed a shield to her back when counterattacking the Living Armor, preparing for any unexpected Bomb Rock explosions, shows that our countermeasures are paying off well.

“Are you injured?” Grace asked.

“No problem here. Sheila?”

“I’m fine too. But Living Armors don’t have any scent and don’t make sounds until they move, so they’re troublesome.”

“…Yeah. They seem calculated enough to be ignored by Golems. Their ambush position was also placed where it couldn’t be seen from the passageway we entered from.”

I looked again at the space above the passageway exit. It felt like a waiting area carved square into the wall. Only groups like Living Armors could patiently wait in ambush in such narrow spaces…

Luring attention to the treasure chest room visible ahead while ambushing from above. Quite elaborate.

Now then… what about that treasure chest? First, I’ll send the Aqua Golems ahead. Have them step into the room and check for any spaces to the sides or above.

“Hmm. Checking for traps.”

Once safety was confirmed, Sheila carefully looked around the small room… and immediately pulled her head back in.

“…The ceiling is dangerous.”

She said this while pointing upward. I also looked up into the room… I see. There’s a slight gap between the ceiling and walls.

A ceiling drop trap, huh? A mechanism where the ceiling falls and crushes anyone inside the room when triggered. Probably a trap linked to the iron treasure chest conspicuously placed at the very back of the room.

After seeing this trap… those Living Armors from earlier might have had the role of launching surprise attacks from behind if intruders headed straight for the small room, preventing escape from the trap room.

Since we didn’t head straight for the trap room, they switched to an ambush from above. Couldn’t be more troublesome.

Anyway, when the trap activates, it crushes the entire room along with the treasure chest at the back. Is the chest itself the trap?

“Shall we try collecting it?”

There’s some distance, but… I cut off my magical power circulation once and emitted Earth Magic Magnetic Wave from outside the room, pulling the treasure chest toward me with force. The moment it was pulled from its position, I heard something activate. With a roar, a massive stone block—barely deserving the name “ceiling”—crushed the entire small room. Just before that, I had pulled the treasure chest out of the room with magnetism.

It seems the trap was activated by the weight of the treasure chest and its contents. Probably a mechanism where it won’t activate if something else is placed inside the box?

“Theodore-kun, as expected.”

Irmhild smiled happily and clasped her hands together.

I immediately moved to investigate the treasure chest.

“Not the keyhole part… but the contents? I sense magical power.”

“If that’s the case, it’s probably not a magic trap… I think.”

“If it turns out to be a magic trap, I’ll transfer it to another area. Somewhere like the Great Corruption Lake shouldn’t be a problem.”

Claudia said this quietly with her eyes closed.

“Hmm. I’ll check if there are traps.”

Saying this, Sheila moved to unlock it.

She inserted a tool into the keyhole and worked on it… before long, there was the sound of the lock opening, and the treasure chest opened its mouth.

“…A Wand?”

A type of magic staff. Size-wise, it’s only about as long as my waist.

The primarily black wand has delicate silver decorations, with a large blue-glowing stone set at the end. Probably some kind of magic stone.

“I sense considerable magical power… but appraisal should wait until we return.”

“Understood. I’ll transfer it safely then.”

When I handed the Wand to Claudia, she immediately transferred it away.

Being a magic staff, it wasn’t heavy. And at the bottom of the treasure chest, a magic array was drawn in an inconspicuous color.

So then—the construction was such that the trap wouldn’t activate if magical power remained in the treasure chest, rather than based on weight. Probably designed so you could successfully collect just the contents by leaving something like a Magic Slave in the box.

Even if there’s some kind of mechanism, it’s likely a legitimate magic wand. Depending on its performance, having a party member use it might be good. Well, for now we’ll put it on hold.

It must have been quite some time since we started wandering through the maze. Caduceus is handling the mapping. The approximate length of each passageway. The positions of corners and rooms are accurately memorized, so we know exactly how we got here from the entrance.

It’s easy to understand since it displays our traveled path transformed into a three-dimensional representation. Thanks to that, we’re getting a rough idea of the maze’s overall layout.

“…Let’s continue in this direction. From the entrance, this would be the farthest location in terms of distance.”

Given this maze’s troublesome nature, I suspect the exit might be in a place that requires detours, even if you know about them.

We continue advancing cautiously as before. We don’t have to worry about being affected by the heat, and we don’t need to collect Transference Stones. We should allocate that much more awareness to vigilance.

As we scattered the Living Armors and Heavy Armors that attack with surprise attacks and pincer movements as their basics, along with Bomb Rocks and Hellhounds—we eventually found a door slightly different in nature from what we’d seen so far.

It was the same kind of door as the one we descended into the maze from. After carefully checking for traps and opening the door, we saw a spiral staircase leading upward.

“Will this take us to the castle courtyard? Be careful since Bomb Rocks sometimes camouflage themselves as garden stones. And of course, don’t let your guard down on the spiral staircase either.”

“Understood.”

After confirming that everyone, starting with Grace, nodded, we began ascending the spiral staircase.

Well then… If we emerge into the courtyard, the Sub-Guardian should be there, along with the return stone monument.

“The Sub-Guardian in the courtyard was a Lava Chimera, right?”

“Yeah. A chimera that spits molten rock. There are Elephas Soldiers with it too.”

I’m pretending I read about it in documents, but I have fought the real thing in BFO, after all.

For countermeasures, we should probably focus on water magic. There are also bipedal elephant warriors that appear simultaneously… those might be in Grace’s area of expertise.

More problematic than that is the terrain. The courtyard has artificial ponds and waterways… but what flows through them is lava.

We can handle this by focusing on aerial combat and avoiding getting close to the lava areas. I’ll handle the Lava Chimera.

And—the spiral staircase was coming to an end. We opened the door and advanced into the courtyard. There, illuminated in vivid red, was a scorching world even hotter than the underground maze.

Lava flowing down from the castle walls poured into the waterways at the courtyard’s edge, forming artificial ponds and small streams that crossed the courtyard.

This much was as expected. But—

“That is—”

The corpse of a decapitated Elephas Soldier lay scattered in the courtyard. Evidence of Bomb Rocks detonating here and there was visible.

And—the corpse of a Lava Chimera with its upper body plunged into a lava pool, motionless, and the figure of a single knight sitting atop its massive body, carrying an absurdly long sword.

A knight clad in silver armor polished enough to reflect the scenery.

When the knight noticed our presence, it stood up with sword in hand. And spoke.

“—Are you those who seek the Orb?”

“The Orb…?”

Who is this? They don’t feel like a demon…

As I took a defensive stance and looked at the knight, the knight continued.

“If you do not seek the Orb, then depart via that stone monument.”

“And if we say we do seek it?”

“That much is obvious. My master commanded me to measure whether you possess power worthy of entrusting the Orb. Know that though the door’s Seal remains unbroken, you cannot advance to the door unless you demonstrate your power to me.”

This knight… essentially serves the same role as the Water Dragon in the Water Spirit Hall, then.

“I am the shadow left by the Mirror Knight Lazaro. I awakened with the water’s release and, by my master’s command, have been awaiting you here.”

“Mirror Knight…!”

It was Rosemary who reacted to those words.

“You know of him?”

“Yes. A legendary knight of Verdgar…”

When Grace asked, Rosemary furrowed her brows and said.

“I said I am a shadow. I am Lazaro yet not Lazaro. Merely a remnant incorporated into the labyrinth, inheriting only the ideal and techniques.”

“…A magical creature’s… replica, I suppose?”

When Claudia said this, Lazaro raised his sword before his eyes, holding it aloft as if presenting it.

“That understanding will suffice. I have honed my skills continuously for this day to come. Therefore—know that whether you be descendants of my master or masters of the labyrinth, I cannot let you pass unless you demonstrate power worthy of entrustment. This is proof of my loyalty to the royal family, the final mission bestowed upon me by the king.”

Lazaro’s words—were probably directed at Marlene, Rosemary, and Claudia.

So then, the master who created this shadow of Lazaro would be… the Verdgar king of that time and the Seven Sages who cooperated with him, I suppose?

The fact that it’s not the original person itself is probably because human bodies and minds cannot withstand the vast flow of time.

It’s different from Claudia.

“Understood…”

I nodded, took a deep breath, and stepped forward.

“So we fight our way through. That’s fine, right?”

“Exactly.”

Lazaro leaped and landed in the center of the courtyard.

We were supposed to fight the Sub-Guardian… but this has turned out quite different from our plans.

“I’ll fight alone. Everyone, don’t interfere.”

After telling everyone this, I stepped forward.

“Commendable, youth.”

His voice tone had a somewhat pleased ring to it.

I can’t see the face beneath the helmet… but is he smiling? His standing posture, sword lowered in natural stance, shows no openings. Naturally, I could feel my own face twisting into a joyful expression.

+++

# **300 – Water Mirror**

Even though I said I would face him alone, Lazaro showed no sign of taking it as an insult or letting his guard down. Perhaps it was because he held in high regard anyone capable of reaching the Blazing Fortress. He must have considered the possibility of his own defeat… but that couldn’t be the only reason.

By showing him the spectacle of me slaying the Lava Chimera, I intended to demonstrate my capabilities to someone who possessed the skill to advance through the Blazing Fortress.

Even if he could detect our approach because he was integrated with the labyrinth… timing his entrance into the courtyard to coincide with our arrival, defeating the Sub-Guardians, and creating a situation where we could see their corpses was only possible because he possessed sufficient strength and reserves.

Precisely because we were opponents capable of advancing through the fortress interior, he must have estimated that we could gauge each other’s capabilities.

“Before we begin, there is one thing I should mention. I am but a shadow, and therefore do not possess extensive knowledge. That is to say, there is no need for any restraint. If there is anything you wish to know, you would do better to ask my master, who will awaken when the Seal is broken.”

…I see. Because he is a Magical Creature, he hasn’t inherited all of Lazaro’s memories. Combat, loyalty, and mission. Only the necessary elements remain; the information is held by those whom Lazaro recognizes as his master.

But the number of people Lazaro would recognize in such a way… probably isn’t very large.

“So the shadow of the former King Verdgar is the lord of the Blazing Fortress.”

“That is correct.”

Lazaro answered quietly. Fighting Spirit rose from his entire body, coiling around his sword. Slowly, as if performing Iai, he drew his Greatsword back and assumed a Stance.

I wrapped Ouroboros in Magical Power and kicked off the ground. The moment I stepped in, Lazaro also charged forward.

A bizarre movement—as if his body had simply grown larger in an instant. Judging from the Greatsword’s Stance, the Slash Attack trajectory would be from the side, or perhaps from above.

Yet the first strike was an upward swing from directly below. It cleaved through the courtyard ground as if it were butter, the Greatsword rebounding upward. I performed a Form Shift to evade it. A metallic mass like a storm passed right by my side.

Lazaro killed the sword’s momentum through sheer physical strength alone, then swung the halted tip horizontally. A fusion of brute force and honed skill.

But I stepped in regardless. I blocked it with Ouroboros, concentrating my Magical Power, and deployed a Shield in the opposite direction to withstand the impact without being blown away.

Despite having shifted the point of impact, the moment I blocked it, a heavy Shockwave pierced through. The form of the Fighting Spirit coiling around the Greatsword’s blade. And the quality of that impact.

More of a Strike than a Slash Attack. He was killing the blade’s edge through manipulation of his Fighting Spirit.

It was likely a consideration for this being a test of strength—to avoid killing even with a direct hit—but it wasn’t mere leniency or holding back. It was simply him wielding his sword as he saw fit.

After all, with a heavy Weapon like that, a bad hit would mean death, and even without that, serious injury would be unavoidable.

That’s precisely why this was a ground battle. A head-on clash using skill. Otherwise, it would be meaningless.

Sliding Ouroboros along the blade I had blocked, I took another step forward. He released one hand from his sword and launched a Back Fist imbued with Fighting Spirit.

I blocked it with a Shield, simultaneously driving a fist upward from below. Shockwave Strike. As his arm rebounded, I twisted my body and swept Ouroboros in a wrapping motion from the blind spot behind him. By the time my fist had rebounded and slipped past his side, Lazaro had also stepped forward.

Without even turning around, the sword carved through the ground and rebounded upward from below. The moment it cut the ground and the moment it aimed for the opponent. He was switching the quality of his Fighting Spirit. I evaded with a Cartwheel. Lazaro also shifted his body to face me and immediately charged forward.

Again. That peculiar footwork, gliding without changing the height of his head or shoulders. A movement that disrupted the sense of distance. Gripping Ouroboros with both hands, I lunged forward with my whole body, crashing into his sword as if to push through. I received it diagonally and was deflected. The momentum carried me backward.

No problem. Although this is a ground battle, as part of my Martial Arts, I’ll mobilize my aerial combat techniques as well. Kicking off the Shield two, three times, I shifted my position left and right while activating Mirage Body to send forth illusions.

“This is—”

Making a movement as if striking from diagonally above, I thrust from below with the opposite end toward his flank. Lazaro swung his sword upward with his right hand to intercept the attack from above, while concentrating Fighting Spirit in his free left hand to catch the tip of Ouroboros. His left hand’s reaction was barely in time… but to see through this without prior knowledge.

Inside the sword’s range. Not a blow from the blade, but the pommel descending as if swinging a fist down. I met it with Ouroboros. The pommel wrapped in Fighting Spirit collided violently. Deflected, I overlapped my illusion and body again before flying off in another direction.

Lazaro stomped his foot, shattering the ground and sending up a cloud of dust, then accurately tracked my true body by catching the flow of air with the corner of his eye. Illusions don’t disturb the air, so they can be distinguished.

I received the Greatsword with the Dragon Staff and redirected it. Deflecting, parrying, striking back, scattering countless sparks.

The Greatsword, which I had dodged, curved at a right angle to pursue me. I blocked it with a Shield, placed a hand on my Armor’s abdomen, and drove in a Shockwave Strike.

Lazaro momentarily stepped back, but then pressed forward as if intensifying the pressure.

The moment our Weapons clashed, were deflected, and distance opened between us, Lazaro’s empty hand shot upward. A tsunami-like Fighting Spirit Shockwave flew toward me. I leaped far to the side and also unleashed Magic. A Spear of Lightning Strike. As Lazaro stood his ground, his sword flashed, and the released Lightning Strike decayed, scattering into the void. That was—should I say he interfered with it using Fighting Spirit to disperse it?

“Severing demons is the Tachi of the Water Mirror”… was it? One of the Hidden Arts of Fighting Spirit Techniques. A Technique that uses refined, Cleansing energy to sever demons.

Effective against Magic… and against Demons. It should also interfere with a Demon’s Flight Technique. Probably—the origin of Lazaro’s epithet. Half-baked Techniques will be cut down, this one will.

“…Magical Power Circulation, is it. To think the Water Mirror couldn’t completely block it… And that honing… How splendid. But—not yet. It’s still insufficient.”

That’s right. Even so, a Battle Mage’s Technique doesn’t decay completely. But after looking at his own palm, Lazaro made a fist.

“…Ah, I suppose so.”

What Lazaro seeks is an opponent with enough strength to slay a High-ranking Demon. What I’ve shown so far isn’t enough to satisfy him.

I refined my Magical Power, raising it as I assumed a Stance. As Ouroboros roared within that, he too began emitting an unprecedented, massive amount of Fighting Spirit from his entire body.

As if by mutual agreement, we stepped in. We closed the distance at a speed that made the kicked ground explode. The descending Greatsword. The rebounding Dragon Staff. Collision and impact. A weight greater than before. But I wasn’t losing the exchange. Our Weapons were deflected from each other.

The Greatsword showed a storm-like return swing. I redirected it and struck with the Dragon Staff’s blow. Gouging the ground, scattering streams of lava, we clashed violently time and time again.

Slipping through, I swept across his flank. Not a direct hit. The blow I drove into his flank, Lazaro was defending by concentrating his Fighting Spirit. A tactic of wearing him down by landing numerous Shockwave Strikes… probably isn’t what’s being sought here.

The moment distance opened, a crawling Fighting Spirit Shockwave flew toward me. I avoided it without using Magic, relying on my body alone, and charged the shortest distance through the stream of lava it had split along the way.

He’s smiling. I can’t see inside his Helmet, but Lazaro must surely be smiling too. Countless scattered sparks. The incessant clashing of blades and the roaring sound of cutting wind. We shifted positions, crossing like dancers. Bouncing from Shield to Shield, we engaged as we pleased.

Inside the Greatsword’s range. Into that space where I should be at a disadvantage, Lazaro willingly stepped forward. A reckless body check. I received it with a Shield. He stopped the body check, but with a sharp battle cry, he unleashed a Palm Strike that shattered my Shield to pieces. A Palm Strike wrapped in Fighting Spirit of the same quality as the Water Mirror. To think such a thing—was possible.

He pushed my body upward as if to lift me. And there—a horizontal torso-cleaving strike bore down. I couldn’t block it completely with a Shield. If I tried to disengage, his free hand would probably grab my clothing. If I receive it—the Shield will be severed by the Water Mirror Tachi.

I positioned Ouroboros, wrapped in circulating Magical Power, in the Slash Attack’s trajectory to receive it as a Shield. It didn’t need to be perfect. I placed it in the trajectory, imbued with Magical Power so intense it shone. Ouroboros, having received the sword, dug into my body. I anchored myself with a Shield to avoid being blown away. The Greatsword, which had tried to complete its swing, stopped its movement—that was the moment.

“This is—!”

I had driven a Palm Strike upward from below toward the middle of the blade. The spiral Magical Shockwave I had used on Zadias. Simultaneously, I fixed the sword’s tip from above with a Magic Shield.

As a result, the Greatsword snapped in half from the middle, shattering to pieces. I retrieved Ouroboros and returned the Magical Power I had wrapped around it to my main body. Flowing it across my body surface from arm to waist. From waist to leg.

“Fly!”

Full-body coordination. A kicking blow released with added twist. The second Spiral Shockwave, focused on my toes, caught Lazaro’s torso. A violent force detonated at a single point. Lazaro’s body spun like a windmill as he was blown away toward the gate leading to the main keep.

The first and second shots. I combined the Magical Power I had left unused and immediately deployed a giant Magic Circle.

Lightning Magic, 7th Tier: Lightning Blast. A Magic that the Water Mirror cannot completely block.

I unleashed it not at Lazaro—who was still airborne—but toward the sky above the courtyard.

The white light of the Lightning Strike illuminated the courtyard. As expected, there seemed to be a Barrier in the sky. The enormous Lightning Strike, enough to fill one’s vision, was blocked by the Barrier and disappeared while scattering purple electricity in the air. A moment later, Lazaro crashed back-first into the gate.

Holding Ouroboros at the ready, I looked toward Lazaro. Lazaro tried to stand using his broken Greatsword as a support on the ground… but he shook his head and sat down on the spot, leaning against the gate.

“My defeat, it seems. It was, after all, merely a test of skill.”

+++

# **301 – The Magician and the Ancient Knight**

“Theodore-sama!”

Led by Ashley, everyone came running over.

“Are you injured?”

“I’m fine. The Ouroboros took the hit for me.”

I might end up with some bruises later… but considering who I fought and how, that’s to be expected.

Just to be safe, Ashley used Healing Magic on me.

“Theodore, was it?”

Lazaro spoke. His voice was remarkably calm.

“You have good companions.”

“Yes. They’re precious to me.”

When I nodded at Lazaro’s words, I thought I could hear him chuckle softly beneath his helmet.

“At your age, with such skill. Your Magical Power Circulation… you must be a descendant of those sorcerers.”

“It seems so. I only recently found out myself, so I don’t know much about it. Do you know something about that?”

When I asked, Lazaro shook his head.

“As I said earlier. I possess only the minimal memories necessary to be myself and fulfill my purpose. I only spoke with those sorcerers face to face when fighting the Demons. I could tell you why I took up the sword, or how those sorcerers fought, but I doubt that’s the information you’re seeking.”

Why he took up the sword. I see… Motivation is an important topic.

“Not necessarily. I think many people would want to hear about it, and I’m interested too.”

“Hmm. Well, I have some questions for you as well. But first… why don’t you collect the spoils from the monsters?”

Lazaro pointed toward the corpses of the Lava Chimera and Elephas Soldiers.

Some of the monster corpses Lazaro had slain had disappeared… but the Lava Chimera left behind a fairly high-quality Magic Stone. Though it doesn’t have the Fire Element like the Flame Demon’s Magic Stone, it should be quite useful for building the airship.

From the Elephas Soldier, we got ivory. It should have various uses.

After finishing collecting the materials, I went to Lazaro, who was standing by the stone monument, to continue our earlier conversation.

“What did you want to ask me?”

“There are several things… First, I’d like to know about the situation outside. For someone of your caliber to come retrieve the Orb… it can’t be for nothing.”

“That’s right… Well then—”

I proceeded to tell Lazaro about our fight against the Demon group.

“—You even defeated the Black Bones? I wouldn’t have believed it if not for having tested your strength myself…”

When I briefly explained the circumstances, Lazaro shook his head. Gardinis, huh? That guy seems to have been notorious since Lazaro’s time.

“Is there anything else you wanted to ask?”

“Hm? Ah, no, it’s a trivial matter. I was fighting you to test you. But, young man… you were different. For example, that clothing of yours.”

Lazaro glanced at my Chimera Coat. It seems he had noticed that my clothing was some kind of Magic Tool. It was supposed to be a contest of skill with just our weapons… True, I didn’t use Nemea, Capella, or Balor.

“You had no reason to hold back your cards and accommodate my methods. I understand you wanted to earn my recognition, but I wondered if you really needed to go that far… It just struck me as curious. You probably already guessed, but I’m not human.”

Saying this, he opened the visor of his helmet. Inside was a skeletal face. After showing it briefly, he immediately lowered the visor again.

“Even this form isn’t made from real bones. It’s all just a creation of magic.”

Considering this is the Blazing Fortress, I thought it would be a harsh place for a normal human to be stationed…

Perhaps he was given properties close to an undead to preserve a human’s will. His Fighting Spirit, and especially his use of Water Mirror, probably place him well outside the framework of ordinary undead.

But… Lazaro’s question…

I can understand that Lazaro accepted defeat and his own destruction. If the opponent who defeats him is someone from the Verdgar royal family or Claudia’s side, then even in defeat, he would have achieved his purpose.

The fact that he wields a Greatsword also makes it difficult for opponents to hold back against him. That’s precisely why Lazaro told us not to hesitate and to come to defeat him. That’s also why he revealed that someone else had the information. Or perhaps… he thinks I was being soft for not coming to kill him.

“…It’s not that I looked down on you. How should I put it… It’s stubbornness.”

“Stubbornness?”

“I hate Demons. For me, killing you—who has fulfilled your mission for so long—for the sake of fighting Demons would be putting the cart before the horse. I couldn’t stand it.”

When I said this, Lazaro froze for a moment, then began to chuckle softly. Soon he was laughing out loud, his shoulders shaking.

“I see, I see. Indeed, I hate Demons too. The living Lazaro and you might have gotten along well, young man.”

“Perhaps. But I don’t think you’re an imposter. Since your mission is over, don’t you think we could explore ways for you not to be bound to the labyrinth… the Blazing Fortress?”

“Kukuku. You become more interesting. Even after seeing my face, you can still say that?”

“I don’t think appearance matters much.”

If I said otherwise, my words to Claudia would become lies too.

When I spoke, Claudia closed her eyes and smiled quietly.

“If we create an outpost of the Blazing Fortress in Termwills… you might be able to go outside. Though that would require a contract with the castle lord.”

“Hmm. I don’t understand much about magic… but I’ll look forward to what happens after my master awakens.”

Saying this, Lazaro offered a handshake. I took his hand.

“I’ll come again before the seal is released. I’d like to visit up to the Sealed Door. Would it be alright if I collect the broken sword?”

“Fine by me. What do you intend to use it for?”

“No. I was thinking of repairing it and returning it. I imagine it would be difficult to be in the Blazing Fortress without a weapon.”

“Hmm.”

Lazaro pensively touched his chin, then picked up the Elephas Soldier’s scimitar that was lying nearby. This too seemed to be a considerably heavy weapon.

When he thrust the thick-bladed scimitar’s tip into the ground, a heavy sound and vibration resonated through my feet.

“Then… let’s make it a promise. This blade should suffice for the time being.”

“Understood. Then, until another day.”

“Mm. My battle with you… it’s been a long time since I enjoyed one so much.”

“Me too.”

After exchanging these words—we left the labyrinth via the stone monument, seen off by Lazaro.

After returning from the labyrinth… I decided to first head to the Adventurer Guild to exchange today’s spoils—the staff, ivory, Living Armor parts, Hellhound pelts, and other materials—for money.

During the wait while our materials were being appraised, Rosemary murmured.

“…The Mirror Knight Lazaro, huh?”

“I didn’t get to ask earlier, but what kind of stories are told about him?”

When Grace asked, Rosemary covered her mouth with her feather fan as she answered.

“He’s a famous figure in the Verdgar Knight Order. According to literature, he devised the secret technique Water Mirror and saved Verdgar from crisis. Considering the situation at the time, it was probably related to Demons after all.”

So he was the one who created Water Mirror. I didn’t know that.

“I’ve heard stories about the Silver Knight. In fairy tales, it was just about how he led the knight order and fought Demons.”

Ashley said.

“The Mirror… Silver Knight. Lazaro might be the basis for that. But while that mirror-like armor is famous, it seems not much was known about the person beneath it.”

“That’s probably for the same reason as me.”

“Most likely. The important thing was that there was a Demon Slayer, and if he served as a standard-bearer, his armored appearance was sufficient.”

Also, they probably didn’t want to leak information about Water Mirror.

As for why Lazaro took up the sword… even without being told, it’s something you can guess. Since he probably hates Demons too, that’s likely why he understood my reasoning.

…Well then. After we’re done here, should I head to the workshop as I told Old Sigmund? I’ve also added the plan to have Lazaro’s sword repaired.

+++

# **302 – Towards the Full Moon Night**

“This is… quite the masterwork,” Viola murmured admiringly as she examined Lazaro’s greatsword.

Ah. So it really was a fine piece after all. I wonder if breaking it was problematic.

After finishing our business at the Adventurer Guild, we had immediately brought it to the workshop.

“We encountered various things in the labyrinth. I’d like to have this sword repaired – is it possible?”

“I’ll give it a try. I can’t believe I get to handle such a fine weapon.”

Viola cheerfully carried the greatsword into the adjacent room. Hmm. With that attitude, she’ll probably be able to repair it. As she left, Grace returned carrying a tea set on a tray.

Well then, let’s have a leisurely conversation over tea.

“So you went to the Blazing Fortress? What happened there?” Alfred asked, tilting his head as I took a breather while drinking the tea Grace had prepared.

“Well, do you know about the Mirror Knight Lazaro?”

“Ah. That story has been passed down in the Verdgar royal family.”

“It seems they transplanted Lazaro’s memories and combat skills into a magical creature to serve as a guardian for the Orb.”

When I said this, Alfred’s eyes widened.

“He apparently wanted to test whether I was worthy of entrusting with the Orb, so we had a sparring match to gauge my skills,” Rosemary added by way of explanation.

“I see… So that’s why Theo-kun fought him.”

“It was like this – he stopped the sword’s movement, then pinched it with his shield and snapped it from below,” Sheila explained with gestures.

“…Well now. If I kept being surprised by everything Theo-kun does, I’d never survive… But still, that was quite something to do to an opponent like that.”

“I think at the end, he was also going all-in to win. He probably intended to break my ribs around there and finish me off.”

If he had been using feints or maintaining the flexibility to change tactics based on my movements, it would have been difficult to deliberately break his sword.

“And so, regarding who likely left Lazaro’s shadow behind… I believe it might have been one of the Seven Sages who cooperated with Verdgar.”

Old Sigmund stroked his beard when I broached the subject.

“Can we hear from that person?”

“I believe we can. However, it seems he doesn’t retain many memories unrelated to combat. Since there’s also the shadow of the Verdgar king from that time, he said he’d like you to hear the story from him once the seal is broken.”

“Oh?”

“From my perspective… I’m wondering if such techniques for creating magical creatures still exist in Silvatoria. While we could create an outpost of the Blazing Fortress outside the labyrinth to allow them to leave… I think the best outcome would be for both Lazaro and the former king to be released from the labyrinth and be able to live ordinary lives after fulfilling their duties.”

At my words, Old Sigmund nodded as if convinced. He and Valentina both wore somewhat happy expressions.

The same goes for Claudia. If the Seven Sages used the labyrinth’s mechanisms to create the seal, then researching their techniques and spell formulas should be useful not only for Lazaro and the others, but also for Claudia’s liberation.

“In that case, I’d be happy to cooperate.”

“If we’re talking about techniques for creating such unique magical creatures, would they be in the ancient documents stored in the treasure room?” Valentina said after a moment’s thought.

“Most likely. If the Seven Sages were involved in sealing the demon within the labyrinth, then sealing-related techniques would probably be treated as secret arts.”

“When His Majesty Eberhart returns, it seems we’ll need to head to Vinesdora as well,” the two of them began discussing arrangements for that time.

Since Zadias and Volheim likely have information too, we’ll probably need to visit Vinesdora ourselves.

For now, let’s have them take a look at today’s harvest of magic stones and such.

“And… these are today’s spoils.”

I placed the Lava Chimera’s magic stone and other items we brought back on the table.

“My, my. To bring back such magic stones. Encountering such formidable creatures so readily is characteristic of the Boundary Labyrinth… but no, it’s only possible because you’re here to defeat them.”

“I should add that the monster that housed this magic stone was defeated by Sir Lazaro, so I didn’t actually fight it,” I clarified.

It seems we still need to collect a few more magic stones for the airship construction. Well, let’s continue exploring the labyrinth at this pace.

When we returned home, Justia the Siren and Dominique the Harpy had come to visit.

It was about the upcoming full moon performance. Since Irmhild had been out with us in Silvatoria, they needed to practice together.

I worked on deciphering Mother’s notes while listening to their performance in the game room. It seemed they were practicing a new song.

Clear singing voices and musical tones filled the entertainment room. The Carbuncles who had been playing in the courtyard stopped their chasing game and lined up along the game room window frame, listening intently.

Eventually, as if they had finished a round of practice, Justia looked up and said, “Irm was practicing properly after all.”

“The new song went smoothly too. With this, the performance should be fine.”

“Though it wasn’t really practice – she was just so happy to learn the new song that she played it everywhere she went,” Irmhild said with a wry smile.

“Is the coordination with the stage going well?”

“That’s fine. They’ve let us practice at the theater several times already.”

“Actually, we’d like to perform with Sheila and Cyrille too, including the new instruments.”

“Right?” When I asked, the three monster girls exchanged glances and said this.

Sheila plays drums, and Cyrille the Centaur plays bagpipes.

“Hmm. Still need more practice. We also have to think about the stage effects.”

“It changes things when new instruments are added,” Sheila and Cyrille nodded.

Aside from Irmhild, Sheila had been out in Silvatoria, so she hadn’t had much time to practice.

“It might be good to practice with both of them here too. Our sound coordination has been going well, so we have time.”

“Then let’s,” they decided to practice with all five of them this time. Everyone else in the game room seemed interested in their practice too, stopping their billiards and darts games to watch.

“This is fascinating. So she can handle multiple percussion instruments by herself?” Camilla said, watching from where she had been relaxing with Elliot. Ashley nodded at her words.

“Theodore-sama made them.”

“I see…”

“It’s not like we’ve never seen them before,” Elliot and Old Sigmund nodded admiringly at Ashley’s words.

Sheila and the others seemed ready.

They started with Sheila’s solo part, it seemed. Regular, subdued drum sounds echoed through the room. Cyrille, who had released her Humanization Spell, tapped her hooves in rhythm with the drums as if doing a tap dance.

The drum sounds resonating in our lower abdomens and the floor-tapping sounds overlapped briskly, creating a pleasant rhythm.

The drumming had a somewhat ethnic feel to it. Irmhild and the others’ performance and singing voices layered over it. Cyrille was playing the bagpipes while dancing. Powerful drums combined with mystical singing voices… creating a song that felt expansive, both mysterious and grand.

As the song progressed, Sheila’s drumming elevated the entire musical composition. Her precise rhythm-keeping was truly impressive. The singing ended, and the final part featured another drum solo by Sheila. Her two sticks flashed at considerable speed, striking drums and cymbals.

Leaving just a slight aftertaste and reverberation, Sheila’s movements stopped.

Then, applause erupted from everyone present in the game room.

“It’s a wonderful song,” Grace said with a smile.

“…Even though you said you needed more practice, it doesn’t look like there are any problems,” Rosemary said while clapping, and Marlene nodded repeatedly.

“We can only really show one song like this satisfactorily.”

I see. So it’s a matter of repertoire.

“What about the stage production?”

“That’s more or less decided.”

Hmm. In that case…

“How about joining in to perform one song towards the end of the concert?”

“That’s a good idea. Then it doesn’t matter if the program is long or short.”

“What do you two think?” At my suggestion, they looked happy and were encouraging Sheila and Cyrille to participate.

“Then… I’ll do my best.”

“We need to practice.”

“Hmm.”

Sheila had her usual expression, but that was just her way of showing determination. They continued their performance practice. Yes, I’m looking forward to seeing how the next performance turns out.

+++

# **303 – Before the Performance**

The day of the performance had arrived.

First, I went to pick them up at Marquis Zilbolt’s domain, then transported the Marquis and his party directly to the ritual site before heading to Peresford Academy.

My companions were Tephra, Marquis Zilbolt, Lady Belinda, and the members of the Intelligence Unit who had returned from Vinesdora to the Marquis’s domain. They had been invited as this time’s honored guests.

“Good day, Theodore-sama. Father, Mother, it’s wonderful to see you both looking so well.”

“Good day.”

“Indeed. It’s equally wonderful to see you looking well too, Romina.”

Romina, who had been waiting at the Peresford Academy dormitory after hearing about the arrangements in advance, showed a happy expression and bowed as her parents descended from the carriage.

“Good day, Ophelia-sama, Romina-sama.”

“Good day, Ashley-sama.”

It seemed Ophelia had come along too. Since she’s quite caring, she appears to have built a good relationship with Romina. Ashley exchanged smiling greetings with Ophelia and Romina.

“There’s still quite some time before the theater performance begins. What would you like to do? If you have no plans, you’re welcome to pass the time at our home.”

Ilmhild and the others’ performance wasn’t scheduled until around evening. When I asked, Marquis Zilbolt replied.

“That’s very kind. Let me see… Last time we visited Termwills, we couldn’t really relax much… First, we’ll head to secure our lodging, then take a carriage to look around the city a bit. Would it be alright if we visit you after that?”

“Understood. I’ll inform the household accordingly.”

So Marquis Zilbolt and his family would spend time together. They remain such a close-knit family.

“As for our escort, there should be no issues. After all, look at this lineup.”

The Marquis gave a wry smile as he surveyed the carriage carrying the Intelligence Unit members.

“Indeed. Well then, until later.”

“Yes. Until then.”

I gave Marquis Zilbolt and his party their admission tickets and decided to head to the theater. There were quite a few invited guests this time as well, but they were scheduled to enter the theater before the performance began.

Now then. With the main event approaching, I went to check on the theater and found the square more crowded than usual. Apparently, the tickets had sold out long ago, but it seemed some people who couldn’t make it on the day were coming to get refunds. Adventurers were probably gathered at the Guild hoping to snag seats that might become available through refunds. Knights and soldiers were stationed around the square to prevent any trouble from occurring.

There were even lines forming at the stalls in front of the theater selling shaved ice, cotton candy, and carbonated drinks… They seemed to be managing the queues and such too.

Knight Order Commander Mildred was also here. She was probably supervising the soldiers.

Not only King Melvin but also King Eberhart, Princess Stephania, and Princess Adriana were coming to watch today’s theater performance, so security was naturally going to be tight.

Mildred noticed our carriage and approached us.

“Well, if it isn’t the Ambassador,” she called out, so I descended from the carriage to greet her.

“Good day, Dame Mildred. With the increased crowd, it looks quite challenging.”

“Yes, indeed. The hot spring town and theater have become quite the topic of conversation, attracting more and more visitors. Since foreign dignitaries are attending today, I’ve been entrusted with field command.”

“I see.”

Mildred showed a slightly thoughtful expression before asking.

“Speaking of which, I heard about the matter at Blazing Fortress.”

“…Are you referring to the Mirror Knight, by any chance?”

We had arranged for Alfred to inform King Melvin about Lazaro, planning to discuss everything together after today’s performance—but as one of King Melvin’s close aides, it seemed the information had reached Mildred.

“Yes. The Mirror Knight Lazaro is actually my ancestor. Though I haven’t made this widely known.”

“Is that so?”

That was somewhat surprising. It seemed to be information even Rosemary wasn’t aware of—though she was hiding her mouth behind her feather fan, her eyes appeared wide. Mildred gave a wry smile at our reaction.

“I’m from a branch family, you see. I’d rather not have people say I became Knight Order Commander due to my lineage after revealing details about my origins.”

I see. Even though Mildred is said to have sword skills that stand out even among the knights… I get the sense she must have faced various hardships. King Melvin probably knows, of course, but since it’s not something Mildred wants publicized, he likely hasn’t made a point of announcing it.

“We plan to reforge his sword and bring it to Blazing Fortress in the near future… Would you care to accompany us?”

“…Is that acceptable?”

“Yes. Once we have a concrete plan, I’ll contact you as soon as possible. That should make it easier to coordinate our schedules.”

“Understood. I’ll also petition His Majesty regarding this matter.”

Being both Knight Order Commander and one of King Melvin’s close aides, Mildred must be quite busy with various matters.

“Well then, we’ll be going inside the theater to look around.”

“Yes. I’m looking forward to today’s performance.”

“Thank you.”

After saying this, I parted ways with Mildred for now, had the carriage stop at the staff entrance, and entered the theater from there.

“Well then, I’m off to practice.”

“See you later, Theodore-kun.”

“I’m heading out.”

Sheila, Ilmhild, and Cyrille headed toward the stage.

“Hmm. This is another place Theodore created, isn’t it?”

Tephra looked around the theater with apparent interest.

“Yeah. Well, there’s still time before the performance starts, but I’ll show you around while checking things.”

As for me, I decided to check if there were any issues within the theater while inspecting the facilities. I toured the theater with Seraphina, explaining various equipment to Tephra.

“Are there any areas under particular strain?”

“Hmm. Everything seems fine, I think?”

With Seraphina perched on my shoulder, I looked around the theater. After all, Seraphina had checked everything during construction, and the workmanship is solid. There don’t appear to be any particular problems.

At the theater’s internal concession stands, employees were busy making shaved ice and cotton candy or transporting them to the external stalls. The magic tools seemed to be functioning without issues.

“The employees have been issued uniforms, I see. Having uniformity really creates an atmosphere.”

When Claudia spoke admiringly, Marlene nodded.

The theater employees had been provided with uniforms—servant-style outfits but with matching hats featuring feather decorations. King Melvin had handled this aspect, and his sense of style is indeed excellent.

Young people were notably prominent among the employees. This included those who had graduated from the orphanage and started working at the theater or hot spring town.

They seemed quite busy but were working happily. I shouldn’t get in their way, so I decided to go check the stage equipment.

When I went backstage, I saw Brad, the boy I’d met at the orphanage. Though I should mention I knew him from when I was disguised as Mathius, so of course he doesn’t recognize me.

The feather decoration on his hat was white—apparently the color indicating an apprentice. This was probably because Brad hadn’t yet left the orphanage.

Brad was standing slightly behind the stage equipment operator, watching the rehearsal procedures and operation sequences with a serious expression. Incidentally, the person operating the stage equipment was Annie from the Mage Corps on temporary assignment—also an acquaintance of Alfred’s.

She’s someone I met once when I first visited Theoreme Castle.

Apparently she was selected from the Mage Corps because it’s preferable for someone operating stage equipment to possess magical power and be familiar with magic tool operation. There’s a possibility Alfred pulled some strings since he considers her trustworthy.

“Well, if it isn’t the Ambassador.”

Not wanting to be disruptive, I was observing from a slight distance when Annie noticed me during a break and greeted me.

“Good day.”

“Good day, Ambassador.”

When I returned the greeting, Brad also bowed his head.

“Good work. The number of musical pieces has increased, but are the preparations going smoothly?”

As I spoke, I glanced toward the stage. The five of them seemed to be in the middle of practice. I could see Forestbird and the others applauding from the audience seats. They must have escorted Justia and Dominique to the theater.

“Yes. We just ran through the new piece as well. I don’t think there will be any issues with the sequence.”

Annie adjusted her glasses while smiling cheerfully.

“Are there any problems with the stage equipment?”

“Everything’s running smoothly. Oh, let me introduce you. This is Brad from the orphanage, here as an apprentice.”

“N-nice to meet you, Ambassador. My name is Brad. Pleased to make your acquaintance.”

Brad stood at attention with a nervous expression. The mischievous boy I remembered from before was nowhere to be seen. You could tell he was taking his work seriously.

“Indeed. Pleased to meet you.”

“He’s quite talented, actually. I’ve been teaching at the orphanage, and he seems to have some magical aptitude.”

“Is that so?”

“Yes. He’s very eager to work at the theater, so he’s been studying the magic tool control panel. We even let him operate it during practice sessions. His enthusiasm seems genuine too.”

Magical aptitude, huh? Considering aspects like replenishing magical power in magic tools, it’s certainly preferable for someone handling the control panel to have substantial magical power.

Brad, having been introduced like that by Annie, scratched his cheek somewhat sheepishly and said,

“Magicians and the magic tools they installed once saved our—my—our lives.”

That must be referring to when the Duoveris Cult followers attacked.

“I think it’s amazing how the theater can move people using magic and magic tools. That’s why I asked to study here as an apprentice.”

…I see.

“I’m counting on you. Do your best.”

“Yes! I’ll do my best!”

When I smiled back, Brad bowed deeply. …So the stage equipment and control panel are fine.

Now all that’s left is to wait for the performance to begin. I decided to move to the audience seating area, greet Forestbird and the others, and watch the rehearsal.

“Hearing you say that makes me happy.”

“…Yeah. I suppose so.”

When my eyes met Grace’s, she smiled back happily. …Well. I’m glad I built the theater—it’s quite encouraging. I feel hopeful about the theater’s future prospects.

+++

# **304 – Five Performers**

As dusk fell and showtime approached, the invited guests began appearing at the theater one by one.

First came Father and his group. Then Elliot and the others from the Barony of Silun who had joined up with them, Old Sigmund, Valentina, and Marquis Zilbolt’s party arrived together.

Since Father and I are publicly maintaining some distance, we arranged for Ashley to extend the invitations and have them enter first.

Well, we’ve actually reconciled behind the scenes, and key figures around King Melvin—like Chancellor Howard—are aware of this. King Melvin said that if anyone tries to exploit this situation, it could actually help us determine whether they have ulterior motives.

“Thank you for inviting us today.”

“Not at all. We should be thanking you for coming.”

I greeted Father, Elliot and the others, and the entire Zilbolt household. Though my exchange with Father was purely formal, as I guided them from the entrance hall inside, he suddenly smiled softly and said,

“This is amazing… I heard you built this theater too, Theo…”

Father murmured while looking around the theater entrance. Daryl had his mouth hanging open for a moment… but soon seemed to realize this wasn’t very becoming for a noble heir, closing his mouth and shaking his head slightly with a solemn expression.

“The building, yes. But it’s also the result of cooperation from many people. Now, this way please.”

I guided Father and the others to the guest seats—the ones with the best view.

As the theater’s history grows longer, seats near the stage might become more popular, but for now, the best seats for viewing are reserved for guests.

The popularity of stage-side seats… apparently comes from noble wanting to be seen by the audience during performances. But that’s a story from Earth.

“Thank you, Theo.”

“Of course.”

I bowed to Father.

“We’ll take our time enjoying this with everyone today.”

“With Theodore-dono’s involvement, I’m looking forward to seeing what kind of performance we’ll witness.”

“Indeed. Just from the building’s structure, it seems designed to allow sound to spread easily.”

Elliot, Marquis Zilbolt, and Old Sigmund each made similar comments.

Though it seems to be Father and Marquis Zilbolt’s first meeting, they appeared to be exchanging calm words about the theater’s construction.

This is what you’d expect from fellow lords, I suppose. It seems an unexpected connection has formed between Father and Marquis Zilbolt, but when opportunities arise, building connections is simply what nobles do.

Elliot too was happily chatting with Camilla, Donato, and Kennel. Old Sigmund and Valentina seemed to be analyzing the theater’s magic tools… The atmosphere was peaceful and quite pleasant.

…Well, that should take care of this group. There are still more guests to welcome, so I returned to the entrance hall.

Arriving under knight escort, King Melvin, King Eberhart, Princess Stephania, and Princess Adriana appeared.

“Oh, Theodore!”

“We’re looking forward to being entertained today.”

The moment they saw my face, King Melvin and King Eberhart broke into broad smiles. Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana… perhaps mindful of the knights’ presence, maintained the calm smiles befitting royalty and greeted me quietly.

“We’ve been expecting you. Please, this way.”

I returned their greetings and guided them to the guest seats.

When I opened the door leading from the entrance hall to the audience seating and showed them inside, King Eberhart let out an impressed “Oh.”

“This… you’ve made considerations for sound projection. I see.”

“The magic construction techniques are impressive too… It’s wonderful. It was worth restraining my curiosity.”

“Right?”

“And after this, we have the hot springs. Marvelous.”

The two princesses exchanged words in frank tones, though quietly. Yet their gestures remained those of the upper class—quite practiced and polished.

Next, the temple officials and Guild members who had helped when Irmhild and the others held their concert earlier also entered the theater.

“Good evening, Theodore-sama. I’ve been looking forward to this day for so long!”

Miriam appeared with a beaming smile. The Dwarf craftsmen were with her too.

Since this isn’t the premiere performance, I won’t be giving any stage greetings. The theater staff will first take the stage to announce precautions, then the performance will begin on schedule. I plan to watch the show from the audience seats with everyone else.

After the VIPs finished entering, the nobles and their invited guests also came in. They each took their seats, followed by the general audience. Among them were Isabella from the Thieves Guild and Dorothy, the daughter of the former Guild Master. When they noticed me, they gave a slight glance and smile, bowing their heads in acknowledgment.

It seems all the guests I invited showed up. The general audience seating filled to capacity almost immediately after entry began.

“Hmm… It’s crowded with people… but the atmosphere seems good. Even I’m getting excited.”

Tephra, sitting in the audience seats, seemed to be in quite high spirits. Perhaps the audience’s anticipation for the performance was having an effect. For viewing, her hair was somewhat noticeable, so she apparently decided to hide it with a hood.

“Is it about time? I’m looking forward to it.”

As the audience seats filled and the doors closed, Grace asked.

“Yes. Before it starts, they’ll announce precautions, then the lights will dim.”

“The emergency evacuation routes and that the performance will begin after the lights go out, right?”

Claudia inquired.

“Correct. That’s what I talked about from the stage before.”

“The performers seem to appreciate that too.”

Added Rosemary.

Indeed. Though it’s become a standard procedure done every time… perhaps because Dominique started singing from the audience during the first concert, the rule of staying quiet after the lights dim seems to have caught on surprisingly quickly with the audience. Apparently, it’s well-received by the performers since they can start smoothly.

Just then, a staff member in uniform appeared from the wings. The chatter immediately quieted, and they were welcomed with applause. Marlene was also smiling cheerfully and clapping.

The staff member walked to center stage, bowed, and then in a clear, resonant voice announced thanks for coming to the theater and the precautions.

After one final bow, they returned to the wings accompanied by applause.

Without delay, the audience lights began extinguishing one by one from the stage side. The remaining audience chatter rapidly faded away.

And then—the theater was enveloped in darkness and silence. After a brief pause—

From somewhere, the gentle plucking of a harp resonated through the audience. Near the theater’s ceiling, wrapped in a faint blue light, the Siren Justia appeared.

It wasn’t a stage device—Justia herself was using a magic tool. This allowed for slightly broader production possibilities than before.

With a gentle singing voice, Justia in her dress floated as if swaying on waves. It was the Sirens’ lullaby. Playing a beautiful, simple melody while wrapped in bubbles and particles of light, she slowly danced above the audience.

Perhaps it was due to her racial characteristics. There was a mystique that instantly drew the audience into another world.

Singing voices overlapped. Irmhild and Dominique. They descended from the stage with swaying, gravity-defying movements. The three landed softly on the stage. A bow was met with thunderous applause.

“Thank you for coming to the Boundary Theater. I am the Siren Justia.”

Justia greeted the audience while playing her instrument. Dominique and Irmhild followed suit. After waiting for the applause to subside, the next piece began.

Dominique’s cheerful singing voice echoed as she danced through the air. When that ended, Irmhild’s fast-paced, dance-inducing music followed, successively exciting the audience.

The stage changing colors with the cyclorama according to the music. Scattering particles of light. Swirls of shimmering bubbles.

The new songs Irmhild and the others had been practicing were also performed. Repeat visitors probably noticed the subtle differences from before.

Then, as the program approached its conclusion—Irmhild spoke to the audience.

“Today, we’d like to introduce someone to everyone. Our friends Sheila and Cyrille.”

As Irmhild said this and reached a hand toward the wings, Sheila and Cyrille entered the stage. Both were wearing dresses. Cyrille’s was a specially tailored outfit for a Centaur.

Sheila bowed, then removed the silk cloth covering something prepared on stage. Beneath it was a drum set. She began playing a light rhythm as if in greeting. Starting with a regular beat, she gradually added pattern variations, steadily increasing the tempo.

The drum sounds that made you want to nod your head in time with the dazzlingly swift stick movements. Perhaps because it was a solo and she could do as she pleased, it was clear she was really getting into it. Whether due to excellent reflexes and dexterity, or being accustomed to dual wielding…

When I had Golems demonstrate programmed drum patterns as examples, she learned them with incredible speed. Apparently, the motivation to perform with Irmhild had really fired her up.

After raising the tempo to what seemed the maximum possible, she gradually slowed it down, finally striking a cymbal before speaking.

“I’m Sheila. Nice to meet you.”

Sheila’s demeanor was as usual. This was the drum set’s debut in this country, but even so, her performance would convey her high skill level even to those unfamiliar with it.

As if snapping out of their momentary astonishment, the audience erupted in loud applause.

Then, Cyrille had brought her bagpipes from the start.
