Playing a majestic sound with the bagpipes while clopping her hooves. A regular, powerful marching rhythm came from her four legs. This must also be something passed down in the Labyrinth Village. She seemed quite accustomed to it.

The atmosphere changed considerably from before—there was a relaxed, somewhat nostalgic air. Cyrille’s expression was calm, and she seemed to be enjoying playing.

After the short but profound piece ended, Cyrille took a breath before greeting.

“I’m Cyrille the Centaur. Pleased to meet you.”

Applause erupted again. This time, while different from the drum set’s, it felt more orthodox.

Then the five of them performed a piece together. It was the song they’d played for us in the recreation room.

Beginning with Sheila’s restrained drum part, different from her earlier performance, everyone’s instruments and singing voices gradually overlapped.

Mystical and grand. Lights evoking a setting sun illuminated the cyclorama. Soon, the curtain of night fell. Shining stars, a floating moon—shooting stars. The stage devices wove a nighttime scene matching the music’s progression.

As discussed during planning… the production matching the music was quite impressive. It was a grand piece worthy of being placed near the end.

Eventually, the song reached its climax—and concluded with Sheila’s drum part, just as it had begun.

The performance ended. The standing audience erupted in thunderous applause. The royal group in the guest seats also stood and applauded. My, my.

Irmhild and the others lined up, holding hands, and bowed to the audience. The curtain descended. The unceasing applause.

There was an encore too. Four pieces performed by the three of them. Then one more including Sheila and Cyrille. This time it was a light, cheerful song that made you want to dance. Apparently, they managed to add one more song through effort. Ending with this piece would likely leave a fun, excited feeling as an afterglow even after leaving the theater.

+++

# **305 – Master of the Airship**

“Oh! Theodore-kun! Everyone!”

When I went to check on the backstage area, I found Irmhild and the others holding hands and celebrating their successful performance. When Irmhild noticed us, she turned a beaming smile our way.

“Yeah. Good work, everyone. That was great.”

“Thank you. Hmm… It was our first time as a group of five, but it felt really good,” said Justia with a radiant smile.

“Sheila, Cyrille, how was it?”

“Mmm. It was fun,” Sheila answered with a small smile when I asked for their impressions.

Sheila was as detached as ever, but with her tail held straight up, it seemed like she was more excited internally than she appeared on the surface.

“It makes me happy when everyone enjoys it.”

“Right.”

Dominique nodded at Cyrille’s words. Watching them, Claudia smiled gently.

“To have the songs I taught performed before everyone… It’s a strange feeling, in a way.”

Well, they were songs passed down from the Labyrinth Village.

“I’d love to hear Claudia-sama perform too.”

When Seraphina said that, Cyrille also nodded.

“I also remember being lulled to sleep by the princess’s songs and instruments when I was little.”

“Um… Yes, that’s right. I couldn’t perform before a large crowd like Irmhild and the others… but if it’s just for all of you, that would be fine.”

Claudia nodded while blushing slightly. Seeing everyone celebrating together was heartwarming, but… since they needed to change clothes and such, I decided to leave the room here and prepare for our move.

After this, we were heading to the hot spring town as planned. We would move to the Fire Spirit Hot Spring with almost all the people we invited today, relax there for a while, and then have discussions with King Melvin, King Eberhart, and the others.

Father and the others, and Marquis Zilbolt, weren’t participating in the meeting, but they were invited to the hot spring town.

By the time we split up and headed to the hot spring town by carriage, the sun had completely set. The hot spring town… from what I could see from the carriage, construction of shops and such seemed to have started in various places. As for the therapeutic baths, they were already functional.

Arriving at the Fire Spirit Hot Spring, a wonderful aroma wafted through the air. Just like during the hot spring town’s unveiling, chefs had come from the Royal Castle to prepare dinner for everyone.

It seemed they wanted everyone to be able to eat at their own pace, just like last time.

“Theo… I heard you built this entire district… that outer wall too?”

Right after getting off the carriage in front of the entrance, Father asked.

“Yes. Although when I say the entire district, it’s only some of the buildings. The therapeutic baths and ritual hall located further away, then the outer wall… and after that, just the sewage system maintenance, I suppose.”

“…Wouldn’t you say that’s almost everything?”

Daryl shook his head.

“…Hmm. The theater and that performance’s production—no, I should have known since you worked on the mansion’s basement…”

Father groaned. Kathryn’s eyes were wide, and Daryl was smiling with a distant look in his eyes.

“…After showing us such a magnificent thing at the theater, and now this on top of it.”

“I wonder what we’ll find inside.”

Old Sigmund and Valentina also wore somewhat strained smiles.

“The Fire Spirit Hot Spring has many attractions too.”

“Hmm. Shall we go around together, Steph?”

“That sounds good. But we have a meeting later, so shall we come together another day?”

“Yes. Rather than rushing through it, I prefer taking our time to fully enjoy it too.”

So said Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana. That the two were so enthusiastic… was somewhat expected. From a little distance away, Rosemary watched them while hiding her mouth behind a feather fan, her expression indescribable.

Marlene seemed happily amused by Princess Stephania’s heightened excitement.

“Now then, a few explanations.”

First, I had everyone enter and conveyed several precautions about the Fire Spirit Hot Spring. Just things like the location of the changing rooms, how to use the bath robes, and explanations about the slider and sauna.

“With that, my explanations are finished.”

After I finished explaining, Grace spoke to me.

“Then, we’ll go take a bath too.”

“Yeah. Okay, let’s meet in the rest area after we’re done.”

“Yes.”

Grace nodded quietly.

“Camilla-sama, I’ll guide you.”

“Thank you, Ashley-sama.”

It seemed Ashley would be guiding Camilla too.

“Okay Camilla, see you later.”

“Yes, Elliot.”

We split into men and women heading to the changing rooms. Elliot and Camilla waved at each other with smiles as they parted.

Well then. I’ll take it easy until the discussions begin.

“Haaah…”

I sank into the large bath’s tub up to my shoulders and let out a breath. It warmed me to my core perfectly.

Everyone… seemed to be enjoying the Fire Spirit Hot Spring in their own ways. Daryl also appeared to have been tense the whole time amidst the kings, lords, and royalty, but he finally seemed to catch his breath in the tub, looking like he’d come back to life.

That said, Albert and Elliot were with him now. As for Albert, even though he’s a prince, he’s an easygoing person, and perhaps because Daryl understood that and they were close in age, he seemed able to relax to some extent.

“Oh ho. So this bubble bath Magic Tool can be purchased?”

“Well, if it’s Silvatoria, making the same thing shouldn’t be difficult.”

“No, no. For things like this, one should show respect to the pioneer. I’d definitely like to purchase it.”

King Melvin and King Eberhart exchanged such conversation in the jacuzzi-style bath. Albert wore a wry smile. It seemed the Labyrinth Trading Company would prosper too, which was fine.

“This hot water seems to have a strange Magical Power,” said Elliot.

“It seems to be the same as the hot water from Mt. Tephra. It appears to have various effects.”

“I see. So you built therapeutic baths too. This does indeed seem effective.”

“I often use the hot spring at the ritual hall. Even if I push myself a bit, the fatigue doesn’t linger.”

Albert smiled. …Yeah. I do feel somewhat responsible for that.

“Hmm. This is good.”

“The fatigue is fading.”

Old Sigmund returned to us with Father, rubbing his shoulders. It seemed they had gone to the waterfall bath.

“Oh, Theodore. We’re enjoying ourselves.”

“I’m glad you like it.”

The two sank into the tub. The three generations of father and son bathing together gave me a strange feeling. I decided to enjoy the bath while looking up at the full moon visible through the large bath’s window.

After a while, King Melvin and King Eberhart moved from the jacuzzi over to us.

“Theodore. Albert. Do you have a moment?”

“What is it?”

“Yes. After we get out of the bath, we’ll have our discussion, but before that, we thought we’d tell you what we can.”

“Understood. Then…”

With Old Sigmund joining us, the five of us moved to a spot slightly away from everyone else.

“What did you want to discuss?”

“Yes. It’s about your reward.”

“In other words… considering your achievements, we thought it would be best to give you the airship after providing full support for its development, and let you use it freely at your discretion.”

“What?”

Old Sigmund’s eyes widened. Albert put his hand to his chin and made a thoughtful gesture.

…The airship as a reward. That’s quite an extravagant story.

I had been told I could handle the airship’s development at my discretion, but indeed, how the completed airship would be positioned and handled hadn’t been decided yet.

“However, even though we call it a reward, we’re also thinking about the Demons. Even though we have Teleportation Magic, since its destinations are limited to temples of a certain scale, your mobility is what’s most important.”

“If there’s distance from the teleportation point to the actual site, using an airship would be easier than consuming Vitality or Magical Power,” said Albert.

“And if there are injured people or important individuals who need rescue, having an airship would make it easier to handle… that’s also a factor, right?”

“Indeed. That’s correct.”

“Understood. I’ll take custody of the airship and do my utmost to meet your expectations.”

“Yes. We’re counting on you to create something amazing that will serve as the foundation for airships built in later generations.”

King Melvin grinned, showing his teeth.

Hmm. Airship development, huh. Even if we proceed with the airship we previously discussed for Demon combat… if the purpose changes to things like transportation between cities, naturally the Materials and Equipment would need to change too.

If it’s to serve as the foundation for airships built later… besides the one we’re currently trying to build, I should also develop ideas for airships focused on other uses to some extent. After all, we’re gathering considerable technical power and resources… so there’s definitely some cost disregard happening, no matter how you look at it.

# **306 – Hot Spring Conference**

Though there was still time before the conference, I had been away in Silvatoria for a while. I decided to get out of the bath a bit early and do some equipment inspections.

Safety inspections around the drainage outlets were important. I checked the drainage outlets in the pool. Once I verified the magic tools were functioning properly, the inspection would be complete.

As I was moving around checking various areas and conducting a safety inspection of the small pool at the end of the water slide, Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana came sliding down together with a splash.

They probably also decided to get out of the bath early to look around the pool.

“Ah, that was fun!”

“It’s designed so you can safely turn even without slowing down.”

“It’s all calculated, isn’t it? Now that I know, for the third time I’ll—”

The two surfaced with laughter.

“Oh, my?”

Princess Stephania seemed slightly surprised to see me there, covering her mouth.

“Mmm, mmm. Good evening, Sir Theodore. Were you sliding too?”

Princess Adriana also cleared her throat softly before asking that.

“No. I was inspecting the equipment. Since we left for Silvatoria shortly after creating the Fire Spirit Hot Spring, I wanted to check on things.”

“I see. That’s good, being thorough with your work.”

“Thank you. I’m glad to see you’re enjoying yourselves.”

When I answered, Princess Adriana also smiled wryly and nodded.

“You probably heard us, but… is it really okay not to slow down?”

It seemed this was their second time on the slide. Having gotten more used to it than the first time, they probably tried increasing their speed.

“It’s fine. We tested it with Aqua Golems of various builds sliding down and accelerating, and adjusted it so they wouldn’t fly out.”

“So it really is calculated.”

Princess Stephania nodded admiringly.

“Well then, Steph. Shall we race next time?”

“Sounds good. I accept your challenge.”

The two seemed to be having quite a good time. With them switching gears properly like this, I didn’t think they’d be late for the conference or end up cutting into dinner time because they were running late—or so I hoped.

“Theodore”

After finishing the pool inspection, I went to check on the rest area, and on the way met Sheila and the others with Marlene.

“Ah. Are you out of the bath?”

“We are. Since there’s still some time, we thought we’d take Marlene-sama to play with Justia and Dominique.”

Irmhild said this while pointing at the lazy river pool.

I gently stroked Marlene’s hair. Playing with everyone… Marlene was smiling happily.

“I’ll release my Humanization Technique and swim with her on my back.”

Said Justia. Marlene smiled happily.

“I see. Well, Marlene, go play. I said I’d wait at the rest area, so I’ll head over there for now. Having Caduceus deliver a message would be a bit…”

When I said this and stroked Marlene’s hair, she nodded.

“I’ll let you know if we go for dinner.”

“Understood.”

“We’ll wrap things up then too.”

“Ah, Theo”

While resting in the rest area, it seemed Grace and the others had also gotten out of the bath.

Slightly damp hair, the faint scent of soap tickling the nostrils, and skin tinged with redness.

There’s something uniquely appealing about people fresh from the bath, or so one might say.

“How was the bath over there?”

“It was lovely. I didn’t notice any particular issues.”

Ashley smiled. Yeah. Even with bath robes, since the men’s and women’s baths are separate, I couldn’t exactly go around inspecting them openly.

“This hot spring really is wonderful. It makes my skin glow.”

Rosemary said while lightly stroking her white arm, and the other women nodded in agreement.

“What shall we do about dinner?”

“Hmm. Well, if we go, I’ll call Sheila and the others too. What about you, Camilla-san?”

Since Camilla is with us too, it would be a bit rude to go ahead without her.

Camilla probably wants to have dinner with Elliot.

“I think I’ll wait for Elliot and Father.”

“Understood. Then shall we wait a bit too? Elliot-san and Donato-san seemed to be in the steam bath together. I don’t think they’ll stay in too long, so they should be out soon.”

“Is that so? Thank you.”

Saying this, Camilla bowed slightly.

We went to check the poolside a bit, had dinner, and then proceeded to the conference.

Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana were also conference participants. They properly wrapped up their pool play and returned to have dinner.

Well, they seemed to be thoroughly enjoying themselves, floating along the lazy river pool with Marlene, Sheila, Irmhild and the others…

But anyway.

“Well then, Theo.”

“Yes, Father.”

Those not attending the conference would return after eating dinner, so I went to see off Father and the others from Marquis Zilbolt’s household at the entrance.

“Lord Siegmund. My apologies for the haste.”

“Not at all. You have your duties as a lord. I understand you can’t take it easy.”

Father and Old Sigmund exchanged words like that. Father planned to return to his territory tomorrow with Kennel via dragon palanquin.

“I’ll also visit Gartner County and the Barony of Silun.”

Old Sigmund and Valentina wanted to visit Mother’s grave. There was also the consideration of increasing the locations where Claudia could teleport to in case of emergency.

“Hmm… I’ll be waiting, Theo.”

“Well then, see you later. Theodore.”

“Yeah, see you.”

Daryl said this while boarding the carriage.

“Thank you for your hospitality during our stay.”

Kathryn also bowed deeply and boarded the carriage—and so Father and the others returned to the villa.

“Then, we shall return to our lodgings.”

“Thank you for today.”

“Yes. Please be careful on your way.”

Marquis Zilbolt and Lady Belinda.

“Then, see you at the academy.”

“Yes, Ashley-sama. Well then, Theodore-sama.”

Ashley and Romina also exchanged words.

“Yes. Lady Romina.”

Marquis Zilbolt also returned to his lodgings, protected by his intelligence unit escort.

Once the carriages had departed, the night-time hot spring town was quite quiet, partly because the townscape wasn’t completed yet.

This place too would eventually become bustling with people even at night. Such aimless thoughts crossed my mind… but well, there was no point thinking about it.

Then let’s head to the conference.

We all went together back to the Fire Spirit Hot Spring rest area. The location was the terrace seating of the rest area. The reason was that you could see the blue-lit pool, making for a nice night view.

Here we were all gathered for the conference. When Old Sigmund and I took our seats, King Eberhart smiled.

“Holding a conference in a place like this is quite tasteful.”

“Indeed.”

In response to King Eberhart’s comment, King Melvin narrowed his eyes while looking at the glowing pool.

Conference attendees included me and my party members, members of the Verdgar and Silvatoria royal families, the two from the Sages’ Academy, and Elliot too.

Tephra and Seraphina, along with Camilla’s family, were playing billiards and darts in the game room on the other side of the rest area with Justia and Dominique. Since the discussion about Elliot concerned Camilla’s family too, we had them stay rather than leave. Justia and Dominique also ended up staying at our house tonight.

“Then—shall we begin the conference?”

There were several topics. Well then.

“First, regarding Verdgar and Silvatoria… we’ve reached agreement with Eberhart to recognize the demons as enemies and to coordinate and cooperate with each other.”

“Hmm. Regarding technical cooperation, Silvatoria will provide airships, and Verdgar will provide aerial combat gear.”

Said the two kings. This part seemed to be going as planned.

“Then regarding that, I’ll complete the full set of magic tools.”

Said Albert. The aerial combat gear set would be delivered to Silvatoria, and they would produce it there. Well, it would probably be best to demonstrate how to use it.

“Hmm. Then we’ll leave that to you. Regarding the airships, we’ve already discussed it with Theodore and agreed to entrust their operation to Theodore. Next—we must discuss the matter of the Moon Goddess.”

It must be about Claudia. When King Melvin looked at her, Claudia closed her eyes and nodded quietly.

Old Sigmund stroked his beard, showing a thoughtful expression. About the relationship between the Moon Goddess and Claudia… he probably suspected there was something, but he hadn’t asked about it.

Since Claudia’s every mannerism was that of the upper class, Princess Adriana also seemed endlessly interested.

“…Theodore kept it hidden as something deeply connected to our country… but since our country has also become deeply involved with Silvatoria’s internal affairs, we too must reveal our internal situation if we’re to build trust. If we’re to form an alliance against the demons and walk together, we must share this information even more.”

“King Melvin. From there, I will explain.”

“…Is that acceptable?”

“Yes.”

Saying this, Claudia stood up. Since King Melvin used honorifics toward Claudia, those unaware of the circumstances seemed slightly surprised—but their eyes went completely round at her next words.

“I am Claudia Shuastrus. Administrator of the Boundary Labyrinth, and a moon royal who descended to the surface long ago… Well, some call me the Moon Goddess, Shuus.”

# **307 – The New Knight**

“…This isn’t… metaphorical, is it?”

King Eberhart showed a surprised expression, but then seemed to recall something and his expression turned serious.

“Indeed, considering that powerful blessing, this does make sense.”

“Everything I’ve told you is the complete truth. I guarantee its veracity upon my name as King of Verdgar.”

King Melvin responded to King Eberhart’s words.

Everyone seemed to be experiencing varying degrees of confusion. A brief silence fell, which was broken by Old Sigmund.

“So that’s why… that extraordinary teleportation magic, something unimaginable under normal circumstances… It’s not something to be spoken of lightly.”

“Yes. That’s why that magic isn’t solely my power. I also borrow the labyrinth’s power and the strength of everyone praying at the temple.”

Claudia spoke in her usual tone.

Indeed. Precisely because the Sages’ Academy possessing teleportation magic is on Silvatoria’s side, we cannot leave these doubts unaddressed. Whether it’s teleportation using the Moon Temple or anything else, it’s necessary during emergencies. We want to avoid the foolishness of coordination gaps arising from distrust.

“…I knew you were no ordinary person, but… this is…”

“Indeed, even when fighting the Black Knights, the miasma didn’t affect you at all.”

Princess Adriana and Elliot showed astonished expressions.

“Um. Claudia-sama is Theodore-kun’s fiancée, correct? Which means…”

At Valentina’s words, Old Sigmund’s expression twitched.

“That would make him the goddess’s husband. I thought I was beyond surprise, but now I’m truly speechless.”

“…That’s the situation. Regarding the labyrinth, there are aspects we cannot handle directly. That’s where Theodore bridges the gap for us. I believe you now understand both the labyrinth’s importance and Theodore’s position in our country.”

King Eberhart nodded as if satisfied with King Melvin’s words.

“…I see. I understand the importance. With that said… there’s something I’d like to request of Theodore-dono.”

“If it’s something I can do.”

“Indeed. This would be an ongoing request. Would you be willing to perform the purification of the miasma that the Silvatoria king receives through the ritual? Of course, I promise we’ll prepare adequate compensation.”

Given that currently no one else can use circulating ki, I had anticipated this request. Part of conveying Claudia’s importance was likely to communicate my position in Verdgar and gain understanding from King Eberhart and Old Sigmund.

Just as Elliot returned to Verdgar, there might have been considerations about me, as a direct descendant of the seven families, being on Silvatoria’s side.

“I humbly accept.”

There’s no reason to refuse this. A prompt agreement should be fine.

“Oh! You’ll do it? My thanks!”

“I’ve heard that users of magical power circulation have their bodies revitalized, making them resistant to aging and able to maintain their youthfulness indefinitely. This should ensure the Silvatoria king’s wellbeing for several generations.”

Said Old Sigmund. …Is that so? I wasn’t aware of the long-term effects of magical power circulation.

“Indeed. That’s reassuring. And one more thing—this isn’t for immediately, but since it concerns you as well, I’d like you to consider it.”

King Eberhart said this and looked toward Old Sigmund.

“Hmm… This is about the Wilcloud family, I presume?”

“Indeed.”

The two nodded to each other. Old Sigmund then took over the explanation.

“With Patricia gone, we have the problem of the Wilcloud family having no successor…”

“The Wilcloud family’s succession issue?”

“Indeed. However, the family headship isn’t an immediate concern. Though I’m of advanced age, we’ve discussed and finalized with the other six families the plan to adopt Valentina into the Wilcloud family as the next head.”

Valentina bowed in response to Old Sigmund’s words.

I see. Since the seven sage families are also related, even if not direct descendants, adopting someone as a temporary head makes sense.

This ensures the Wilcloud family won’t die out for the foreseeable future, regardless of what I decide to do. But the head family of the seven families having no direct descendant… that must indeed be problematic.

Which brings us to the discussion about me.

“We understand that given Theodore’s position, he cannot leave Verdgar. With that in mind, if we may express our hope, we’d like to eventually welcome a direct descendant of yours as the Wilcloud family head…”

“I see… That’s certainly not something too early to discuss.”

This involves not just me, but the future of my children as well.

“…Indeed. We don’t want to force someone unwilling, nor separate young children from their parents just because they’re successors. Of course, if they have the will and talent, we couldn’t ask for more.”

…That’s true. Considering the nature of the Sages’ Academy, not just any direct descendant will do. While it’s a long-term matter, we need to start thinking about it now.

The premise is having someone who properly understands and is determined to correctly inherit the ancient policies and values of the Wilcloud family and the other six families. If they also have the talent to use magical power circulation, that would be ideal…

And of course, that naturally involves education from the early stages. No one can predict who will have aptitude.

“Understood. I’ll consider it.”

“My apologies for having to bring this up with you now. It shows our inadequacy…”

“Not at all. This also concerns my mother’s family home.”

“I appreciate you saying that.”

So, that should cover matters regarding me?

“Indeed… I’m glad we’ve reached understanding. Next—”

King Melvin turned his gaze toward Elliot.

“Elliot. This concerns you.”

“I’m listening.”

As Elliot straightened his posture, King Melvin nodded.

“Indeed. Actually, after discussions with Eberhart, we’ve decided to form a joint operational unit against demons from both Verdgar and Silvatoria to assist Theodore. They’ll undergo training assuming combat against demons, including aerial battles. I want to appoint you as that unit’s commander.”

“Me, sir?”

“Exactly. I’ve heard you have experience leading soldiers in monster extermination within Silvatoria. Additionally, this decision considers your capabilities, connections in both countries, and familiarity with Theodore’s circumstances.”

“From Silvatoria’s side, it’s already been decided that Elmer and others from Marquis Zilbolt’s subordinates will be assigned.”

“Indeed. After you’ve achieved merits, I plan to raise the Silun barony’s rank and grant Elliot territory in the north. With this promise, even if someone emerges later to support Elliot, it shouldn’t cause confusion in the Silun barony.”

Hmm. …For example, if Ashley’s rank were raised to viscount or count. Then Ashley, as the head, could transfer the original baron rank of the Silun family to Elliot. Since ranks come with territories, he could eventually govern the north.

The aim is likely to create that path by having him achieve merits as the operational unit leader and gain accomplishments worthy of nobility.

From King Melvin’s perspective, he can establish a noble close to the Verdgar royal family as a northern lord… And even if supporters of Elliot emerge in the Silun barony, since he’s promised to become a lord eventually, there’s no reason to cause trouble. They’ve really thought this through.

Elliot’s eyes widened, but he bowed deeply.

“Though lacking in talent, I will devote my full efforts.”

“Indeed. Then as of today, your status is under my direct command. I’ll contact the unit members separately, but officially from this moment, you’re now my personal knight. You may inform Donato and the others accordingly. If necessary, I’ll arrange for a residence in Termwills as well.”

“Yes! I’m deeply grateful for your repeated consideration!”

Elliot responded with the courtesy of a subordinate. Well, this should settle matters regarding the Silun barony.

Actually, regarding Elliot and Camilla, it seems like they might proceed all the way to marriage. His previously uncertain status is now confirmed, and with the concerns removed, there’s no reason not to.

+++

#  **308 – Models and Aerial Maneuvers**

—The hot spring meeting had concluded, and a new day dawned.

“Good morning, Cecilia.”

“Good morning, Master.”

We gathered in the dining hall to see everyone. The current residents were Old Sigmund and Valentina, Elliot and Camilla’s family, plus Justia and Dominique.

“Good morning, Elliot-san, Camilla-san.”

“Yes. Good morning.”

Elliot and Camilla entered the dining hall together. With Elliot escorting Camilla by holding her hand, they gave off the atmosphere of a couple who would likely become quite lovey-dovey.

…Well then. Since various matters were settled last night, things will probably start moving in different directions.

Especially for Elliot, who will become the captain of the newly established unit—both in terms of work and his personal life, as discussions about marriage seem to be progressing, so he’ll likely be quite busy.

Once everyone had gathered, I asked Elliot during breakfast.

“By the way, it seemed like His Majesty Melvin had something else to say to you after that.”

“Yes. While there’s the matter of establishing the new unit, first regarding marriage, it looks like we’ll be searching for a new home.”

I see. Since he’ll be independent, he probably can’t continue living at my place.

“How about asking Rosetta-sensei to mediate finding a new home?”

Ashley suggested.

“Rosetta-sensei… was she the one who taught Ashley healing magic?”

“Yes. When Grace and I first came to Termwills, she helped us too. This house—though it’s been remodeled now—was originally mediated by Rosetta-san as well. If needed, I can contact her via the communication device.”

“Then—I’ll take you up on that offer. Thank you.”

Saying this, Elliot smiled gently and bowed slightly.

Hmm. He doesn’t seem too concerned about financial matters, but Elliot was quite well-known as a magic knight in Silvatoria, and becoming a knight directly under the king likely means he has some leeway.

When I contacted Rosetta via the communication device, she replied that she had no lectures today and was free. Well then… I’ll tell Elliot where Rosetta’s house is located.

“We’re planning to go to the workshop and conduct experiments.”

“Understood. Once things are settled and I have time, I’ll stop by.”

“Yes.”

After nodding back to Elliot, I turned my gaze to Justia and Dominique.

“What about you two? I can take you back when returning to the Guild.”

“Sounds interesting. Can we come watch?”

“Yeah. We want to see.”

“Then that’s fine with me.”

Today we planned to create a model airship in the workshop and conduct experiments. Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana had also expressed interest in observing.

“Hmm. The appearance will probably be something like this.”

When I created a scaled model of the airship and made it float in the workshop’s courtyard, Marlene applauded for me. Yeah. She had a happy expression. Maybe she remembered the paper airplane from before.

“Will that become the same shape as the completed version?”

“That’s the plan. Though we still need to make adjustments from here.”

When I answered Valentina’s question, she nodded with interest.

We brought out desks and arranged chairs in the courtyard, proceeding with adjustment work while everyone watched.

“Hmm. Perhaps because the sails are gone, it has changed quite significantly from existing ship forms.”

Old Sigmund offered his impressions after seeing it.

“It doesn’t feel much like a ship… but isn’t that good?”

“With the same material as that Golem, it will be a white ship. With some decoration, it will surely become elegant.”

Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana were analyzing it.

To reduce air resistance, the overall silhouette is streamlined. Main wings on both sides, tail wings at the rear of the hull. And two magical propulsion units equipped at the stern.

Since sails aren’t needed, the top is clean. Instead, we included a bridge section so that crew members wouldn’t fall off even during some degree of aerial maneuvers. Though it’s called a bridge, it doesn’t protrude that much, but it should provide defense for the crew from pressure changes during rapid ascent or descent, as well as the cold at high altitudes.

Except for the view from the cockpit, we plan to use the vision of magical creatures to grasp the entire surroundings. This vision through magical creatures is also planned to be applied for aiming the rotating cannons installed throughout the hull.

The crew won’t expose themselves at all from inside the ship, instead using the vision of magical creatures to detect enemy appearances and positions, then intercept approaching opponents.

We want to thoroughly check the movable range of the rotating cannons and eliminate blind spots.

I tilted my teacup to empty it, then took a breath. After that, I lightly slapped both my cheeks to psych myself up.

“Alright. Shall we try flying it? I’ll need to concentrate a bit.”

When I said this, everyone’s gaze focused on the model. The three girls—Irmhild, who had been playing music as a substitute for BGM, along with Justia and Dominique—stopped their performance to create an environment where I could concentrate.

As everyone watched with bated breath, I used both Levitation and Wind Magic to simulate the forces experienced during flight. During this, I made adjustments to any parts that concerned me.

I floated and supported the model here, adding adjustments while intuitively checking what kind of load would occur with various behaviors. The actual thing will be dozens of times larger. The required force—both for flying and floating—will be that much greater. Since we’re doing this with a model, I need to concentrate intensely to perceive the minute loads.

While flying it, I adjusted the shape of the main wings several times. I repeatedly made fine adjustments to maximize lift when moving forward.

Stability during flight. What about air resistance? How much will the ship tilt when turning? Where on the ship will large loads occur? The strength of areas receiving loads.

I checked each of these one by one, and whenever something concerned me, I repeatedly made corrections and fine adjustments to the hull structure and magic output balance. Fixing one place sometimes affected the whole, making it quite troublesome.

Five, six, seven, eight. After flying it for a while while deploying multiple Magic Circles in layers, the unreasonable parts gradually decreased, and I also got the hang of operating the model.

“Shall I try changing the behavior a bit?”

Though not originally planned, it seems possible to perform somewhat unique aerial maneuvers even with the power currently equipped on the airship. It would probably be good to get accustomed to behaviors for evasion too.

Rapid ascent while turning, vertical rotation from ascent, diving into inverted flight, rolling. While finely adjusting Wind Magic, I investigated how much strain was possible and what kind of load would be placed on the crew inside.

Finally, I made the airship model, which had made a large turn, float above my palm and stop. …Hmm. Is this about right?

“…Are you planning to do that with people aboard?”

Alfred was the one who asked. His smile seemed slightly strained. Old Sigmund and Valentina too. Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana… on the contrary, they looked somewhat happy.

“…No, that’s not the plan. It was more about… well, experimenting to see what movements are possible just by operating the output of the magic tools.”

“Meaning—if Theodore is piloting, similar movements would be possible with the actual ship too, right?”

Rosemary asked while hiding her mouth with her feather fan. Rosemary seemed to be enjoying this.

“Hmm. That would be… probably.”

Since I’ll be documenting what I learned from this as a Spell Formula… it will probably be like that.

“If Theo is piloting, shouldn’t we feel at ease?”

“…That’s right, probably. Though it looked reckless, it should be fine.”

When Grace said this, Claudia nodded, and Ashley smiled. Well, yeah… It makes me happy to be trusted, but… Ah. The G-forces on the crew could be mitigated by Levitation Magic Tools each possesses.

In any case, to ensure safety upon safety, we’ll need to conduct many more experiments.

“For now, I’m planning to fix the chairs inside the ship to the floor. And attach belts to those chairs too, so bodies won’t be thrown from them.”

“That’s reassuring.”

“Otherwise, we’d bump our bodies inside the ship.”

In other words, seat belts. Sheila nodded, and Irmhild gave a wry smile.

“What about me?”

Seraphina asked.

“I’ll make special seats for Seraphina, Lavigne, and Eclair too. Since the ship is under my care, I can manage that much flexibility.”

“Yay!”

Seraphina happily spread both arms and danced around. I could see she was subtly trying to imitate the aerial maneuvers from earlier.

Regarding the airship’s materials, I heard arrangements are currently progressing rapidly. Since I’ve already been taught the Spell Formulas for processing the hull, once the required amount is gathered, we plan to start by making the framework and exterior.

After the exterior is done, next is the interior. The core floating device, external monitoring system via magical creatures, anti-demon weaponry, wings, propulsion units. These magic tools will be incorporated in order.

We’ll proceed with labyrinth exploration, airship construction, and new unit training in parallel… and once these take shape to some extent, we’ll probably head out to investigate Beriondora.

+++

# **309 – Report from the Magic Kingdom**

With the warm reception from the Silvatoria royal family and the discussions at the hot springs concluded, King Eberhart was scheduled to return to Silvatoria.

Marquis Zilbolt, who had been invited to the theater, also couldn’t stay long and was preparing to return to his territory.

We too had business in Vinesdora and wanted to hear further updates. First, we would be seeing off Marquis Zilbolt and Lady Belinda. Since we were sending off Marquis Zilbolt, it would be at the ceremonial grounds, where the three members of the Marquis’s family and his Intelligence Unit would gather at the meeting point.

“You’ve gone through a lot for this.”

“Not at all. We intend to give our all to avoid tarnishing the Marquis’s honor.”

“Compared to the work Zadias brought us, this is such rewarding duty.”

“Indeed.”

With these words, Marquis Zilbolt and his Intelligence Unit members—Elmer, Donovan, and Lionel—shared a laugh.

Regarding the newly established unit, Elmer, Donovan, Lionel, and several others would remain in Termwills under Elliot’s command.

From our perspective, we had merely invited them and hadn’t intended for this outcome… but according to King Eberhart, Marquis Zilbolt’s visit to Termwills happened to be perfect timing for discussing the matter. The three—Elmer and the others—had apparently volunteered, saying it was a way to repay their debt to the Marquis and to us.

“But aren’t they key members of your Intelligence Unit? Will that be alright?”

“Indeed, they are… but for now, matters related to the demons should take priority over the relatively settled domestic issues in Silvatoria. Well, as long as things remain calm in my territory, we have enough personnel.”

“…I see.”

The Marquis’s domain seemed well-staffed, from the Knight Order Commander to the head magician.

Marquis Zilbolt gave a quiet bow before exchanging words with Romina as well.

“We who remain in Termwills will protect the Young Lady with our lives.”

“Good. I’m counting on you.”

“Thank you, Elmer.”

Both Marquis Zilbolt and Romina smiled wryly. This was Romina’s first time leaving her parents’ side, after all. Having three Intelligence Unit members staying behind with her would likely ease her anxiety.

“Shall we go, then?”

After finishing the farewell greetings, prompted by Claudia, we teleported to Marquis Zilbolt’s territory.

After seeing Marquis Zilbolt and Lady Belinda off to their territory, we next met up with King Eberhart at the royal castle before teleporting to Vinesdora. Enveloped in light, when we opened our eyes, we were already above Vinesdora’s Moon Temple.

As we floated gently down to the ground from our slightly elevated position, the clerics and shrine maidens stared wide-eyed at King Eberhart’s sudden visit.

Our companions were our Party Members: King Eberhart and his knight escort; Old Sigmund and Valentina. Princess Adriana was to remain in Termwills as King Eberhart’s representative.

“…Long-distance teleportation… is truly convenient.”

“Indeed. We are fortunate that this is made possible through the goddess’s power and will.”

When Old Sigmund shared his thoughts, King Eberhart responded with a wry smile.

The magic wielded through Claudia’s will, and the contract the Verdgar royal family had with the labyrinth, meant that even with succession changes, there were aspects requiring restraint.

Though it was unclear how much time Claudia had spent in the labyrinth, it could be said she was trusted precisely because she had consistently desired peace up to this day.

“Your Majesty Eberhart… what is this…?”

“Hmm. My apologies for the disturbance. As I mentioned before, this is new magic made possible by borrowing power from the temple and the goddess Shuath.”

“I, I see…”

King Eberhart assured the gathering shrine maidens that there was no problem.

“I, I see… So this is what the dream revelation was showing us.”

The Head Shrine Maiden and head cleric had apparently received a revelation from Claudia beforehand. Though slightly bewildered, they seemed to accept it. When their eyes met Claudia’s, they smiled.

“According to Your Majesty’s will and the guidance of Goddess Shuath.”

Saying this, the Head Shrine Maiden and others knelt. The Moon Temple side seemed fine. We then all headed to Vinesdora’s royal castle.

Old Sigmund and Valentina had business picking up materials and documents at the Sages’ Academy, but first they needed to check if there had been any changes during their absence and confirm security.

“Your Majesty…! You’ve returned!”

Upon arriving at the royal castle, King Eberhart’s aides came to greet him.

“Yes. Report on matters during my absence.”

Walking through the corridors of Vinesdora’s royal castle, King Eberhart and his aide continued their conversation as we listened.

“Yes! First, regarding domestic affairs—although there was some confusion following Zadias’s downfall, things have relatively stabilized. Most of the nobles seem to be taking a wait-and-see approach.”

“Hmm. No one tried to commit seppuku out of loyalty to Zadias?”

King Eberhart spoke ironically with a wry smile.

“Those close to Zadias seem to be trembling, afraid that sparks might reach them.”

“For such people, if they show submission, even passively, that should suffice. A few warning words and instructing them to continue contributing to the kingdom’s development should be enough deterrent. However, maintain a certain level of vigilance.”

“As you command.”

“People connected only by interests… that’s just how they are, but… if you pressure them too much, they might bare their fangs. If they don’t actively oppose us even with minor issues, leaving them be might be best in the current situation.”

Rosemary, who had been listening to the conversation, murmured this while hiding her mouth behind her feather fan.

Hmm. Even if some nobles in Silvatoria had cooperated with Zadias to some extent, eliminating them now would cause more practical harm. Aftermath handling is often more troublesome anyway.

With Zadias’s own messes still needing cleanup and demon-related matters unresolved, the approach was to issue warnings while simultaneously hinting at their necessity to the kingdom, thereby reducing hostility. Using both carrot and stick appropriately—if they weren’t extremely dissatisfied with the status quo, they’d likely stay quiet.

Receiving reports and giving instructions, we were led deeper into the castle to a guest room. Tea was promptly served.

“Anything else unusual?”

When King Eberhart asked, his aide’s expression darkened slightly.

“…Actually, one item from the treasure room was taken out by Zadias.”

“…And that is?”

“Something called the Ancient Key.”

“A key, you say?”

King Eberhart also seemed unfamiliar with it, his expression clouding.

“According to the inventory, it’s an item passed down since before Silvatoria’s founding.”

“…That would be right. If it’s called ‘ancient’ in Silvatoria, it must be an artifact from Beriondora. Its purpose, intended use, and current whereabouts?”

“Regarding its purpose… it’s recorded as ‘an item the royal family should manage.'”

“That… was left as an obligation by a past king, I presume?”

Only a royal ancestor could leave such a duty for the royal family.

“That is the assumption. Regarding why he took it, Zadias said it was for a trade to obtain the demon’s secret techniques. As for its whereabouts, he claims not to know.”

“…How utterly… shoddy and irresponsible. Used in a trade with demons, and the key’s location unknown. Their objectives remain unclear too, you say?”

King Eberhart sighed and put a hand to his forehead. Shaking his head, he looked up and told his aide:

“…Continue the investigation and interrogation. Have the relevant inventory brought here.”

“Yes!”

The aide bowed apologetically and left the guest room.

“You heard it. I’d like to hear your opinions, if I may.”

King Eberhart reseated himself in his chair and turned toward us.

Hmm. A key… a key.

“…Thinking straightforwardly from the word ‘key’… it would be used for some door, or perhaps it’s necessary to break some seal.”

“A seal… Should we assume it’s related to the seal of ancient demons?”

That was possible too… but there was something slightly concerning about simply agreeing.

“In Silvatoria, it seems countermeasures and seals against demons are consolidated with the Sages’ Academy.”

“…Indeed. If it were related to the seal of ancient demons, it would fall under our jurisdiction.”

Old Sigmund pondered deeply.

“Can we speak directly with Zadias and Volheim?”

“It’s not impossible, but… at the very least, Zadias might not be able to hold a proper conversation if you go yourself.”

“Why is that? Is he still immobilized by intense pain?”

“No… That’s part of it, but it seems you completely broke his spirit. Every time he’s interrogated, he just trembles at the mere mention of you, screaming not to hand him over, and the session gets interrupted.”

King Eberhart said this as if finding it difficult to say, or perhaps apologetically.

“Is that so…”

…Hmm. Did I break him too much? Considering I crushed any chance of his resurgence, it might not be a bad thing.

# **310 – Inheritance of the Shrine Maiden**

“Right this way. I’ll be right over there, so please call if you need anything.”

“Thank you.”

After thanking the soldier, I peered through the iron bars.

“Y-You!? —Ggh, guuuh!”

The moment our eyes met, Volheim tried to leap up from his crude bed as if repelled. But the wounds he received from our fight probably hadn’t healed due to Miasma Erosion. He seemed to be struck by intense pain, clutching his stomach and writhing.

I’d heard Volheim’s injuries were less severe compared to Zadias, which is why I requested this meeting… but how should I put this? If this is how Volheim is, then it’s probably better not to face Zadias after all. Both he and Zadias seem to have developed trauma regarding me, but this reaction makes it difficult to even exchange greetings.

“I heard that unlike Zadias, you’re capable of some conversation.”

“W-What do you want to talk about…! There’s nothing to discuss…!”

Volheim said this while sweating profusely on his forehead and grimacing. He had dark circles under his eyes. Probably couldn’t sleep properly due to the pain.

I heard both Zadias and Volheim have recovered enough to exchange words, but proper interrogation hasn’t been possible yet. Apparently the damage from their injuries was surprisingly severe, and they can’t handle intensive questioning in their weakened state, so they’re waiting for their injuries and Vitality to recover a bit more. Still, since we’re managing to extract some information like this, I can’t complain.

“What do you know about the Ancient Key that Zadias gave to the demons? Is it correct that the key was used in a Trade with Alvelinde and ended up with the demons in Beriondora?”

“Y-You…”

When I directly confronted him with what we already knew, Volheim’s mouth opened and closed repeatedly. …This reaction.

“Seems like you know something about what Zadias was doing too. I think it would be wiser to talk before the interrogation intensifies.”

When I said this, Volheim made a face like he’d bitten into something bitter, but eventually spoke in a weak voice.

“…I don’t know… the key’s purpose. I just heard it was a key that should be under the Royal Family’s management, so perhaps it’s meant for use in Beriondora’s Royal Castle.”

Hmm. Considering the scale of what they’ve done, they’ll probably be given Magic Potions during the Magical Inquisition as standard procedure. He must understand that staying silent is pointless.

“So you handed it over because Alvelinde requested it, even though you didn’t know its purpose.”

“…W-We needed it to formulaize the Flight Technique those demons use. If we could analyze and reproduce it, we could eventually counter it too. W-We should have surpassed them eventually…!”

…So this was the content of their Trade. Volheim’s excuse in response to my criticism sounded like justification after being exposed.

That said, while Zadias and the demons were in a cooperative relationship… they probably planned to betray and eliminate the demons once cooperation was no longer necessary. We also considered developing counter-techniques from Volheim’s research… but I don’t think they’re opponents we could defeat just by sealing one Flight Technique.

That would be like claiming we could defeat demons just because we can fly. As a researcher, the bait dangled before him must have looked delicious, but his outlook was naive.

“And you dared to say that, even though the key might revive the demon lord or lead to even worse situations?”

“The demon… lord?”

Volheim looked puzzled.

“Didn’t you know this? Either way, it seems certain that Alvelinde’s faction has gathered in Beriondora.”

Everything up to this point was just confirming what we’d already figured out from previous information. For me… there’s one more thing I need to ask.

“—There’s one more thing I want to ask.”

“W-What is it?”

Perhaps sensing the slight change in my tone, Volheim answered with a somewhat higher-pitched voice.

“Where did you get information about Mother?”

Zadias ordered Marquis Zilbolt to investigate Gartner County, where Mother had been. That much is fine. But where did Zadias and his group obtain that information in the first place?

And it was quite incomplete information at that. Since Zadias and the others had been searching for Mother’s whereabouts all along, chronologically speaking, they must have recently learned about it and dispatched the sabotage unit… but in that case, the fact that information about me and Father was missing is concerning.

So, where and how did they obtain the original information? If the Black Knights investigated first and only recently obtained information about Mother… they should have known more about her surroundings.

“Th-That is…”

“Let me say this first. I might let other things slide, but if I judge you’re telling worthless lies about this matter, I won’t show mercy even if you’re injured.”

At my words, Volheim’s eyes widened.

“…Th-That demon woman. She approached us with a Trade offer, saying she had her own information network, so I asked if she knew the Sealing Shrine Maiden’s whereabouts… and she said that shrine maiden should already be dead…”

“—That is”

“I-It’s true. She said the timing when the Sealing Shrine Maiden’s contract was broken matched when a demon called the King of Deathly Slumber rampaged in a region of Verdgar… Th-That’s why…!”

…I see.

I don’t know what position the King of Deathly Slumber holds among Beriondora’s demons, or whether they’re directly connected… but something related to the lord’s Seal must have been affected by Mother’s death.

That’s why Alvelinde and the others had means to remotely learn about Mother’s location and the circumstances.

But according to the information the demons had… they only knew about Mother’s title and her approximate location.

So. How much did the demons know? If the Sealing Shrine Maiden was an obstacle for the demons, and if they had targeted Mother from the beginning… then the King of Deathly Slumber showing off and rampaging would only create disadvantages.

The demons must have learned about Mother after that incident six years ago. That encounter was coincidental—or was it?

…Even if it was, they seized the opportunity presented by the incident six years ago to begin their actions.

“Wh-What are you… smiling about?”

“—You people were lucky.”

If you had sold information about Mother to the demons, and that led to what happened, my response to Zadias and Volheim would have been different.

I’ve asked what I needed to ask, learned what I wanted to know. After glancing at the wide-eyed Volheim, I left the dungeon.

“…That Zadias. Truly never does anything worthwhile.”

When I returned to the VIP room and told everyone what I learned from my conversation with Volheim, King Eberhart shook his head.

“The Sealing Shrine Maiden protects the four directions through a ritual… that’s right, isn’t it?”

Rosemary, who had been listening, furrowed her brows as she spoke.

“This protection of the four directions through the ritual—perhaps we should view it as the same as what Alvelinde calls the contract.”

At Claudia’s words, Grace nodded.

“There are four Miasma Orbs too. If we consider there being four Seals as well… it matches.”

Verdgar is like that, but… information has been lost in Beriondora and Silvatoria too due to battles with demons and the passage of time.

The meaning of placing a Sealing Shrine Maiden. If it’s directly connected to the lord’s Seal…

“I think the contract breaking might have released the Miasma Orbs.”

“That would mean… there’s been no change in the situation around the Seal itself.”

“That’s right. Regarding the Seal alone, it hasn’t worsened according to the information we have. We need to investigate the key further though…”

When I answered, Ashley looked up, met my gaze directly, and nodded.

“We might be on the defensive after the Miasma Orbs were released. But if we can create new Seals… that would give it meaning.”

Regarding the Sealing Shrine Maiden, I heard that the daughter of one of the elders would be newly appointed, and the ritual should have been completed on the night of the recent full moon. Since Vinesdora’s safety was confirmed, Old Sigmund and Valentina went to the Sages’ Academy with Ignis and Lavigne. If any problems arose regarding the shrine maiden, they would probably return immediately.

And speaking of which, it seems both of them have returned. A civil official knocked on the door and said.

“Lord Sigmund and Lady Valentina have returned.”

“Hmm. Show them in.”

When King Eberhart prompted, Old Sigmund and Valentina soon arrived in the VIP room. They were accompanied by another girl… who looked somewhat troubled.

“And who is this?”

“Hmm. Let me introduce her. This is Charlotte Orgran, newly chosen as the Sealing Shrine Maiden.”

“I’m honored to be introduced. My name is Charlotte Orgran.”

The girl bowed. Chronologically, she would be a child born after Mother ran away. She didn’t seem to be among them when I released the memories before.

“Nice to meet you. My name is Theodore Gartner.”

First things first, let’s get the introductions done. Everyone introduced themselves to Charlotte in turn. I introduced Marlene too. Marlene quietly bowed, holding the hem of her skirt.

“Charlotte here was born during our house arrest. Perhaps Volheim and the others thought it unwise to let the elder family’s bloodline die out, so they told us the truth about our relationships before we lost our memories. She’s undoubtedly the genuine young lady of the Orgran family.”

I see.

I heard Volheim and the others were teaching magic to the elder family members, especially the children… and Charlotte apparently directly petitioned that “even if we’ve lost our memories, we’re not criminals, so we should be given more freedom,” which made Volheim and the others regard her as a nuisance.

Apparently she’s been participating in research at the Sages’ Academy until now to remove the memory Seal. In other words, Zadias was exploiting family ties, making even the elder’s daughter with potential cooperate… but judging by this appearance, those two must have earned the children’s resentment too.

Anyway, the elders took their time selecting her. There shouldn’t be any mistake in their choice.

“…But, Grandfather Sigmund. I’m sure I don’t have the talent to be a shrine maiden. The ritual on the night of the recent full moon… ended in Failure.”

…So this is why she looks troubled.

“We returned to tell you all about it. We were supposed to gather materials…”

“It might not be a matter of talent.”

At my words, Charlotte looked at me with surprise.

I told her again what we learned from my exchange with Volheim that I’d just shared with everyone.

“—So then… because the Seal was broken, my contract didn’t work properly?”

“That’s how I see it… but even if maintaining the contract is difficult, I don’t think inheriting the Sealing Technique is meaningless when considering the future. Since the Seal was created once, it should be possible to create it again.”

That’s the skill we’ll need then.

“And if the demons try to interfere, we’ll Smash them with force and carve our path.”

Nothing has changed from before. We just have more reasons to fight them.

When I said this definitively, Charlotte seemed momentarily taken aback, but eventually bowed deeply toward me.

“Please… take care of me. I may be inexperienced, but I’ll do my best too.”

“Likewise.”

Saying this, I shook Charlotte’s hand.

# **311 – The Grudges of the Magicians**

“I look forward to hearing good news then.”

“Yes. I’ll see you again soon.”

“Indeed.”

After being seen off by King Eberhart, we left the royal castle and headed toward the grounds of the Sages’ Academy.

It had been decided that books and materials would be brought to Termwills for deciphering and research. There were apparently various items that could and couldn’t be taken out from the Sages’ Academy, but the academy side would compensate by having the elders continue their work.

In short, while we needed to occasionally come to Silvatoria to hear updates, there was also the purpose of checking whether there were any movements from demons. It was necessary work and shouldn’t be too troublesome.

“Ah, Theodore-kun.”

We showed our faces at the tower within the academy grounds. The members of the seven families were in the process of pulling out various books and documents from the forbidden library and treasure room and lining them up on desks in the grand library.

When we appeared, they stopped their work and gathered around.

“Good day.”

“Well, it’s good you came.”

After greeting the members of the seven families, they each offered words of welcome. They seemed quite pleased that we had shown up.

“We heard you and Lord Siegmund were coming, so we were just bringing out the prepared books from the inner library.”

Let’s see. This was Emil Orgran, one of the heads of the seven families, right?

His appearance was different from when we last met, now sporting a monocle and mustache style. He was Charlotte’s father.

“Thank you.”

“Not at all. This is about all we can do.”

Emil said this with a laugh.

“Father.”

“Charlotte? Is something the matter?”

Charlotte bowed to Emil. Seeing this, Emil’s expression turned serious. Perhaps because Charlotte’s atmosphere had changed from before. Maybe he had some thoughts about Charlotte’s transformation.

“I spoke with Theodore-sama at the castle.”

“Oh?”

“Hmm. We should share the previous discussion with everyone as well.”

Old Siegmund said this while looking at me. I nodded and explained to everyone what I had learned from my conversation with Volheim and about the role of the Sealing Shrine Maiden.

“So that’s why – since the seal has already been broken, the contract might not have been established.”

“I see… It seems we’ve been falling behind.”

“That might be true. However, I’m considering inheriting the sealing technique. While reconstructing the demon’s seal is also a goal, it would definitely be a loss if the technique itself were lost.”

“Is that so. So that’s why Charlotte…”

“Father. May I also head to Termwills, like Grandfather Siegmund and Valentina-sama?”

“…Yes. Go prepare for your journey.”

When Emil nodded, Charlotte left the grand library with a serious expression to gather her belongings.

“I’m sorry to have my daughter under your guidance. You must be busy enough as it is.”

“No. Returning what Mother left to where it originally belongs… is something I should do too.”

“Is that so…”

Emil closed his eyes. Was he remembering my mother?

As if collecting himself, Emil nodded and picked up a book.

“These ancient documents here contain descriptions related to Termwills’ labyrinth. I believe information about seals and barriers will also emerge as deciphering progresses.”

“So they’re secret techniques after all.”

“Indeed. However, in our view, considering the roles that Theodore and his companions will bear in the future, we believe you should be the one to inherit them.”

“As the direct descendant of the Wilcloud family with deep connections to the labyrinth. And as a battle mage who has slain demons. Things related to the labyrinth should be placed in the labyrinth rather than left in our care.”

“…Then… I’ll take custody of them.”

I said this with a bow.

“Good. We’re preparing the items that can be taken out, so please wait here a little longer.”

“Yes.”

Past materials contained spell formulas for using the labyrinth, barrier magic, and sealing techniques. Plus research on Volheim’s miasma techniques. We would take back whatever we could from these and conduct research and deciphering in parallel at both Termwills and Vinesdora.

“While we work, we’d like to hear about your demon-slaying story too.”

The elders smiled.

“That’s right. Come to think of it, we’ve heard that Theodore-kun defeated demons, but we don’t know the details.”

“Ah, indeed. I’m quite curious.”

…So it came to that, and I shared the detailed circumstances of the battle with the demons, also with the intention of sharing information about the orbs and miasma orbs… but…

Starting with Linette, then Blazing Heat, then Dancing Sword – each time a demon’s epithet came up, the elders’ laughter grew drier.

At some point, Irmhild started playing music as if providing BGM, adding realism to the story of the battle with demons. Charlotte, who had finished packing her belongings, returned to the grand library, and before I knew it, it had turned into a recollection session about our battles with demons.

Marlene too, with Seraphina on her shoulder, both listening seriously with earnest nods. Thanks to that, there was plenty of merit in telling the story.

“My, my. A demon who manipulates summoning magic is already quite unusual, but Blazing Heat and Dancing Sword…”

“Unusual… Is that so?”

“Those fellows tend to be overly focused on their own power.”

…Yeah, that might be true. While Linette didn’t possess miasma characteristics… the hole she left behind might be unexpectedly significant for demons.

“Blazing Heat, with its intense heat, made approaching impossible even if you blocked the miasma, and I hear he was a master swordsman even without using heat.”

“Dancing Sword too. They say he sent out countless swords and cut down the subjugation team without moving a single step.”

“To think you managed to defeat such beings… We had thought that to defeat high-ranking demons, you could only create situations where they couldn’t escape with barriers and fight them with numbers, taking turns to wear them down.”

“Indeed. To deploy multiple barriers against heat, and shield deployment in all directions… and still manage to fight. It seems your ability in magical power control is on a completely different dimension from ours.”

The elders nodded as if convinced.

“We’ve also heard you defeated the Corrosion Princess… Are there others?”

“After Dancing Sword came Black Bones.”

When Sheila said this, the elders’ faces stiffened.

“Black… Bones!?”

“Gardinis of the Black Skull! You actually defeated him!?”

What was this? Their reaction seemed slightly different from when we mentioned Blazing Heat and Dancing Sword.

“Yes. He seemed to be the founder of the Duoveris Cult. Is there something about that demon?”

“Something? He’s the direct enemy of our ancestors! This is a great achievement!”

“…I didn’t know that.”

Indeed… he seemed to have combat experience with battle mages and knew how to deal with them. He also spoke as if he had confident information about the loss of teleportation magic… So he had direct karma with the seven families.

“The one who fought him was the head of the Burgmüller family at the time, I believe.”

“Indeed. When retreating from Beriondora, he served as rear guard to let the people escape. There, together with the white wyvern Boldonov, he stopped the pursuit of the Black Skull.”

“So you’ve avenged my ancestor’s enemy!”

The current head of the Burgmüller family said this while patting my shoulder with a beaming smile.

“I’d very much like to hear about your battle with the Black Skull.”

“Well then. First – it started when the Duoveris Cult launched an attack.”

“Ah– So you stole techniques during your fight with him.”

“It’s like a striking method that transmits impact through magic shields and such.”

Saying this, I created a block of ice and delivered a light impact strike through a shield. Then fine cracks appeared in the ice block.

“Oh…”

“This is fascinating.”

The elders looked at the ice block I created with curious expressions.

“…This would be terrifying technology if used by an enemy.”

“No wonder the Black Skull was notorious as a magician killer.”

Valentina, who had returned after packing her bag, and Charlotte nodded in agreement.

“–Well, that was an interesting story.”

“But what concerns me are the words Gardinis left behind.”

“‘The first one as an ancient demon.’ That ‘youngster’ part is concerning.”

“Perhaps their leader? I hear the Black Skull was fixated on his achievements. For such a demon to mention someone alongside ancient demons… They can’t be ordinary.”

A demon that Gardinis considered worthy of comparison.

“…We should probably assume they’re at least equal to Gardinis, or possibly superior.”

“We don’t know their identity, but if they’re that significant, might there be some record somewhere?”

Grace, who had been thinking, said this. Rosemary, hiding her mouth with a feather fan, nodded in agreement.

“Since he particularly emphasized ‘youngster,’ perhaps we should also investigate damage caused by relatively new demons.”

“They might be mixed in there. If we trace from there… we might be able to figure something out.”

At Ashley’s words, Claudia closed her eyes.

“That’s true. High-ranking demons tend to intentionally spread their infamy. But a ‘youngster’ according to a veteran demon… the range is ambiguous.”

“Then let’s investigate that as well.”

The elders nodded. Regarding recent demon information, I should probably ask King Melvin about it when we return to Termwills. He might have information from neighboring countries too.

+++

# **312 – Guide to the Boundary City**

After receiving the materials from the elders, we returned to Termwills.

“Well then, let’s go.”

Claudia’s teleportation magic activated, enveloping our surroundings in light. When the white light subsided, we found ourselves at the Termwilz Ritual Site.

Since Vinesdora is a city in the north, the temperature felt considerably warmer when we suddenly teleported to Termwills.

“So this is teleportation magic…”

This was Charlotte’s first time traveling via teleportation magic, so both the scenery and temperature changed in an instant. She looked around with considerable admiration. Teleportation magic had also come up in Gardinis’s stories, and she seemed quite impressed.

She appeared to be captivated by the ritual site’s spring, flower fields, and the flower fairies flitting about with Seraphina… but when her gaze swept around, it became fixed on the towering Theoreme Castle, and she wore an expression of surprise.

King Eberhart had returned to Silvatoria, but Old Sigmund and Valentina would remain in Termwills to continue deciphering, research, and development at the workshop and my house. Charlotte would join them, and we would proceed with inheriting the sealing technique in parallel.

“First, let’s put the items we received at home, then go out into the city for some shopping. I’ll give you a brief tour of the town then.”

“Understood, Theodore-sensei.”

…It seemed Charlotte had decided to call me “sensei.”

We were almost the same age, and it felt a bit odd to be called “sensei” or “master,” but she said that since she was learning the sealing technique, she wanted to clearly establish a teacher-student relationship regardless of age. Well, there was some logic to that, so I compromised with “sensei” rather than being called “master.”

Regardless of what Charlotte called me… I thought I’d buy some ingredients to welcome her. Old Sigmund and Valentina had been to the theater and hot springs since coming to Termwills, but they hadn’t gone out specifically to explore the town. This might be a good opportunity to show them around Termwills.

“Shall we go, then?”

After temporarily storing the items received from the Sages’ Academy in the hidden study, we headed outside. Since both Valentina and Charlotte had rarely been out in the city, let alone outside the country, I decided we’d walk this time to also serve as a city tour.

Marlene also seemed happy, perhaps because she didn’t often go out on her own. When our eyes met, she smiled at me.

“Termwills is divided into central, east, west, north, and south districts… each with its own characteristics. This Eastern District is one of the safer areas in Termwills.”

“Indeed, it’s a beautiful townscape.”

Charlotte nodded while looking at the Eastern District. The well-maintained cobblestone streets were wide with good visibility. The many solidly constructed buildings were probably characteristic of the Eastern District.

“Peresford Academy is down the street over there.”

“Ah, I’ve heard of the academy.”

“It’s famous. It’s often mentioned alongside the Sages’ Academy.”

“Shall we take a look on our way back?”

Since she seemed interested and was looking toward where Peresford Academy was located, I suggested this, and she nodded happily.

“Theodore-sama and I are also enrolled there.”

“If you think it necessary, you could attend. I have materials from the academy at home too. Next—over there are Brightwelt Workshop and Labyrinth Trading Company. Basically, you can handle most errands in this vicinity and the central district alone.”

Valentina and Charlotte hadn’t had freedom of movement until now, and just commuting between home and workplace would be dull. I wanted to avoid unsafe things like going out alone, but I should explain about safe and unsafe areas and what to be careful about.

We then headed toward the central area where the temple and Adventurer Guild were located.

“In the Western District, opposite the Eastern District, there’s the port and orphanage. From here, it would be on the other side of Theoreme Castle.”

“The orphanage is where Sheila and I were cared for, and Director Sandra and the staff are mostly kind people… but basically, the Western District—especially near the port—has poor public safety.”

“If you have business in the Western District and need to go, it’s better not to go alone. If you let me know, I’ll accompany you.”

Sheila and Irmhild said.

“Y-yes.”

“Understood.”

Charlotte and Valentina nodded with serious expressions. Hearing about the poor public safety seemed to make them somewhat tense. That said, the Western District had the Thieves Guild hideout… and if Sheila was with you, it might actually be relatively safe.

“The Northern District is more of a commercial area… I get the impression there are many shops there. You might go there often if you need something. This time, we’re going to buy ingredients at the market in the square in front of the temple, so we won’t go that far.”

“Then… what about the Southern District?”

“The Southern District has many artisans and workshops, and you see many Dwarves there. Perhaps because there are many Dwarves, I feel there are also many taverns.”

While the Eastern District was a quiet residential area, the Southern District had a somewhat rough impression.

Although it was an area where taverns thrived because of the many Dwarves… perhaps because Dwarves are exceptionally strong when it comes to alcohol, the public safety isn’t actually that bad considering the number of taverns. However, the southwestern area near the Western District does become more disorderly as human drunks increase.

“Then there’s the Central District. Here, there are many buildings with unique architectural styles, almost integrated with the labyrinth. There are many noble villas and wealthy merchant residences, and since soldiers patrol frequently, it’s among the safer categories. The square around the Moon Temple we’re heading to now is a bit different because people gather there.”

“From the temple, you can also descend into the labyrinth.”

“The market in front of the temple sells ingredients from the labyrinth, so it’s the place we use most often.”

Grace and Ashley added explanations about the square.

“Recently, a new theater and hot spring district were added.”

“The area around the ritual site we teleported to is the hot spring district.”

At Sheila and Rosemary’s additional explanations, Charlotte’s eyes widened.

As we walked toward the Moon Temple, unlike the relatively quiet Eastern District, it gradually became more crowded and lively. When we reached the main street, carriages came and went, street vendors spread their wares at the roadside—it was simply vibrant.

Seeing a higher proportion of different races like Dwarves, Elves, Lizardmen, and Hawkmen compared to other places was characteristic of Termwills. With adventurers added to that mix, it might appear quite chaotic to someone seeing it for the first time. Old Sigmund remained composed, but Valentina seemed somewhat unsettled, and Charlotte’s eyes were darting around in astonishment.

“I’d heard it was a large city… but it’s quite different from Vinesdora.”

Charlotte murmured her impression. Vinesdora could also be called a major urban area, but somehow it gave an overall orderly impression.

“Perhaps so.”

“Hey, Theodore!”

Just as we arrived at the square while exchanging words, a voice called out from the crowd.

Looking in that direction, I saw it was Auria who had called out. Smiling while waving her hand, she ran over from across the street. Somehow, it looked like the excitement of a child spotting a friend in town. Not that I’d tell her that.

Justia, Dominique. And Forestbird seemed to be accompanying them as escorts.

“Good afternoon. This is Auria-san, the Adventurer Guild Master of Termwills.”

After introducing Auria, I introduced her companions as well. The surprised expression when I introduced Auria was… well, perhaps unavoidable.

“Hello, Theo-kun.”

“Isn’t it unusual for you to be out walking?”

Lucian and Robin from Forestbird said.

“Good afternoon. I was giving my grandfather and relatives a tour of the town.”

“Is that so? We were asked to provide a little escort to the front of the theater.”

Fitz said. The front of the theater… that would be the stall selling shaved ice, carbonated drinks, and cotton candy. This probably meant Justia and Dominique had accompanied Auria on her outing.

“Nice to meet you. I’m Monica from Forestbird, an adventurer.”

“I am Siegmund Willcloud.”

Old Sigmund bowed quietly. Valentina and Charlotte also introduced themselves.

“Grandfather… so that would make you Lisa’s father, then?”

“Oh, you know my daughter?”

“Indeed. I was looked after by the Guild during my adventuring days. There were many adventurers saved because Lisa was there.”

Auria smiled.

Hmm. It seemed I could hear stories from a different perspective than Rosetta’s. Old Sigmund would want to hear about Mother, and since I planned to make dinner lavish to welcome Charlotte today, having more people might be better. Maybe I should invite Auria and the others over.

“Today, we’re out shopping to welcome Charlotte… How about coming over to my house later? You’ll probably have to wait in line for quite some time at the stall in front of the theater, right?”

“Oh ho. I’ll go. Definitely!”

Auria nodded immediately with two affirmative responses. Well, if she came to the house, carbonated drinks and such would be unlimited. Though it felt like the Guild Master’s dignity was being traded off in return.

“Hmm. In that case, I must fetch that thing from the Guild.”

“Ah. That one, huh…”

She must mean the skull staff Mother made. It had no practical use, but it seemed to be Auria’s favorite. Well… Old Sigmund and Valentina already knew about Mother’s sense, so it should be fine.

+++

# **313 – Welcome Party for the New Shrine Maiden**

“It really is a continuous rich harvest. Even outside the labyrinth, seafood seems abundant,” I noted.

For now, I parted ways with Auria and the others, heading toward the market.

Thanks to the liberation of the Water Spirit Hall, the abundance of seafood was remarkable – shrimp, crab, shellfish, and fish. While seafood wasn’t bad, I also wanted to prepare monster-based ingredients unique to the Boundary City. As I browsed the market looking for suitable ingredients for the welcome party, something caught my eye.

“Hmm… I think I’ll buy this and take it home.”

“What kind of monster is this? It’s a bird… right?”

Grace tilted her head in curiosity.

“Yes. It’s a bird monster called Sprintbird.”

Sprintbirds were monsters resembling ostriches or cassowaries. On Earth, they would be extinct species, though they might be closer to moas. They were flightless birds that could run at high speeds using their powerful legs.

They had fierce temperaments, were ferocious and strong. With sharp beaks and claws, their attack methods were simple yet dangerous, earning them a reputation as hazardous monsters.

However, proportional to their danger level, their feathers were beautiful and had value as ornaments. The Sprintbird’s feathers seemed to have already been plucked, but as an ingredient, there were no issues.

“I’ve heard they originally inhabit southern regions.”
