“Then it might be good for the welcome party.”

“Yes. I don’t think this ingredient makes its way to Silvatoria.”

Considering that, this seemed like a good choice for today’s main ingredient.

“Hmm. For southern monsters to appear as well, the labyrinth truly is fascinating,” Old Sigmund observed the Sprintbird with interest.

So I decided to buy the Sprintbird meat along with seafood, vegetables, and fruits to take home.

The Sprintbird was quite large, so I would have preferred to transport it by carriage, but today we were on foot. While I could have stuffed such ingredients directly into Rosemary’s Magic Bag… I felt somewhat reluctant to do so. Instead, I used Wood Magic and Earth Magic to create a makeshift cart and decided to carry it back that way.

After paying for the bird and creating the cart, when I had the Golem load the Sprintbird, the market vendors stared wide-eyed… but well, it couldn’t be helped. I had the Golem push the cart all the way home.

“Welcome home, Master,” Cecilia greeted me with a bow as she came out to meet us.

“I’m home, Cecilia.”

“Nice to meet you. I’m Charlotte Orgran.”

“That’s very polite of you. I’m Cecilia, serving as the head of staff under Theodore-sama.”

Cecilia and Charlotte exchanged greetings.

“Charlotte is affiliated with the Sages’ Academy. She’ll be working with us at Termwills going forward. I bought various things to hold a welcome party, so I’d like you to use them for tonight’s dinner.”

“Understood. This is… a bird?”

Cecilia looked at the Sprintbird with interest before nodding.

“Then I think I’ll try grilling the meat from around the waist area.”

“The sinewy parts might be good for stew dishes,” Cecilia and Grace conversed.

Hmm. So filet steak and stew, then.

“Sounds good. I’m looking forward to the results.”

“Leave it to us. Since it’s a rare ingredient, we’ll join forces with Mihaela-sama and put extra effort into it.”

Just as we were having this conversation, Elliot and the others seemed to have returned home. We met Elliot, Camilla, and Donato in the entrance hall.

“Welcome home, Elliot-sama.”

“I’ve just returned. Theodore-dono, have you returned as well?”

“Yes, I came back from Silvatoria and went to the market for a bit. This is Charlotte, who has come from the Sages’ Academy as the successor to the Sealing Shrine Maiden.”

“Nice to meet you. I’m Charlotte Orgran, as introduced.”

“That’s very polite of you. I’m Elliot Rodias=Siln.”

I introduced Charlotte to Elliot. Camilla and Donato also introduced themselves to Charlotte in turn.

Regarding the new residence, it seemed they had been looking at furniture to use in the new home with Camilla today, since Rosetta had arranged an introduction to a merchant. The crucial meeting with the merchant was scheduled for two days later.

…Hmm. When I first came here, I went furniture shopping with Grace too, didn’t I.

“How was today?”

“It was quite enjoyable, Ashley. I found several items I liked.”

“The selection was good, so there were moments when my eyes wandered.”

“That’s right,” Elliot and Camilla exchanged smiles. Ashley and Donato watched them happily – quite a peaceful scene.

The atmosphere between Elliot and Camilla was already completely that of newlyweds.

“I hope you find a good house.”

“Yes. According to Rosetta-san, the merchant said there’s a good property in the Eastern District. I think the new residence will probably be nearby.”

I see. The Eastern District would be close by and have good security.

Since Elliot and I planned to continue coordinating against demons going forward, having houses nearby would make cooperation easier and more convenient.

“By the way, what monster is that?”

“Ah. It’s a bird monster called Sprintbird. We thought we’d use it for tonight’s dinner as part of the welcome.”

“That sounds enjoyable.”

It seemed everyone was curious about the Sprintbird. I had the Golem carry the ingredients into the house. When we brought them to the kitchen, Mihaela saw them and joined the cooking team, immediately starting the preparations. Yes. I’m looking forward to tonight’s dinner.

When dinner time came, Auria and the others visited as planned. Deputy Guild Master Oswald, Justia, Dominique. And then Forestbird – four people in total.

“This is just a small token,” said Auria. She had brought a gift. Vibrant turquoise and red feather ornaments… These, weren’t they made from Sprintbird feathers?

“These feather ornaments…”

“Yes. It seems a rare monster was defeated in the labyrinth. These are protective charms made from its feathers. Feather ornaments made from Sprintbird feathers are said to ward off evil and bring good fortune. A craftsman immediately processed them and put them up for sale in the market, so I ended up buying one.”

“I see.”

What a coincidence, or rather… I couldn’t help but smile wryly.

Come to think of it, in BFO, when equipped as decorations, they provided fairly high resistance. The protective effect was probably not mistaken.

“Thank you very much. Right away. Now, please come this way.”

Starting with dinner, of course.

When I showed Auria and the others to the dining room, everything was already perfectly prepared. The filet steak with its reddish hue and the sinew meat stew were spreading an appetite-whetting aroma throughout the area.

“This is quite… a feast. Perhaps my gift of a protective charm was insufficient?”

“No. That’s not the case at all,” I replied to Auria, then showed everyone the feather ornaments.

“Auria-san gave me Sprintbird feather ornaments as a gift.”

At these words, Rosemary nodded while hiding her mouth behind her feather fan. It seemed she was laughing.

“It seems we noticed the same things.”

“Hmm? What is it?”

“Today’s main dish is also Sprintbird.”

“What?” Auria also stared wide-eyed.

The Sprintbird had given me a wild impression, but the filet steak had quite an elegant taste. The meat texture had good chewiness, but the flavor itself was not gamey.

Perhaps the Sprintbird’s base ingredient flavor was relatively mild, but Grace and the others’ seasoning was exceptional, fully bringing out the ingredient’s quality. The sinew meat stew was also well-simmered and had a melting texture on the tongue.

“It was very delicious. To receive such wonderful treatment for my welcome… I’m truly happy,” Charlotte stood up and bowed deeply. Grace, Cecilia, and Mihaela responded with gentle smiles.

“I’ve eaten Sprintbird a few times before… but it’s been a while since I’ve had something this tasty,” Oswald said.

“Really now. Eating something like this makes us want to go hunt them too.”

“It looks like a big catch, so hunting them seems dangerous… I wonder where they appear?”

Robin and Fitz were having that conversation.

“Sprintbirds are in Phantom Mist Valley, aren’t they?”

Claudia said. She seemed to know what appeared where.

“Ah, you can reach it from the branch after the 20th underground floor.”

“But the difficulty seems quite high…”

“They say they sometimes appear at the bottom of the valley and run around… So if we encounter them, we’ll probably have to fight them properly. Since illusions appear in the mist, we’ll need countermeasures for that area too.”

They provided information about Sprintbirds and the valley. Hmm. Since Robin and the others were steadily gaining strength, I thought they could probably win.

While drinking tea and having such conversations after the meal, when the topic momentarily lapsed, Valentina asked Auria.

“Speaking of which, I heard you were bringing the staff made by Patricia—Lisa.”

“Yes. I’ve brought it.”

Perhaps because the meal had settled, Auria took out a long, narrow package from her hand luggage.

“It’s Mother’s prototype, isn’t it?”

“Yes. It was interesting, so I had her give it to me.”

Auria produced the infamous skull staff. It was an item featuring an iron ball adorned with a skeletal head from which spikes protruded, connected to the staff by chains.

Apparently, mithril was embedded in the center of the iron ball, and magic stones were set in the eye sockets… and this properly served as a magic catalyst with a magical power amplification function… supposedly.

“Hmm. This is certainly… undoubtedly her work.”

“Indeed… It’s definitely something Patricia made.”

Old Sigmund and Valentina took one look and affirmed this while nodding to each other. They didn’t seem surprised – if anything, they even seemed nostalgic.

“Th-this is…? D-does the Sealing Shrine Maiden have to handle this?”

Charlotte’s eyes were darting around at the outrageousness of the item… but well. Since even Mother acknowledged it as a failure, those worries were unfounded.

“I don’t dislike it,” Sheila said, while Irmhild smiled wryly.

“Does it bite?”

“Well… I think there’s no need to worry about that.”

When Seraphina asked, I assured her it was fine. Since the skeletal design was relatively realistic, Marlene also seemed to be blinking rapidly.

“I tried using it a few times… but as far as wrapping it in lightning strikes and using it as a blunt weapon, there were no problems.”

The concept was supposedly to allow magic to be fired from various angles… but it fit better to call it a morning star.

+++

# **314 – The Shrine Maiden and the Sacred Beast**

After dinner, we moved to the game room to relax. Some played games, others chatted leisurely – everyone was spending time in their own way. Sheila and Irmhild were playing calm-sounding music. Since it was an unfamiliar tune, they might have been practicing a new piece.

Old Sigmund and Valentina were playing darts with Auria while sharing fond memories of Mother.

“Hmm… From Lisa’s demeanor, I assumed she was a noble from Silvatoria… I suppose you could say I wasn’t far off, though not entirely accurate.”

“That understanding is fine. The Adventurer Guild here has been good to my daughter, for which I’m grateful.”

“Not at all. It’s the Guild that received help.”

That was the kind of conversation they were having. Just when you’d think it was becoming a sentimental talk, Auria would be holding cotton candy in one hand, which kind of ruined the atmosphere.

As for Charlotte—

“I must say… I’ve seen many unusual things since coming to Termwills, but your home has surprised me almost as much as the castle,” she murmured.

Apparently, this was her impression after trying various magic tools. The game room’s items seemed unexpected for someone from the Labyrinth Village. Whether it was the billiards table or cards, she could probably tell they were made with magic.

After touching and examining everything, she had been seriously observing the billiards table, cards, and carbonated drink server… but when the Lindwurm arrived just outside the game room earlier, her demeanor changed slightly.

She seemed interested in the Carbuncles playing by sliding down its tail like a slide, and I noticed she was starting to get a bit restless.

Somehow… while she tries to be serious, she still has childlike aspects. Maybe she’s holding back because I’m here.

When I made eye contact with Fortok, the leader of the Carbuncles, he nodded as if to say he understood.

“Hmm. That human girl over there is interested in us?”

“Eh? W-well, I—”

Suddenly being spoken to by Fortok left Charlotte flustered.

“Nay, I understand. Apparently, we’re quite rare outside. It’s understandable for a magician to be interested… Yes, what you’d call academic curiosity, right? Normally we wouldn’t interact with humans… but since you’re Theodore’s relative, we’ll make an exception and let you observe us up close.”

At these words, Charlotte’s eyes widened. Her expression mixed surprise and expectation.

Though Fortok says that… the Carbuncles are highly intelligent and can read emotions, so they can distinguish between humans who are safe to approach and those who aren’t. They understand the outside is dangerous, so they have no intention of going outside the mansion or to places visible from outside, but they interact quite casually with us. Sometimes they perch on someone’s shoulder.

In that sense, Charlotte must have been judged as “safe” by the Carbuncles.

Well… Charlotte being serious, having heard about the Labyrinth Village’s circumstances, she would hold back. I think she would keep her distance from the Carbuncles without an excuse, but she can’t help being curious about them. Fortok, noticing this emotion, created a pretext for Charlotte.

“Th-that’s right. Yes. It’s academically important. Certainly.”

Charlotte nodded as if convincing herself and approached the Carbuncles. Immediately, the small Carbuncles jumped onto the windowsill, approached Charlotte, and shook their heads vertically once as if bowing. Charlotte also politely pinched the hem of her skirt and bowed in return.

“How mysterious… like gems.”

“This is like a second eye for us. Well, as long as you’re careful with that part, touching us shouldn’t be a problem.”

Taking Fortok’s words, Charlotte hesitantly reached out to a Carbuncle. Then the Carbuncle, without hesitation, ran up Charlotte’s arm and perched neatly on her shoulder.

Charlotte seemed not to have expected this, laughing ticklishly and twisting her body. Then more Carbuncles gathered around her… Well, the Carbuncles are friendly and playful. Maybe they find Charlotte’s emotional reactions amusing. The Carbuncle on her shoulder seemed interested in Charlotte’s vertical curls.

The Lindwurm outside the window turned its head to look at Charlotte. Charlotte seemed somewhat intimidated by the wyvern seen up close, but when the Lindwurm quietly closed its eyelids to show it meant no harm, Charlotte seemed to understand. When she gently stroked its nose, the Lindwurm lazily turned its head and curled up as before, though it continued playing with the Carbuncles using only its tail.

Lavigne passed by with Carbuncles on her back, making it quite lively.

“This place—what a wonderful environment…”

With Carbuncles on her palms and shoulders, Charlotte murmured thoughtfully. Hmm. It seems Charlotte likes animals.

Ashley and Marlene joined in, creating quite an endearing scene. Grace, Claudia, and Rosemary were watching with warm smiles. Well… though Rosemary was hiding her mouth behind her feather fan.

“It’s good to see Miss Charlotte fitting in so well,” Elliot said, narrowing his eyes as he watched.

“It can be difficult to adjust until you get used to a new environment.”

“Yes. I also had a hard time when I first came to Silvatoria since I didn’t know anything.”

In Elliot’s case, with amnesia and injuries added to the mix, his circumstances were different and his struggles must have been considerable.

“Speaking of which, you must be having a hard time too, Elliot-san? With establishing a new unit and all.”

“That’s true. I have meetings scheduled to introduce myself to the unit members… but well, I’m used to it.”

He smiled as he said this. Having survived life-threatening situations, he certainly gives the impression of being well-trained.

Hmm… maybe it would be good to have Charlotte and Elliot accompany us when we go to Vinesdora next time. For Elliot, this would apply when heading to the Barony of Silun as well.

“By the way, His Majesty Melvin mentioned that we might need to create a landing area for airships somewhere at the edge of the city.”

“Ah… I received that consultation from Alfred via communication device. It’s probably because the number of people and amount of supplies an airship can transport at once is completely different from a dragon palanquin.”

“…I see. His Majesty Melvin seems to be thinking ahead to when airships become more widespread.”

“I think so. I’ve also reported about the incident at Vinesdora’s Royal Castle.”

Looking further ahead, having airships able to land directly at the Royal Castle would create various inconveniences. Specifically, there would be concerns about airships loaded with soldiers and weapons landing at the Royal Castle to stage a coup.

Or rather, since Zadias actually did that… we can’t rule out someone attempting something similar in the future.

Therefore, the area around the Royal Castle needs to be designated as a no-fly zone, requiring dedicated landing areas for airships.

“For the landing area location, I’m considering the western district. It faces the sea and has good visibility. Since there’s already a port there, it should be convenient for transporting supplies too.”

“The sea and—an aerial port, you mean?”

“That’s right.”

Literally an “air port” – an airport. An airport. There’s the question of how airships should take off, land, and dock… First, since they can take off and land vertically, we don’t need runways, so we probably don’t need particularly large areas of land.

A simple approach would be… taking advantage of the airship’s boat-like base, what about having them float on the sea? While docked, we wouldn’t need to use magic tools for levitation, which should save magical power. We’d need waterproofing and rust prevention measures, but that shouldn’t be too difficult.

Then we’d probably need guidance lights for nighttime takeoffs and landings? We could probably supplement this with magic tools. As for a control tower… I suspect we’ll need one once the number of airships increases.

That said, regarding the airport, this is assuming airships are completed and become somewhat widespread, so there’s still time—

“We’ll also need a place to build airships. The area near the port is spacious, so utilizing that area might be reasonable.”

For building airships, the workshop’s courtyard is definitely too small and visible. On the other hand, the square in front of the Knight’s Tower where we’re currently preparing materials is where knights and soldiers usually train, so we can’t occupy it for too long.

Perhaps it would be best to prepare a dedicated location near the port and build new facilities there. I should use Earth Magic to create models and work out the basic form.

+++

# **315 – Golem of the Port**

–The next morning dawned. First, I escorted Auria, Justia, and Dominique to the Adventurer Guild, then immediately headed to the Royal Castle with everyone.

“Oh, you’ve arrived, Theodore.”

“Good morning, Your Majesty Melvin.”

I continued by greeting Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana as well.

“Good morning, Your Highness.”

“Yes, good morning.”

“Good morning, Ambassador.”

“Hmm. Well then, shall we proceed?”

When we appeared at the Royal Castle, King Melvin with his escort was waiting for us. Today we were scheduled to board the airship and head to the airspace above the western district’s harbor.

The plan was to go inspect the potential site for building a shipyard and airport.

“Good morning, Dame Mildred.”

“Ambassador.”

Since the Knight Order Commander Mildred was also present, I took the opportunity during greetings to briefly mention updates about Lazaro’s greatsword.

“Please wait a little longer regarding the matter of the Blazing Fortress. It seems the greatsword’s repair will take a bit more time.”

According to Alfred, it was apparently made from quite a unique metal.

Rather than just reconnecting the broken part, they were currently reforging the entire blade. The blacksmith Viola said that since Alfred could access the Royal Castle’s archives, they could easily obtain valuable manufacturing techniques as information, which was helpful… but there didn’t seem to be any issues with the repair itself.

Alfred also mentioned he was preparing a full set of aerial combat equipment for when he meets Lazaro. I suppose when we go to the Blazing Fortress next time, we’ll be giving Lazaro the aerial combat equipment.

“Thank you. There’s no particular hurry on my part, so please don’t worry about it. Please convey that to the blacksmith as well.”

“Understood.”

After finishing communications with Mildred, we boarded the airship and departed for the western district. Those accompanying us were just our Party members – King Melvin, Princess Stephania, and Princess Adriana, along with their knight escorts, and then Alfred, Elliot, Old Sigmund, Valentina, and Charlotte, who would likely be deeply involved with the airport.

“My, my. An airship. And to think this isn’t even its final form yet – quite astonishing.”

King Melvin, standing on the deck, voiced his impressions of riding an airship for the first time. His expression seemed somewhat amused.

“Since it has many blind spots, if we can resolve those issues, it might make a good transport ship. If we choose its purpose carefully, we won’t need to use special materials, and manufacturing could be done cheaply.”

“Having different final forms depending on the application. Hmm. That makes sense.”

Old Sigmund grasped the helm and touched the crystal ball beside him, causing the ship to begin ascending.

After crossing over the castle walls at a leisurely pace, it turned toward the western district and began moving forward.

“Training facilities for the newly established unit… might not be a bad idea either. Since it’s an anti-demon unit, it would be better not to reveal too much about their training methods.”

So said King Melvin. Probably part of information control.

“Having them as attached facilities might be good too. That is, if we have enough land.”

“No need to worry about that. All the land around Termwills falls under the royal family’s jurisdiction, so if necessary, we can simply expand the facilities from the outer edges further outward.”

“I see…”

This kind of flexibility feels characteristic of the royal family. Well, for me, having flexibility is certainly welcome.

While we were talking, the airship arrived near the western district’s harbor, so we immediately examined the terrain from above.

“You can really see it well from up here. The breakwater forms a circle extending from the outer wall. So that means the barrier covers an area slightly outside of that, I suppose?”

Rosemary looked down at the harbor from the deck and spoke.

We created a scaled model of the entire Termwills area, albeit a simple one, to get a rough idea of how far the barrier extended.

“What will happen with the barrier?”

Grace tilted her head.

“Ah. I think it will be similar to the hot spring district. When we completed the outer wall, the hot spring area became covered by Termwills’ barrier too… So if we cover something to separate it from the outside world, it should function.”

If we build facilities at the outer edge and create an outer wall… that area should also be recognized as “inside” through the spell formula and incorporated into the barrier.

“This area here – seems usable.”

I pointed to part of the model and a corner of the actual landscape. Everyone compared the model with the actual terrain. Near the barrier’s outer edge, there was a rocky hill-like terrain that protruded slightly toward the sea, though not enough to be called a cape.

At first glance, it didn’t look like flat land, and the pointed terrain gave the impression of being difficult to use. To utilize this kind of terrain, you’d normally build a lighthouse at the tip, I suppose. However, in Termwills’ case, Theoreme Castle is visible from quite far out at sea, functioning as a lighthouse substitute, so there was no need for one.

“Hmm. What are you planning to do?”

King Melvin seemed to be enjoying himself, making various predictions about what I was thinking.

“I’m considering carving out this small cape and modifying it into a shipyard and harbor. If we carve out the surrounding terrain to create flat land, we can reuse the entire area as building materials without particularly securing construction materials, which would save us the trouble of preparation and such.”

I remade the model focusing only on the rocky hill area, preserving only the sea-facing part from around the slope connecting to the rocky hill as a breakwater, while carving out most of the terrain to remake it into flat land.

The plan is to modify the inside of the breakwater into a shipyard and airport, hollowing out the interior using the former rocky hill terrain and fashioning it into a fortress-like building.

Then, using the leftover soil and sand, we’ll build a high wall covering the facility and connect that wall to Termwills’ outer wall. The top of the wall could serve as a connecting passageway.

The final form would be… a new fortress-like facility facing the sea.

“Well, this is…”

“Only you could do this, Teacher…”

When I finished explaining, everyone wore expressions of astonishment. King Melvin eventually nodded with admiration and said:

“Interesting. Since the hot spring district was created in the eastern district, having new facilities on the opposite diagonal would create symmetry, which would be just right.”

I see. I hadn’t really considered that aspect.

“If I can get permission, I’d like to start construction immediately.”

“That’s even more interesting…. It would be quite a sight to see Howard and the others’ faces when it’s completed.”

King Melvin seemed to ponder for a moment, then raised his head. A mischievous grin appeared on his face, as if he’d thought of a prank.

“Hmm. I shall grant permission in my name.”

“Thank you very much. Then, I’ll be going for a bit. Since it will be large-scale magic construction, if confusion seems likely to arise due to the work–“

“In that case, I’ll dispatch knights to explain that there are no problems.”

“Thank you.”

In that case, I don’t need to hold back. Everyone can literally have a grandstand view.

“Alright, I’ll be going for a bit.”

“Do you need magic potions or vitality recovery magic?”

Ashley asked.

“That’s right. I’ll take breaks along the way, so I’ll ask for them then.”

“Yes.”

“You’ll be making large golems, right? Please be careful not to get injured.”

So said Claudia.

“Yeah. It’s large-scale, so I’ll be careful.”

Taking Seraphina, Caduceus, and Balor with me, I flew from the airship’s deck. When I glanced back, I saw Marlene waving cheerfully toward us. When I waved back, everyone else also smiled and waved in return.

Alright. Let’s do this.

First, I headed to the airspace above the target location. I had Caduceus take crow form and, together with Balor, check that there were no people in the vicinity. I’ll have Caduceus and Balor continue watching the surroundings from above. I’ll be moving a large number of golems, and it would be dangerous if anyone approached during construction.

“Alright… Then, shall we begin?”

“Mm-hmm!”

As if taking Seraphina’s response as a signal, I deployed a magic circle. Using earth magic, I created two, then three Huge Golems, and while using the model as reference, began roughly carving out the terrain.

Since the Huge Golems would be in the way for now, after creating them, I moved them to locations where they wouldn’t obstruct. If I have them wait in a seated position slightly away from the main road… well, that should somewhat reduce their intimidating presence, and no one would likely approach. I released control of the moved Huge Golems, returning them to the same state as ordinary rocks. This was unprecedented large-scale magic construction. I strengthened my power through magical power circulation, psyching myself up to maintain control.

While imagining the sea-facing tip becoming a breakwater and the Termwills side becoming flat land, I proceeded with leveling. The wide sea between the cape and Termwills – that area is scheduled to become the airport.

Preserving the rocky hill to be modified into a building, I continuously carved out the terrain, sending the material to the golem storage area and releasing control, repeating this process.

Once I’d carved out something roughly close to the final form, I used earth magic to reinforce the structure of the sea-facing breakwater side. Following that, I leveled the part that would become flat land. I’ll have golems pave this with stone later. As for the rocky hill remaining on the flat land – I can process it into a building at the end.

Hmm… I feel like my magical power has increased considerably compared to when I first came to Termwills. Even though I’m creating quite a number of Huge Golems, I still feel like I have room to spare.

Part of it is due to continuing labyrinth exploration… but it might also be because I’ve defeated several high-ranking demons both inside and outside the labyrinth.

Unlike during combat, I can refine as much magical power as I want to my heart’s content.

I don’t want to overexert myself with the construction, and if I take several breaks, I should be able to proceed with room to spare. Well… I think I might be able to complete everything by the end of today.

+++

# **316 – Towards the Construction of the Airship**

With the terrain cutting completed, I reactivated the Huge Golems that had become mere rock masses and created stone pavement for the plaza area, along with walls and gates surrounding the facilities. Furthermore, I began reshaping them into building materials for walls connecting to Termwills’ outer walls.

Wall building materials – I had the Huge Golems stack massive stones, structurally reinforced them to prevent collapse, then disassembled them from Huge Golems into regular Golems, transforming them into stone pavement to lay out.

“Hey… Can Golems really disperse and reconfigure at that speed?”

“Don’t be stupid. That thing’s a monster. While controlling the Huge Golem… it’s disassembling the extremities into regular Golems. Then, it’s taking those Golems one by one, disassembling them again, and reconfiguring them… directly into stone pavement. It’s having idle Golems share the work – impossible.”

Some of the knights and Mage Corps members assigned to perimeter security had become spectators. They were muttering such words while watching our work. I could feel the fishermen’s gazes from the harbor too… but I continued working without paying them mind. Once one Huge Golem’s disassembly and building material rearrangement was complete, I moved the next Huge Golem… and so on, progressing steadily.

After finishing the plaza and outer walls came the buildings. I hollowed out the interior of the towering rock remaining in the plaza to create an entrance hall, workshop, dining hall, break room, temporary sleeping quarters, storage, plus baths, toilets, and so on.

“Should we keep this pillar here?”

“Yeah. Since the room is spacious, it’s better not to remove this support.”

“Then I’ll reinforce it.”

While creating spaces considering each room’s purpose, I consulted with Seraphina to erect pillars and reinforce structures. I extended the top floor vertically so it could serve as a control tower.

Currently, since there’s no decoration or interior work, it gives a somewhat rugged impression… but considering it will also serve as training facilities for the anti-Demon unit, this might not be bad as it is.

I might need to work on the floors and roof a bit more. Considering measures against heat and cold, I’ll probably need to replace some building materials using Wood Magic or similar methods… but that can be done slowly later.

Next. The sea area facing the harbor side. I created a pathway along the edge several steps lower than the plaza height. It’s at a height that won’t get submerged even at high tide.

“Does this area of the sea become a fishing ground?”

After reaching that point, I asked the fishermen who were watching the work with stunned expressions about the underwater area. I had asked the Knight Order to bring fishermen willing to cooperate. By hearing opinions from several people and actually looking at the underwater area myself, I should get a general idea.

“…Eh – Ah, ah, no. That area just has depth, you see. Can’t really call it a good fishing ground. Need to go out a bit further.”

“Hmm. Since stones sometimes fall from the cliff. It’s dangerous below, so nobody approaches. Some are actually relieved it’s gone.”

“Is that so? I was thinking of considering other methods if there were reefs… but it seems fine as is.”

I’d heard that reefs become good fishing grounds since fish gather there. I didn’t really want to touch the underwater area, and if necessary, I was considering building a pool within the premises… but it seems there won’t be any problems.

Just to be sure, I should see the underwater area with my own eyes. Wrapping myself in a bubble Shield and lighting a magical lamp, I dove into the sea. From within the water, I checked the seabed terrain. I reinforced areas that seemed unstable.

Hmm… Seems exactly as the fishermen said.

By extending a pier from the edge and installing guide lights there, nighttime takeoffs and landings should become possible.

When I surfaced, I made eye contact with the fishermen who had been peering into the sea wondering what happened to me since I hadn’t come up. I spoke to the astonished fishermen again.

“Then, if this facility causes any issues with fishing catches or ship operations, please report it. I think we can handle it to some extent.”

“U-Understood.”

The fisherman answered with a strained smile.

Continuing work in that manner, taking breaks and receiving lunch provisions from the Knight Order along the way, by the time the sunset dyed the surroundings red, most of the construction was complete. I stacked leftover materials into Blocks. They could be reused when needed.

I looked around. The sight of stone pavement laid out regularly across the plaza. Quite spectacular indeed.

While checking the work results after completing the task, the airship descended in altitude and everyone came down to the plaza.

“Well done. My, my. To finish it in less than a day.”

King Melvin, who had disembarked from the airship, said while looking around.

“It progressed better than expected. We had recovery Magic and Potions prepared too. We had Cursed Melodies played during each break. However, the interior details like building insides aren’t finished yet.”

“Hmm. Then let us prepare the interior furnishings and furniture.”

“Thank you.”

When I answered, King Melvin nodded with satisfaction.

“You showed us something wonderful. Amazing precision… both the stone pavement and walls, you couldn’t slip a sheet of paper between them.”

“It was magnificent. Every time the giant Golem stood up, the terrain was carved away.”

Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana touched the outer walls to verify their quality, looking delighted.

“Haaaah… I feel like I’ve witnessed your true capabilities, sensei.”

“Truly, though he’s my grandson, he’s something unbelievable.”

“Fu, fufu… I feel like common sense is being destroyed.”

Charlotte looked like her soul had left her body. Old Sigmund wore a dry smile while Valentina had a distant look in her eyes.

“So we’ll be training using this as our base. Since we’ll be coordinating with the magician who built this, the unit members’ morale should rise too. Most reassuring.”

Elliot was also squinting while gazing at the buildings.

“Theo, good work. Seraphina, it must have been tough working for so long.”

“I had fun.”

“I’m glad you’re unharmed.”

“Yeah. Keeping the Magic Circle deployed the whole time made my shoulders a bit stiff.”

Grace and Ashley smiled while offering their appreciation. Seraphina still seemed energetic enough to fly around.

“In that case, shall I massage your shoulders later?”

Claudia said that, exchanging smiles with Marlene. Come to think of it, Claudia and Marlene were in the living room today.

“Mm. Then I’ll take you up on that later.”

“Yes, leave it to me.”

“…As for me, seeing a Huge Golem after so long reminded me of what’s in the books.”

Rosemary, hiding her mouth with a feather fan, glanced around. Whether she was laughing or surprised, since she was hiding her expression, it was somewhat hard to tell.

“Well, the Golem’s form was different back then though.”

“That’s true.”

Saying that with a small laugh, Rosemary looked up at the wall.

“Good work, Theodore-kun.”

“Yeah. Thank you.”

Irmhild smiled while Sheila gave a silent thumbs-up. I thanked them and returned Sheila’s thumbs-up.

“Good work, Theo-kun. You mentioned attaching guide lights so ships can land at night, right?”

“That’s the plan. Well, I think we can handle that gradually. Alfred has other work too anyway.”

After exchanging words with everyone, starting with my conversation with Alfred, we shifted back to discussing the shipyard’s future.

“Hmm. Then, shall we have the airship materials prepared at the Royal Castle transported here?”

“Yes. We’ve secured sufficient space, and since it’s inside the walls, it won’t attract much attention, so we should be able to start airship construction without issues. Are the materials ready?”

“Most of what’s needed has been prepared.”

Saying that, King Melvin nodded. His work really is fast.

“Then I think we can start on the framework and exterior.”

“To prevent material theft, we’ll assign security and patrols to this facility. You may proceed with airship construction as you see fit.”

“Thank you.”

“Regarding security, I believe my Dolls could be stationed here as well.”

“Oh? Then using both soldiers and Dolls should work well.”

Rosemary’s simple Dolls, huh. Since they can keep watch tirelessly, having them stationed here would indeed be reassuring.

Next is collecting Magic Stones at the Blazing Fortress. Hmm… It might be about time, or perhaps I should visit the full moon Labyrinth once. For Magic Stone collection purposes, there’s no place more efficient than that location.

According to Claudia, even without waiting for the full moon, if we go through the entrance monument, we can be taken there. In any case, it’s a place we must conquer to reach the deepest part.

+++

# **317 – Holy Land of the South**

“The meet-and-greet tomorrow… apparently the location for the address has been changed,” I informed everyone while relaxing in the living room after returning home from building the shipyard. There was still some time before dinner, so I shared King Melvin’s notification with them.

“You mean the meet-and-greet for the anti-demon unit that was supposed to be held at the Royal Castle?”

“Yes. According to King Melvin, the aim is to boost morale by immediately showing them the newly constructed facility.”

“A meet-and-greet at the shipyard… Since it also serves as the unit’s training facility, it might be just right. I think it also carries the meaning of showing that they have expectations for the unit,” Rosemary said.

“Probably. They might have planned to let them tour it even while under construction. Since it’s almost complete now, I think they changed the gathering location there.”

The permission for Magic Construction likely had reasons along those lines.

“Brother Elliot seems like he’ll be busy,” Ashley said with a wry smile.

“Yeah. Both sides look tough,” I agreed.

In the morning, there’s the meet-and-greet and greetings to unit members. From the afternoon, he has plans to look for a new residence – quite a packed schedule.

As for tomorrow’s meet-and-greet, I’m also supposed to give greetings… Well, it’ll work out somehow. That should be enough about the meet-and-greet.

“Ah, also Claudia. About the Full Moon Labyrinth…”

“Full Moon Labyrinth…”

“Yes. I’m thinking it’s about time we consider conquering that place.”

When I mentioned the plan to conquer the Full Moon Labyrinth, Claudia quietly closed her eyes.

“…I see. I thought we would have to go there someday.”

“Is it truly a dangerous place?” Grace asked.

I nodded in response. “I think it’s more dangerous than the Blazing Fortress. It’s not like we need to go immediately since we want to consider countermeasures. We’ll also need the Magic Stones for the airship after we complete the exterior.”

The Full Moon Labyrinth… originally could only be entered once a month, which is why conquest hasn’t progressed much, and there are few stone tablets.

Rather than gimmicks like terrain and traps, it feels like there are many orthodox power-push type monsters.

However… unless you try to advance deeper, the monster attacks aren’t that fierce. If you just got lost, as long as you act with only escape in mind, survival itself shouldn’t be that difficult.

“I don’t mind taking you there. But before we go, there are several things I should tell you,” Claudia said, looking straight at me.

I nodded and returned her gaze directly.

“First… that labyrinth is different from other places. How should I put it… The labyrinth has monsters appearing in almost all areas… There was a miscalculation there, but if we’re talking about whether it’s fulfilling its purpose, I’d say it’s still functioning.”

“Securing food and resources, and strengthening explorers?”

“Yes. But regarding the Full Moon Labyrinth, the purpose is different. The path leading to the Labyrinth Village, the path leading to the Moonlight Temple. And further beyond. The Moonlight Temple was built later using the location, so it’s slightly different, but for me as the administrator, it’s a path leading to a place I don’t want people to enter.”

I see… So the very nature of the Full Moon Labyrinth differs from other places.

The purpose of the Full Moon Labyrinth is interception and elimination. That’s why if you don’t push deeper and return quietly, it eases its attacks.

I wonder if this reflects Claudia’s wishes… She doesn’t want people to intrude, but she also doesn’t want to take lives recklessly.

“As for the path related to the Labyrinth Village, I’ve already permitted entry, so there’s no need to worry about that. In any case, I’ve sealed the doors, and normally you can’t descend from the Full Moon Labyrinth.”

“…So, I’m thinking of incorporating some content anticipating the Full Moon Labyrinth into our training starting tomorrow.”

“The Full Moon Labyrinth… is it dangerous even for Theodore?” Sheila asked.

“Hmm. There seem to be various troublesome monsters, so it might be dangerous if we let our guard down,” I replied.

We’ve been able to progress smoothly so far because we’ve taken proper countermeasures, but that’s exactly why we might become complacent. I want everyone to stay vigilant.

Marlene and Seraphina nodded with serious expressions. Good, that’s the right attitude.

“There are some descriptions in several documents about the monsters that appear… but I suppose it’s best to ask Lady Claudia about this,” someone noted.

Yeah. I know to some extent too, but there are parts I can’t talk about as if I’ve seen them myself. Working out countermeasures while consulting with Claudia would be more reliable.

“The structure itself is surprisingly simple. The problem is the monsters. As for simple power-push monsters… well, we can overpower them. The first dangerous ones would be monsters with petrification abilities.”

“Petrification abilities – Basilisk and Cockatrice, right?”

At my words, Claudia nodded.

“Yes. Both are there.”

I see… The Full Moon Labyrinth has both Basilisk and Cockatrice – two types of monsters with petrification abilities. This is why we can’t afford to let our guard down.

Basilisk uses Evil Eye. Cockatrice uses breath and direct attacks with its beak. Their methods of petrification differ, so the countermeasures will also vary.

“Is there magic that can cure petrification?” Irmhild tilted her head.

Ashley nodded. “It can be used. It was in the documents we received from Silvatoria.”

“I can also remove it alone. But… it takes time with Circulating Ki, so please assume it’s impossible during combat.”

“So as long as Theo and Lady Ashley are safe, recovery from petrification is possible,” someone noted.

“If even one person gets petrified, we’ll need to immediately consider retreat using Teleportation Magic,” another added.

It’s reassuring that we have several backup measures even if we make mistakes. Looking around at the party members, we also have methods to counter each type of monster. We should maximize safety by leveraging our strengths.

And the next day. For the anti-demon unit meet-and-greet, greetings, and address, people gathered at the newly constructed shipyard.

An airship was docked above the facility, with King Melvin, Prince Josiah, Princess Stephania, and Princess Adriana showing their faces from the deck. Having royalty personally appear to give an address would undoubtedly be the ultimate morale booster. Docking the airship is also part of that.

“It’s been a while, Your Highness Josiah.”

“Ah. Long time no see, Theodore-kun.”

When I greeted Prince Josiah, his face broke into a smile.

“We arrived last night. When I returned to Termwills, the terrain had changed again, which surprised me. I never thought you could build this in one day…”

Saying this while looking around the shipyard, Prince Josiah nodded with admiration.

“I heard you had traveled to the south.”

“Yes. I’m acting as a mediator trying to improve relations between Duke Driscoll and Grand Duke Debonnis. Grand Duke Debonnis said he has intentions to reconcile with the ducal house… but Duke Driscoll is somewhat problematic. Rather than improving relations with the Grand Duke, he seems to want to approach you.”

“Me?”

“Of course, I told him that since you’re my father’s direct vassal, I couldn’t answer anything,” Prince Josiah said with a wry smile.

Though he’s smiling, he seems somewhat tired.

With the Kingdom of Verdugal moving in the anti-demon direction, it appears he’s in the midst of adjustments to ensure no one within the country hinders progress.

“He’s rather worldly, that gentleman,” Prince Josiah commented.

As I was talking with Prince Josiah, King Melvin joined us.

“He sent me a letter too. Asking me to definitely introduce him to Theodore. In short, I think he wants to benefit from association.”

“That man is completely…” Prince Josiah shook his head.

As for me, I could only respond with a wry smile.

“Well, the Duke is our problem, so you don’t need to worry too much about it. We’re thinking of ensuring we don’t get in Theodore’s way as much as possible,” King Melvin said.

“More importantly, while in the south, I also investigated what happened with the Duoveris Cult afterward, and I heard an interesting story,” Prince Josiah said, his expression turning serious as he changed the subject.

“The Duoveris Cult? Are those remnants doing something again?” I asked.

The group led by Gardinis… Come to think of it, with the loss of Gardinis, their founder, I am curious about what happened afterward.

“Ah, no. I heard that group has significantly weakened after losing their central figure, so there’s no need to worry. Since they weren’t originally active within Verdugal’s borders, there was no direct relationship anyway. Rather… it seems there’s a place the cult considers a sacred land.”

“The cult’s sacred land…”

That’s… Considering that cult, regardless of its lower ranks, had Gardinis – one of the oldest demons – as its founder, I can’t help but feel there must be some connection.

While we’re gathering information about demons… based on Prince Josiah’s information, it might be necessary to visit the south at some point.

+++

# **318 – Demon Slayer Knight Order**

“The Duoveris Cult was attempting to infiltrate Verdugal. My uncle apparently captured a cult executive trying to escape across the border and extracted information about the cult’s internal affairs,” said Prince Josiah.

That made sense. Southern stability would be Grand Duke Debonnis’s concern, and if there was information about the cult attempting to infiltrate Verdugal, he would naturally increase his vigilance.

From Termwills’ perspective, Grand Duke Debonnis’s territory lies to the southeast, while the territory near the border that his second son inherited from Roy is to the south.

Apparently, Duke Driscoll was invited by Grand Duke Debonnis as part of his efforts to improve relations. Prince Josiah, having facilitated their connection, attended the meeting as well. It sounded like the kind of situation that would be mentally exhausting.

“I’ve had the civil officials investigate the records about demons… It is indeed a concerning matter,” said King Melvin, crossing his arms and stroking his chin.

“Gardinis’s involvement is troubling. The Black Bones were also involved in Beriondora’s fall, and there were signs they were moving to revive their leader.”

Since Gardinis called him a young upstart, it meant he must have known something about his origins in some way.

Even the veteran Alvelinde appeared young, so while a demon’s appearance doesn’t correspond to their age… do demons share their personal histories with each other among their ranks?

Considering the impression they give, it’s somewhat hard to imagine demons being that familiar with each other. If he learned it through hearsay, there should be records somewhere, and if we could trace those, we might uncover his origins… but well.

“Hmm… We should thoroughly investigate the records about demons, especially those from the southern regions. I’ll have the civil officials look into this matter as well.”

As time was running short, we wrapped up the discussion and concluded our conversation with King Melvin and Prince Josiah.

Looking over the square, I saw the members from Verdugal and Silvatria who would be joining the new unit lined up in formation.

The guests were arranged near the building entrance. From the Royal Castle, important figures around King Melvin had also attended as guests, including Chancellor Howard, Knight Order Commander Mildred, and Court Magician Ricard.

Those attending as my acquaintances included party members, workshop staff, and Silvatria-related personnel.

Alfred wasn’t on the airship but was standing with the workshop staff wearing his disguise ring as if it were perfectly normal. He apparently dislikes standing out as Prince Albert. It might have become second nature to him by now.

Regarding the composition of the new unit, it seemed Mercedes and Chester from the Veldgar Kingdom Knights had also joined.

The Dragon Knight unit doesn’t exactly have personnel to spare, so this must have been judged necessary. The rest were selected from the Mage Corps and soldiers based on their skills, character, background, and other factors, undergoing interviews and confirming their willingness before being assigned.

From Silvatria, first were Elmer and the others. Regarding Donovan and Lionel, it seemed they had regained their official status now that the Zadias matter had been resolved.

The court musicians began playing heroic music, and the ceremony to establish the new unit was declared to begin.

King Melvin appeared on the deck, surveyed the assembled crowd, and spoke.

“Everyone, your efforts are appreciated. In these troubled times with the covert activities of allied demon groups, I find it reassuring that so many brave warriors have gathered here. From this day forward, you shall strive to hone your skills as members of the Demon-Slaying Knight Order and fulfill your duties.”

The official name of the anti-demon unit was announced. King Melvin extended his right arm sideways, indicating the airship and shipyard.

“The wisdom of the magician who built this shipyard in merely one day. The sky-faring ship brought from Silvatria. And the knowledge and power of you brave warriors. All these have gathered here today. The bonds that will be forged through your exchanges and training. I am confident that the martial prowess and wisdom of both nations will dispel the crises facing our two countries.”

His words were met with cheers praising King Melvin. After the cheers subsided, he continued.

“Let me introduce to everyone Elliot Rodias Silun, who will assume the position of Commander of the Demon-Slaying Knight Order. Some of you may have already heard, but Elliot was the eldest son of the Silun baronial family. Though he lost his memory in a ship accident, he achieved military exploits in Silvatria and became renowned as the Magic Knight. Elliot, step forward.”

“Yes, sir!”

Prompted by King Melvin, Elliot, who had been standing in the front row of the knights, took one step forward and bowed in a subject’s salute.

“He regained his memory, fought the demons’ minions in Vinesdora, and has now returned to our country. Beyond his martial prowess and character, I guarantee that his background makes him a suitable person to serve as Commander of the Demon-Slaying Knight Order, connecting our two nations. If anyone questions my decision or believes their own strength makes them more suitable for the position of Commander than him, step forward now.”

He looked around as he said this… but no one stepped forward.

Some aspects of Elliot’s abilities weren’t widely known in Verdugal. By clearly establishing his background and capabilities here, there was likely an aim to solidify Elliot’s position.

“It seems there are no objections. Elliot, what say you?”

“Yes, sir. I humbly accept the appointment as Commander of the Demon-Slaying Knight Order. I intend to devote myself to repaying the debt I owe to His Majesty Melvin and His Majesty Eberhart, earning the trust of all knight order members. And I swear to dedicate my entire soul to fulfilling our tasks.”

“Excellent. Adriana.”

“Yes.”

King Melvin stepped back and handed the proceedings over to Princess Adriana.

“I am Adriana, having come from the Kingdom of Silvatria as representative of my father, Eberhart. I consider it an honor to attend this establishment of the Demon-Slaying Knight Order. Though my abilities may be modest, I am resolved to contribute to the friendship between our two nations. Let us walk this path together.”

She said this with a smile. Applause erupted from the attendees, and King Melvin nodded before continuing.

“Otherworld Ambassador Theodore, step forward.”

“Yes, sir.”

I took one step forward.

“Theodore has achieved remarkable results in recent years and brought aerial combat equipment to our country. This shipyard was also created by Theodore’s hand. The Demon-Slaying Knight Order will coordinate with him, assisting him in opposing the demons. As the foremost expert in aerial combat, he will also provide your instruction. Theodore.”

“Yes.”

I nodded and bowed. King Melvin seemed to be carefully choosing his wording. As part of information control, he was avoiding using the term “demon slayer.”

“I am Theodore Gartner, as introduced by His Majesty Melvin. Though I am still young, I will devote my full efforts to the duties of instruction and training. I look forward to working with you all.”

As I said this, applause broke out… but at the part about “full efforts,” for a moment, the expressions of the knight order members—especially those familiar with me—seemed to twitch. …I don’t intend to push them that hard in training itself. If they get injured during training, it would defeat the whole purpose.

After giving a safe greeting and stepping back, King Melvin took over again.

“That concludes my address. We have prepared a modest celebratory gathering. Everyone, replenish your spirits, deepen your exchanges, and prepare for training and your duties.”

With these words, the ceremony to establish the Demon-Slaying Knight Order concluded. Food was being brought from the Royal Castle to the shipyard building.

After the ceremony ended, we moved to the dining hall inside the building.

It had the atmosphere of a buffet-style standing party. Probably to facilitate interaction among the members.

So, being in the position of receiving greetings, I ended up accepting greetings from the members along with Elliot, with only light eating.

“Ambassador, Commander Elliot. We look forward to working with you.”

“Likewise.”

“Looking forward to working with you.”

After finishing their greetings to us, the knights were shaking hands and actively trying to build good relationships here and there as part of the exchange between Verdugal and Silvatria.

“Still… to create such a facility in just one day.”

“Thank you. Since it also serves as training facilities, if you encounter any inconveniences while using them, we can make adjustments to some extent, so please let us know.”

“I see… That’s unique to magic construction.”

The knights’ smiles twitched. Meanwhile, Elliot was also exchanging words with the knights.

“Commander, we heard you’re the Magic Knight… Being skilled with both sword and magic is reassuring.”

“The use of magic tools is essential for aerial combat. Commander Elliot, what kind of magic do you use?”

“Water Magic. I mastered sword arts adapted to magic in Silvatria.”

“Water Magic… Then, does that include Healing Magic?”

“Yes.”

The members’ expressions brightened upon hearing about Healing Magic.

Like Ashley, having someone who can use Healing Magic is indeed reassuring. From recovering vitality to detoxification, having just one Healing Magic user increases sustained combat capability and reduces casualties. In military forces, Healing Magic users tend to earn trust and respect… and if they can also wield a sword and fight on the front lines, even more so.

“I’m not very knowledgeable about magic… Ambassador, what kind of magic are you skilled in?”

The topic shifted to me.

“I don’t have a particularly specialized element. If I had to say, all types of offensive magic.”

“Or rather, he’s proficient in almost all schools of magic.”

“That’s quite…”

“That’s extremely reassuring when fighting demons.”

“Absolutely.”

Elmer and the others nodded thoughtfully at Elliot’s words. While the reaction was somewhat awkward, it was reassuring that Elliot’s relationship with the Demon-Slaying Knight Order members was off to a reasonably good start.

“…I’m concerned about the Ambassador’s training content.”

“Indeed…”

“No, it’s normal. The ‘full efforts’ part refers to my mindset.”

It means I won’t cut corners when planning the training content or monitoring its progress, so there’s no need to worry.

As usual, we’ll utilize golems for dealing with miasma bullets and miasma swords, methods of aerial maneuver using magic tools, and things like that. Beyond that, experience in actual aerial combat matters, so we might also do sparring.

+++

# **319 – The Shackles of Magical Tools**

After the instructions and introductions for the Demon-Slaying Knight Order, the subsequent social gathering disbanded in the early afternoon. Elliot immediately went out with Camilla to look at potential new homes.

Regarding the shipyard, aside from the cafeteria, the interior and furnishings were not yet complete. Once those aspects were in order, the training for the Demon-Slaying Knight Order would likely begin in earnest. At that time, we would also proceed with preparations for the full moon labyrinth for the party members in parallel. It should serve as a good example for how to use aerial combat gear.

As for the airship’s keel and exterior, the materials had already been brought in, so it should be possible to start constructing the airship’s exterior around the same time as the training.

The Demon-Slaying Knight Order would also be boarding the airship as crew. I think the environment of being able to train while watching the airship being built from the corner of their eyes would be quite motivating.

Now then. We returned home and decided to relax in the game room while discussing the magic tools to be installed on the airship with everyone, including Alfred and Viola.

In the game room where Irmhild and the others played music, we spread out blueprints and took notes while drinking tea.

As for me, I proceeded with the meeting while writing down recordable spell formulas on paper.

“You mentioned changing the properties of magic stones and fixing them… Does that mean you can also create magic stones with properties similar to Claudia, Irmhild, or Seraphina?”

“Yes. It should be possible to adjust the quality of a magic stone to resemble someone’s personal magical aptitude. Changing a magic stone’s properties and fixing its element involves pouring magical power into it while using a spell formula.”

Valentina nodded but added, “However…”

“Turning a race-specific technique into a magic tool… Wouldn’t that be difficult since the spell formula isn’t established?”

“There’s no need to worry about that. Even magical power usage methods not found in existing spell formulas can be recorded for incorporation into a magic tool by, for example, having Seraphina use her technique while I directly observe how she moves her magical power with Circulating Ki.”

Since it’s a magic tool, its actions become somewhat fixed, so it won’t be as free and versatile as Seraphina’s sound manipulation.

Output Irmhild’s Cursed Melody using a wind magic stone, and give it directionality using sound manipulation from a magic stone imbued with Seraphina’s characteristics… Yeah. The mechanism of the sonic cannon itself should be fine.

“…I see. So by sensing the flow of magical power with Circulating Ki, you can also see how to manipulate it. That’s a convenient thing.”

“Until now, we could research and record spell formulas… but the more we tried to do advanced things in the process of utilizing them, the more problems arose.”

Alfred nodded at my words.

“There’s also the issue of magic stone capacity, and it felt quite difficult to utilize them as magic tools.”

“Same with treating them as magic. Special techniques are meaningless with just the spell formula if the magical aptitude doesn’t accompany them.”

What proved practical were items like the Amulet of Evil Repulsion, for which we obtained established production methods from BFO… But even that is a consumable specialized for a single function—anti-curse magic—as a magic tool, and it shatters after blocking curse magic a few times. It’s undoubtedly excellent as countermeasure equipment, though.

“So, with the addition of the technology to change magic stone properties, various shackles have been removed.”

“That’s right.”

When I answered, Valentina smiled happily. The scope has broadened, so applying it should allow for various things.

“Surprisingly, old magic tools with unknown production methods might have been made that way.”

When Grace said that, Rosemary nodded.

“I see. In an era when more people could use Circulating Ki, it might have been possible to turn the unique skills of monsters or specific races into magic tools using the same method as Theodore…”

“…It’s only natural that valuable magic tool production methods would be kept secret. As a result, the methods also get buried.”

Old Sigmund widened his eyes in admiration at Rosemary and Claudia’s words.

“…Hmm. That line of thinking might be correct.”

“With the help of the labyrinth village residents, we might be able to create various magic tools.”

Somehow, a hypothesis was formed in an unexpected direction.

Ouroboros… At the very least, it’s certain that someone who could use Circulating Ki in its production was involved. It might be an item originating from the Seven Sages, but well.

“Well, it seems we’ve strayed a bit from the topic. Let’s return to the airship discussion.”

“Then… regarding the sonic cannon’s targeting?”

“Ah. We succeeded in an experiment on that. We managed to project the doll’s field of view onto a crystal ball. Just as Theo-kun said, when we thinly stretched Mithril Silver and directly connected the doll and the crystal ball, it solved the distance and capacity issues too. But… since what’s projected is spherical, it distorts a little.”

“Maybe making the crystal into a flat panel would be better.”

In short, it’s magical power transmission wires and a monitor panel. Since Alfred’s experiment succeeded, that should resolve the issues with the sonic cannon’s targeting and external monitors.

For long-range reconnaissance, I’d like to mount telescopic magic tools as well, but since those can be recorded as spell formulas, there shouldn’t be any particular problems with implementation.

“Next, we need a mechanism that can rotate a certain range up, down, left, and right.”

“That kind of mechanism… would be Viola’s jurisdiction, right?”

When Alfred broached the subject, Viola nodded.

“Leave that to me. Not just me, but we can also borrow the wisdom of Miriam-san and her master acquaintances. That kind of fine craftsmanship is a Dwarf’s specialty.”

Saying that, Viola lightly tapped her chest area. Mhm. That’s reassuring.

“What about the propulsion devices connected from the armor plates?”

“Normally, they take in air from the front to assist the Air Blast and expel air backward for propulsion. In emergencies, they use the magical power converted by the armor plates to mix fire magic expelled backward for instantaneous acceleration. When not in use, we can probably store it in as large a magic stone as possible.”

Sonic cannons, propulsion devices, and… many defensive devices.

Since we’re fighting demons, I’d like one more trump card… but if it’s a simple weapon, when it spreads, the people without countermeasures will be in trouble, so it’s quite difficult.

If defensive devices are fine, there are ideas like covering the ship’s surroundings with steam or illusions, or refracting light to make it invisible… If it can’t be seen visually, it would undoubtedly be powerful for reconnaissance.

Then, Elliot and Camilla returned.

“We’re back.”

“Welcome back.”

“Did you find a good property?”

“Yes. There was a quite good place very nearby.”

Camilla, asked by Ashley, exchanged smiles with Elliot, creating a harmonious atmosphere.

“We also ordered furniture. We’ve arranged for it to be delivered.”

“Once the inside is tidied up, please come see it.”

“Yes, definitely then.”

When it actually comes to moving… given Elliot’s position, it’s probably more prudent for appearances to wait until after marriage. Until then, I think it’s fine for him to stay at my house without hesitation. It hasn’t been that long since Elliot returned for Ashley either.

“Elliot’s house, a basement?”

Then Sheila asked. This is… not “Is there a basement?” but “Aren’t you making a basement?” right? She said it while making eye contact with me.

“We’ll make one if necessary, but…”

“Is that okay?”

Elliot’s expression brightened.

“Yes. If Elliot-san is fine with it. It’s not much trouble.”

“Since Camilla is here too, having one would be reassuring… May I ask you to do it?”

“Understood. Then let’s find some free time and do it later.”

“An alarm device would be good too. I’ll make it. If linked with a communication device, you’ll know immediately if something’s wrong no matter where you are.”

“Then we’ll need dolls for security too.”

Alfred and Rosemary also seemed enthusiastic about strengthening the security measures for Elliot’s house. Surprisingly, both seem to be getting carried away, thinking ‘might as well.’ Rosemary seems to be smiling, but she’s hiding her mouth with her feather fan.

“I shouldn’t just be protected all the time; I need to regain my senses so I can move when necessary.”

Camilla said. Like Elliot, Camilla seems to be a smallsword user… but she probably has a long gap since she last practiced. Hmm. Smallsword, smallsword.

“Will you train with Mihaela-san and the labyrinth village residents? Also, with aerial combat gear, you could escape by flying through the air if something happens.”

“That might be good.”

Elliot and Camilla nodded with bright expressions. Marlene was also smiling happily. Since she’s honing her smallsword skills with Mihaela, she might be pleased that the number of participants in training is increasing.

+++

# **320 – The White Airship**

The delivery of materials to the shipyard and the installation of equipment inside the facility seemed to be progressing at a rather rapid pace. The first day of training for the Demon-Slaying Knight Order arrived even before the furniture for Elliot’s new residence could be arranged.

After morning greetings to the members of the Demon-Slaying Knight Order lined up in the square, we began the training.

“…Well then. Since this is the first day, I’d like to start with the basic training content. Please look over there.”

I pointed toward Sheila, who was standing a short distance away in the square.

“Are you ready?”

“Mhm.”

Sheila nodded. Then let’s begin.

“First, the basics. We’ll start with running through the air using Magic Shields.”

Responding to my words, Sheila ran across the square while using the Magic Tool. Since it was Sheila, her movements were light, but she was only moving at a speed that could be considered a light jog.

“This is, well, the basic part. The purpose is to train Vitality and Magical Power consumption, and to get accustomed to handling Magic Tools.”

Knights can improve their Magical Power, and Magicians can enhance their Vitality.

“It’s simple, but it should be quite effective.”

I nodded at Elliot’s words. I had previously explained the training content to Elliot, as he is the Commander of the Demon-Slaying Knight Order.

“Yes. And once they become accustomed, instead of just using Shields, they will gradually progress to using Magic Tools like Levitation and Air Blast simultaneously. This will improve their ability to switch between Magic Tools quickly and accurately, aiming to reduce the time it takes to complete one lap around the training ground…”

As if matching my words, Sheila’s leaps with each step became larger and her speed increased. Although Sheila’s own movements hadn’t changed, by switching Magic Tools, the distance and speed of each step’s movement increased.

She was enhancing her jumping power after kicking off with Levitation and accelerating with Air Blast.

Since the Verdgar Knight Order had already introduced Aerial Combat Gear… some were marveling at the smooth switching between Magic Tool uses.

If one becomes proficient, Knights can compensate for lack of Magical Power with Vitality and Martial Arts, while Magicians can offset Vitality consumption by combining Levitation and Air Blast. It’s hard to say definitively which has an advantage or disadvantage.

“An advantage is that it’s easy to start with, and since there are several stages, the content can become more advanced according to each person’s proficiency. Ultimately, the goal is to be able to perform movements like what Sheila is doing now without breaking formation.”

When I said that, several people made thoughtful expressions. They were probably trying to gauge the Difficulty.

The final goal might seem quite challenging, but it’s only planar movement for aerial mobility. If the strength adjustment and switching of Magic Tool usage go well, it might be surprisingly easy.

Another merit is that because the content is simple, the Demon-Slaying Knight Order can continue training on their own even when I’m absent due to Labyrinth conquests, Demon countermeasures, research, and other errands.

When I’m present, it’s just a matter of direct guidance, but I anticipate being absent due to errands fairly often.

If training stagnates during that time, it would be problematic. So, I’m conveying the aerial combat training content in this manner.

That said, Elliot is in command, and the Knight Order members are highly motivated, so they’ll probably proceed actively.

“Irm, next training.”

The place where Irmhild was standing was crowded with colorful pillars of various kinds.

Perhaps it would be good to compare them to totem poles. They were color-coded by height, had different shapes drawn on them, and each one was unique. That is also training equipment. I went there early in the morning and created them using Wood Magic.

“The next basic training will use those densely standing pillars. This training is to get accustomed to three-dimensional movement and to develop instantaneous decision-making ability.”

This training is also simple. It can be done even when I’m absent, and it’s effective.

“Then, let’s begin. Irm. Red, square, triangle, yellow.”

Following my instructions, Irmhild twisted her body as she flew between the pillars, touching the colors and shapes. Even though I say ‘touch,’ it doesn’t necessarily have to be a direct touch. Irmhild swam-like to touch the indicated spots, but it’s also acceptable to use the pillars directly as footholds to jump to the next location.

Waiting for Irmhild to complete the instructions, I specified the next set of four types per set. She weaved between the pillars and responded. Moving in a rhythm similar to the instructions I gave, Irmhild seemed to be enjoying herself quite a bit.

I could make the instructions more complex, like “Red square, triangle, blue triangle, topmost white,” and so on.

Irmhild properly carried out my instructions. After having her complete several more sets, I gave the signal to end.

“Thank you, Irm.”

“That was pretty fun.”

That’s good to hear. Indeed, it might feel like a game. Turning back to the Knight Order, I said.

“As demonstrated, this training involves touching locations distinguished by color and pattern according to instructions. The key to performing it quickly is to change your posture in the air and use the target location itself as a foothold to move to the next spot. It’s training to cultivate three-dimensional movement and decision-making ability using Aerial Combat Gear.”

Since you’ll be moving to find the target location via the shortest distance, you’ll be moving up, down, left, and right between the pillars.

Ideally, you’d be able to move like a pinball, using the target spot as a foothold to move to the next—but well, expecting that much might be harsh.

We plan to proceed with other trainings, such as sparring in the air, methods of Coordination, and evasion methods assuming bullet hell with Miasma Bullets, and so on. Within that, we’ll probably include exercises with Golems.

“Today, first, please run through the air using Magic Tools. After that, we’ll take a break and then have a mock battle with Golems.”

“Then, regarding the running, I’ll leave it to you.”

Elliot nodded. So then… under Elliot’s supervision, the Knight Order members will run several laps around the shipyard square. Since inexperienced individuals can be identified by their movements, if there are any issues, I’ll provide advice later.

The Verdgar Knight Order, which already had widespread use of Aerial Combat Gear, seemed to be at a considerable standard. The other members, being a mix of elite Mage Corps and the Intelligence Unit from the magical superpower Silvatoria, were also moving quite well. Although there were some with awkward movements… as they repeated laps, their movements seemed to gradually improve.

Elliot, Chester, Mercedes, Elmer, Donovan, and others were at a very high level. Those who could use Magic were performing Levitation on their own, leaping with light steps.

In Elliot’s case, it should be relatively new for him… I guess this is a matter of Sense.

Well… it seems there’s no one who particularly needs advice. Since there are no problems with the basic movements, let’s have them run a bit more for training purposes.

“Then, shall we proceed with our work here?”

“It’s the construction of the Magic Array and preparation of Materials, isn’t it?”

I nodded at the words of Valentina and Old Sigmund.

Using Earth Magic, we created a foundation to place the ship and began drawing a Magic Array around it.

Using a powder made by mixing catalysts like crushed Magic Stones, alchemical solutions, and Magic Potions, we drew a Magic Array, creating a huge circle surrounding the foundation. There were small circles at the four directions. Placing the materials inside the small circles completes the preparation.

“Then—let’s begin.”

Taking a deep breath while gathering everyone’s attention. Circulation. Gathering Magical Power, amplifying it with Ouroboros. Following the Spell Formula taught by Old Sigmund, I deployed the Magic Circle.

As if responding, faint pillars of light rose from the five circles, both large and small.

Then, a pure white sphere of light was born at the center of the large middle circle. The materials placed in each of the four small circles were swept up and swirled within the white radiance. Melting, mixing together. It was as if they had been thrown into a crucible or a furnace.

Gradually, shaping that which was forming within the light—stretching it to take the same shape as the airship model.

Strongly, accurately, drawing the image. First, the keel. The part that would become the ship’s skeleton slowly extended lengthwise atop the foundation. Metal with the same texture as the white Golem I saw in Silvatoria spread out, taking clear form exactly as I envisioned.

From the keel to the hull armor. As the control grew more complex, the Magic Circle expanded. Indeed… the speed at which the materials mixed and were refined was slow. And it was a type of Magic that was difficult to control.

“At this speed—to process something of this size…”

“It’s astounding… Normally, several Magicians would divide the process roles…”

Stabilizing the lower structure, making it robust. Not releasing control.

Extend. Extend. As the materials from the four circles were drawn into the vortex of light and diminished, the ship’s exterior gradually revealed its form.

The ship’s sides—creating the main wings. The bow, the stern—and then to the deck. The Magic Circle had already expanded to a scale equivalent to an 8th-tier spell. Gripping Ouroboros tightly, thrusting it into the ground, increasing output with Circulating Ki.

The deck covered the upper part of the hull, and from the deck, the bridge grew upward as if sprouting. The outer shell was made as a single piece.

The circuits that guide Magical Power, the interior, etc., can be sufficiently handled later when building the ship, by using a Spell Formula to transition the Magical Power to a non-converted state.

The Magic Circle continued to expand, increasing its radiance. Both my body and Ouroboros, the heightened Magical Power from circulation scattered sparks around.

Closing my eyes, concentrating my consciousness while drawing the image. Finally, the Magic Circle expanded notably once more… and the upper part of the bridge was formed all at once.

“Haaah…”

After confirming that the whole structure was stable, I released the Spell Formula and let out a large breath. A feeling of fatigue remained from having refined and expended a considerable amount of Magical Power.

Taking a deep breath and opening my eyes, there was the ship, looking exactly like the model enlarged. Though when I say the ship’s form, it’s only the keel and outer shell.

Infusing Magical Power, I lightly tapped the hull. The received impact was converted into Magical Power, and a wave of light ran across the surface of the armor. Hmm… it seems to have gone well.

“To think—controlling the entire outer shell in one go without even pausing for breath…”

“I’m… at a loss for words.”

“I suppose we can only accept it, since it’s you, Sensei.”

Old Sigmund’s eyes were wide open, Valentina shook her head. Charlotte wore a strained smile.

Since making it a single piece would also enhance the Magical Power conversion ability… I really pushed myself. Perhaps because the scale of the Magic Circle, the vortex of light, and the completed airship’s exterior were unnecessarily flashy, the Knights had stopped in their tracks, eyes wide… but prompted by Elliot shaking his head, they resumed their laps.

“Well, at least the form is complete.”

“It’s a white, beautiful ship, isn’t it?”

Grace and Ashley looked up at the ship and smiled at each other. Marlene was also clapping happily together with Seraphina.

“Even though it looks like you made it easily… that was probably at the Difficulty level of an 8th or 9th-tier spell to control, wasn’t it?”

“…Only because your control ability is sufficient. It’s not something that can be made just by taking time.”

Rosemary, hiding a wry smile behind her feather fan, and Claudia, quietly closing her eyes.
