“Well… it’s just the outer shell. There’s nothing inside, and construction is from here on out.”

After this, when Alfred goes to process it, we’ll have to use Spell Formulas to control it so the armor’s Magical Power conversion doesn’t react.

Installing the core and propulsion. Placing Magical Creatures, running circuits connecting to the bridge’s Crystal Panel, placing Sonic Cannons here and there… and then covering such power sections and wiring with the interior as well. Cabins, corridors, the bridge, gun mounts… there’s quite a lot to do.

There was also talk about adding decorations to the exterior. The airship—we’ll gradually bring it closer to completion from here on.

+++

# **321 – Friendship and New Home**

“Guh!”

A knight who failed to dodge a Water Bullet and took a direct hit gritted his teeth as he fell downward. Another immediately moved to cover his position.

The Aqua Golem scattered Water Bullets at both the knight who moved in to replace him and the falling knight as it flew upward and away.

It was Elliot who dove straight in and retrieved the falling knight from the side. A barrage of Water Bullets passed through the space he’d just occupied.

“Over there!”

A blade of Fighting Spirit flew from the side and struck the Aqua Golem that had flown upward, hitting it directly. The one who launched the Fighting Spirit from a distance was Mercedes.

The Demon-Slaying Knight Order was conducting exercises against Golems, with Chester and Elmer also holding back several Golems… Their covering and follow-up for comrades who took hits and fell out of formation was swift.

I had the pinned Aqua Golems temporarily retreat backward, then overlap perfectly before charging at another knight. Elliot, watching from the side, seemed to notice the change in the Golems’ movements.

“The Golems’ movements have changed! Be very careful!”

At Elliot’s warning cry, the Aqua Golem charging straight at a knight swung its arm back in a wide arc. The moment the knight prepared to block, it broke away at the last second, dropping downward as if in free fall.

Almost simultaneously, the Golem behind it fired a Water Bullet from behind its body. This was the real attack.

“What!?”

He barely managed to block it with his shield. Only because he had heightened his alertness was he able to respond.

“Here I go!”

Chester, holding his spear at the ready from the side, charged forward. He pierced through the Aqua Golem, shattering it. It immediately reformed and lunged at Chester.

The members of the Demon-Slaying Knight Order are moving quite well. Then—let’s try increasing the coordination density of the Golems a bit more.

Meanwhile—preparations for the full moon Labyrinth by the Party members were proceeding in parallel. They were training against specially shaped Golems a short distance away.

These were Aqua Golems modeled after the forms of a Basilisk and a Cockatrice. The Basilisk had a magic light embedded in its head, and they were training to fight without looking directly at its light.

We do have options against monsters that use Petrification attacks, such as deploying Ignis to the front… but this is about having them fight properly in disadvantageous situations, assuming an unexpected encounter. The aim is to have them accumulate combat experience, albeit in a simulated form.

The Cockatrice Golem reproduced its Petrification Breath by having it spew mist from its mouth. They had to fight while ensuring they didn’t inhale or get covered by it.

“Over here.”

Sheila flew diagonally upward sideways, almost without looking forward, while drawing the Basilisk’s attention. The Basilisk Golem’s tail strike swept through the space where Sheila had been a moment too late.

Avoiding without looking at the opponent is something only Sheila, with her sharp senses, could do. Irmhild also has temperature sensing, so it’s a blessing that we can avoid being ambushed by these Basilisks and Cockatrices.

“How about this?”

Grace was facing the Cockatrice Golem. As the training Breath approached, Grace used the flat of her axe to create a gust of wind, pushing it back. Simultaneously, her other axe was thrown with tremendous force. It struck the Cockatrice Golem directly. Cockatrices are probably easier to handle compared to Basilisks.

Ashley, Marlene, Rosemary, and Seraphina generally don’t take the front lines… but well, they each have their own methods. Let’s continue the overall training at this pace.

“—Then, we will conclude today’s training. Salute to the Ambassador.”

As Elliot said this, the lined-up knights saluted while regulating their rough breathing. I returned the salute as well.

“Then, dismissed. Everyone, rest well and ensure you don’t carry fatigue into tomorrow.”

With Elliot’s words, they disbanded. They seemed to be heading inside the facility to change. The knight order members let out deep sighs of relief.

“Even after landing on the ground, I still feel like I’m spinning in the air…”

“Just when you think you’ve crossed blades with an upside-down opponent, they scatter Water Bullets as they pull away… What a dizzying battle.”

“Even considering that our opponents are Demons… it’s completely different from training among fellow knights.”

They exchanged impressions of the training while catching their breath.

“They’re conducting Labyrinth Exploration training at the same time as our training… We can only tip our hats to that…”

“Probably… the Golems’ movements will become even more severe. Theodore-dono still seems to have plenty of leeway.”

At Mercedes’ words, the others showed strained smiles.

Other topics emerged too, like whose movements were particularly sharp.

“As expected… the Commander’s movements were quite impressive.”

“Indeed… He truly lives up to being a Magic Knight who made a name for himself in Silvatoria.”

As for Elliot himself, he was quietly regulating his breathing. He seemed to have more Vitality to spare compared to the other knights. It’s a testament to his standing as Commander of the Demon-Slaying Knight Order.

“Well then… I think I’ll go to the hot spring afterward to wash off the sweat.”

“That’s a good idea. We can’t afford to carry fatigue into tomorrow.”

“If the Commander is going, we shall accompany you as well.”

It seemed the members of the Demon-Slaying Knight Order would go to the Fire Spirit Hot Spring with Elliot. If the hot spring helps with restoring energy and fostering camaraderie among the knights, that’s perfect.

“You’ve been sweating, so don’t forget to hydrate.”

“Understood.”

I had been careful to divide the Demon-Slaying Knight Order into several groups for rotating training and ensuring hydration during breaks… but since you sweat in the bath too, I hope they don’t forget about that. There’s a chance they might let their guard down just because training is over.

“Then… I should be back around lunchtime.”

“Yes. I’ll also contact Alfred.”

We had arranged to go see Elliot and Camilla’s new home after regrouping later. We had promised to create a safe room and install an Alarm Device.

Elliot’s new home was practically right next door—you could say it was just a stone’s throw away. It was directly across the street, separated by just one road.

A two-story house. For Elliot and Camilla, it was plenty spacious for the two of them.

Camilla’s father, Donato, apparently would return to his home in the Barony of Silun for the time being. His reasoning was that living in Termwills would be a hassle with the old fences, or so he claimed.

Donato apparently laughed, saying he’d just be in the way, and that they should spend time together as a couple alone.

Well, if we’re talking about the future, it seems the matter will be settled with Elliot becoming the lord, and then Elliot, Camilla, and Donato would relocate there.

“The white walls make for a lovely house.”

“Thank you. That’s what I liked about it.”

Ashley and Camilla exchanged smiles.

“Then, please come inside and look around.”

“Excuse the intrusion.”

Unlocking the door, we entered the house and looked around at the layout.

Living room, kitchen, bathroom, master bedroom, terrace. Several empty rooms. Plus a storage room. It seemed to have all the basics.

“Where should we make the entrance to the safe room?”

“Perhaps around the kitchen area?”

I see. That’s a place Camilla uses often.

“In terms of the layout, the kitchen is below the master bedroom, so it would be good if you could escape from the master bedroom too. How about creating a partition around this edge… and making a staircase to the basement behind it?”

“Having it from the bedroom is reassuring. You can escape even if attacked while sleeping.”

We proceeded to build it as decided through discussion with Elliot and Camilla.

In the kitchen, we installed a disguised dish cabinet made with Wood Magic against the wall. The mechanism was such that you could hide inside the bottom storage compartment, then slide the wall-side panel to enter the hidden passage.

The master bedroom was similar. A mechanism where you enter the bottom compartment of a disguised wardrobe and slide the floorboard to access the hidden passage.

Going down the hidden staircase led to an underground passage. Then the safe room… I transformed the soil into Golems to dig the hole and solidify the surroundings. All that remained was to create a passage from the safe room to the outside.

“I’ll bring the Dolls once they’re finished. They can be used for night watch and as makeshift servants.”

said Rosemary.

“That’s… very convenient.”

Camilla’s eyes widened.

They seemed useful in the workshop too; those Dolls are actually quite handy. According to Rosemary, the reason there were so many Dolls in the hideout she used to use was because she had the Dolls themselves produce parts and mass-produce them.

“Shall we install the Alarm Device after this is done?”

“Thank you.”

We drew Barrier lines just inside the fence and up to the entrance. It was a simplified Alarm Device that would sound a siren if anyone crossed the lines while the Magic Stone was inserted into the main unit.

It could primarily be used during nighttime sleep or when the house is empty.

Placing the main unit by the entrance allows you to turn the Alarm Device on or off when receiving guests. Before bed, you can activate it while locking up. Combined with the Dolls’ security, it should provide considerable protection.

Well, I suppose that covers the security setup for Elliot’s house.

+++

# **322 – The Source of Magic**

Between the Demon-Slaying Knight Order’s training, airship construction, countermeasures for the full moon labyrinth, and the modifications to Elliot’s new home, there are quite a few miscellaneous tasks to handle. Well, Elliot’s new home isn’t really work, though.

Other important tasks include passing on the Sealing Technique to Charlotte, and researching and deciphering the materials and ancient documents entrusted to us by Theoreme Castle and the Sages’ Academy.

So, I’m working on various things with everyone in the game room, spreading out documents. Rosemary continues deciphering the ancient documents borrowed from the royal castle. Old Sigmund and Valentina are deciphering the academy’s materials. Ashley is progressing with her healing magic research, while Marlene and Claudia maintain blessings to prevent the trap in the book that previously caught Rosemary from activating, I suppose.

Irmhild says she’ll focus on playing a Cursed Melody to reduce everyone’s fatigue. Seraphina will apparently be in charge of amplifying Irmhild’s Cursed Melody. As for me… I’m helping Charlotte inherit the Sealing Technique.

“…The chant for the basic spell formula is probably this form,” I finish reciting the incantation presumed to be the basic form of the Sealing Technique. Charlotte seems to be listening with a serious expression, trying not to miss a single word.

I added “probably” because the techniques Mother left behind, like the Attribute Seal and Magic Seal, are already applied forms. I pared down as much as possible from those and conveyed the extremely simple form to Charlotte earlier.

What to seal. And the method. This is what should be called the prototype of the spell formula, completely devoid of such meanings.

What purpose does it serve? It allows one to learn the basics of handling magical power in the Sealing Technique. Mastering this should lead to significant improvement in both the speed and precision of acquiring specific sealing techniques later.

Even if you try to learn applied spell formulas right away, there will be parts where you can’t fully grasp the flow of magical power, so understanding the simplest form helps with that.

“I see. By changing the details here and applying it, I’ll be able to seal various things.”

“Based on comparing several established sealing techniques and the flow of magical power, yes. Grace’s ring is like that too, as are the Magic Seal technique and other derivatives. I analyzed and separated the parts common to the basic system from those that aren’t.”

“…Thank you, sensei. First, I’ll train until I can deploy this spell formula as a Magic Circle.”

Charlotte seems to properly understand its significance and intent… She closes her eyes and repeatedly recites the incantation. She’s probably trying to accurately sense the movement of magical power through the chant.

Using incantation to move magical power is basic. Reproducing that magical power movement without incantation is Chantless. And finally, drawing a magic array with magical power to activate the spell formula leads to the Magic Circle. Charlotte is faithfully following this process to master the Sealing Technique.

“…Hmm. You call that the basic spell formula, but there’s a theory in the Academy that it’s a path leading to the abyss of magic.”

“Is that so?”

When I ask back, Old Sigmund laughs somewhat amusedly.

“Yes. Applied spell formulas are thought to be created by studying how other magics move magical power and adding flesh to the prototype.”

“I can understand that intuitively.”

“That’s right. Clear Blood and Roton Blood have completely opposite effects, but since they’re opposites, when you look at them as magical power usage or spell formulas, various aspects are similar.”

Ashley nods.

Indeed. Like Tempest Drive versus Vortex Drive, or Meteor Hammer versus Solid Hammer… There clearly exist spells of the same lineage.

With BFO, you could simply think of it as a higher-compatibility magic, but looking at the magical power movement, you can tell flesh has been added. That’s why there are parts we separate and manipulate through application.

“There were those who thought that by eliminating such additions, transcending even the barrier of prototype spell formulas… and tracing back to the extreme, the ultimate, lies the root that connects to everything.”

I see… It’s probably like discovering protons and neutrons, or the number zero.

“Extracting that prototype in the first place requires a fairly advanced understanding of magical power movement.”

Valentina says with a wry smile.

“Yes. Therefore, decomposing applied spell formulas and extracting the basic form from them has greater significance than you might think.”

“…That’s interesting. That idea of reaching the root. The spell formulas we use today were created by skillfully combining various prototypes and repeatedly improving them… Understanding prototypes could lead to creating new magic too.”

Rosemary says without stopping her deciphering work. Sitting beside Marlene while tracing the ancient document’s characters, Rosemary has an air of reading some story to her younger sister.

Intuitively, that’s probably right. Looking at current spell formulas from that perspective, they’re quite refined with no waste, and it’s not hard to imagine there were enormous numbers of trial and error before reaching their current forms.

“Thinking that way… I’m able to train as the Sealing Shrine Maiden in the best environment. I must thank the previous generation and sensei.”

“Yes. Do your best.”

“Yes!”

Charlotte nodded with a bright expression.

“Sorry to keep you waiting.”

Then Grace, Sheila, and Cecilia appeared in the game room carrying plates loaded with baked sweets. A fragrant aroma filled the game room. There’s cotton candy and shaved ice too, but freshly baked sweets are probably the best as tea accompaniments.

Grace and Sheila had excused themselves earlier, saying they’d make sweets since they’re not well-versed in magic or ancient documents… But for some reason, Sheila was wearing a maid uniform.

“Did you borrow it?”

“First, the form.”

Sheila says something like that in response to Irmhild’s question.

“That uniform is cute, isn’t it?”

“Shall I make the same one for Seraphina-chan to match?”

“Really?”

“Uh-huh. I like sewing.”

This conversation is between Seraphina and Claire of the Arachne.

“Well then, shall we take a short break?”

Claudia smiles happily watching this exchange. So let’s stop work for a while and have tea time.

After taking a break and refreshing ourselves, we resume work. Since Charlotte is doing repeated practice of the Sealing Technique, I work on bringing the environmental magic power absorption spell formula I’ve been researching closer to completion, with Mother’s notes in hand. The talk about prototypes and the spell formula for creating the airship’s outer shell might provide hints too. As I float a Magic Circle in my palm and try various things through trial and error, Rosemary spoke.

“Southern demons… What about this one?”

“Hm? Which one?”

What Rosemary had spread out wasn’t an ancient document, but something summarizing recent demon damage. She said she asked Alfred to bring several documents from the royal castle’s library. She was comparing a passage from it with a map.

“The King of Ignorance… A nameless demon, huh.”

It says it happened about 30 years ago. Not a name but an epithet. Like Death Sleep, since he’s called King, he’s probably a male demon.

“It says a dark sphere swallowed a country’s castle and scooped it out… According to survivor testimonies, it was a high-ranking demon that manipulated pitch-black darkness.”

“A demon that Gardinis recognizes as capable of opposing him… Then he’s undoubtedly a powerful demon.”

“That’s right. I think we could include him as a candidate based on strength alone… The problem is where the incident occurred.”

Rosemary’s finger traces the map while simultaneously opening the bookmarked section of another book, showing its description.

“This is the destroyed small country. And… apparently a deep forest spreads around this area on the map.”

“…This forest…”

The forest where the Duoveris Cult’s Sacred Land is said to be… from Prince Josiah’s story.

…The King of Ignorance, huh. If he’s a demon that appeared—or awakened—30 years ago, then from Gardinis’s perspective, he’s indeed a youngster.

We need to investigate whether there were similar abilities in past records, and whether the King of Ignorance rampaged elsewhere. But as a strong candidate for the leader of the demon group, this guy would probably come up first.

+++

# **323 – Dance of the Magic Bullets**

The summer was nearly over, and autumn was just around the corner. I felt like the comfortable days were increasing. We stood before the stone monument at the labyrinth’s entrance.

“Are you ready?”

Claudia, touching the stone monument, turned to ask us.

Since our preparations had progressed reasonably well, we decided to venture into the Full Moon Labyrinth. We needed to collect magic stones from the labyrinth’s monsters and advance the construction of the airship.

“Yeah. Let’s go.”

I nodded, looking straight at Claudia, and we were all enveloped in light.

When I opened my eyes—there was a spacious plaza made of white stone.

A broad corridor stretched ahead, with narrow passages extending to the right and left. Golden decorations and stone statues adorned the walls. Pure white pillars. Glowing crystals hanging from the ceiling served as lighting. It was magnificence you wouldn’t expect from inside a labyrinth.

And for good reason. The architectural style resembled Theoreme Castle. However, it was eerily silent, creating a quite different impression.

“So this is the Full Moon Labyrinth… It certainly does resemble the royal castle.”

Rosemary murmured as she looked around, having likely heard some rumors about the Full Moon Labyrinth. Marlene also blinked and surveyed the hall.

One reason it’s long been said that Theoreme Castle and the labyrinth are connected is this similarity in architectural style.

Now. Before proceeding deeper into the Full Moon Labyrinth, let me give a brief explanation.

“First… the narrow passages connected from both sides lead to a maze with shifting structures. There are many relatively small monsters, and the difficulty is apparently significantly lower compared to the front side. Normally, you should collect the transference stones before heading to the front.”

The same applies if you accidentally wander in. The basic approach would be to proceed through the maze side rather than the front, then return to the hall’s stone monument and leave. While the maze side’s difficulty is still considerable, it’s much better than advancing through the main corridor at the front.

“Since Claudia-sama is with us, we can proceed through the front… is that it?”

“Correct. Our objectives are strengthening our combat capabilities and collecting magic stones, so we won’t delve too deep.”

While conquering the Full Moon Labyrinth is a future goal, fighting monsters in the labyrinth itself contributes to strengthening our forces. Well then, let’s proceed.

Leaving the hall, the spacious corridor continued deeper and deeper in a gentle curve. The corridor had a slight incline, structured to spiral downward. Giant pillars stood at equal intervals to the left and right—but that was about it for cover. Basically, there was nowhere to hide or detour.

Ignis took the lead. I also moved to the front.

Following behind Ignis, Sheila, Irmhild and Seraphina, and Grace followed, almost hiding behind Ignis.

The formation continued with Rosemary, Ashley, Marlene and Dullahan. Claudia and Eclair. Lavigne brought up the rear. While the terrain prevented flanking attacks, the familiars would serve as defense for the rearguard. Caduceus was in the middle of the formation.

“…Something big is coming.”

“There are others too… but I don’t think they’re Basilisks or Cockatrices.”

After advancing a short way down the main corridor, Sheila and Irmhild stopped and voiced their caution.

From beyond the gentle curve, giant silhouettes tall enough to reach the main corridor’s ceiling appeared. Their numbers: one… two.

One was a Troll. The other was a Cyclops—a one-eyed giant—armed in armor. Gripping an iron club, it looked our way and roared. The air vibrated intensely.

Accompanying the two large figures were numerous Lesser Demons. Compared to the Flame Demons we saw before, their bodies were slimmer and much smaller. Though lower-class, they were a type of demon. They were more dangerous than they looked. Flapping their wings near the corridor’s ceiling, each held a trident spear.

Running past the Troll and Cyclops at their feet was a pack of saber-toothed tiger-like beasts. But they had wings on their backs. They were Storm Fangs, large carnivorous beasts.

This was the Full Moon Labyrinth’s first baptism. Adventurers who entered unknowingly would likely see such an army approaching and have to run back up the main corridor.

As for Basilisks and Cockatrices… they didn’t seem to be mixed in. But Sheila and Irmhild remained vigilant against the approaching enemies.

“I’ll handle the air. Sheila and Irm, maximum caution against monsters with petrification abilities. Priority over attack.”

“Mm. Understood.”

“Leave it to me!”

I faced the Demons flying up through the main corridor’s airspace toward us.

“I’ll take that Cyclops. Go, Ignis.”

“Then—I’ll take the other one.”

Grace shot out in front of the formation like a bullet. Ignis, following Rosemary’s orders, followed suit.

“Forming a defensive position!”

Ashley constructed a Defense Field.

Once the Defense Field formed, Ashley mounted Lavigne, and Marlene mounted Dullahan’s horse, each securing mobility. Then Caduceus would guard Rosemary.

The roaring Troll swung its iron club down with brute force. Grace, who should have been overwhelmingly outmatched in size, met it head-on. The sound of clashing metal rang out, and both weapons recoiled backward.

Ignis too. Matching the Cyclops’s attack, it slammed its War Hammer. Both Grace and Ignis, facing the Troll and Cyclops, didn’t retreat a step, fiercely exchanging blows. Their weapons collided, heavy metallic sounds echoing through the main corridor. Just as Claudia said. Against enemies relying on strength, meet them with strength. Claudia had inferred that this would be sufficient to counter them, and that was proving correct.

Slipping past a wide swing, an Axe swept across its flank. Slash Attacks carved into its body—but they closed up instantly, repairing themselves.

“Regeneration ability—is it?”

Grace frowned upon seeing this.

Storm Fangs swarmed the defensive position Ashley built from all directions. Blocked by the Defense Field, they twisted their snouts in regardless, trying to force their way through. Fighting Spirit erupted all over their bodies as they attempted to break through the field by force.

Lavigne easily evaded the slowed Storm Fang’s claw strike and scattered ice bullets together with Ashley. Attacks that normally couldn’t be avoided were deflected and scattered by the wind armor surrounding the Storm Fangs.

A ferocious beast that appears with storms. Hence the name Storm Fang. However, carelessly pursuing Ashley, its upper body was swallowed by an ice wall rising from below, immobilizing it.

“Futile.”

An ice block the size of an embrace smashed down on the immobilized winged tiger. Ashley, riding Lavigne, swung an ice-clad Mace as they passed by.

The Storm Fangs heading for Marlene—couldn’t even reach her. Attempting an attack revealed an illusion created by the Lantern. Even trying to chase the real one, Saucers flew from left and right, preventing them from closing the distance.

Eclair approached, hiding behind the Saucers’ shadows. As it stopped moving from taking lightning, Dullahan’s Greatsword strike swept upward from below, clearing them away.

The Storm Fang that leaped at Rosemary from the air was stuck, unable to move in an unnatural shape. It had charged straight into a Trap deployed with magical strings, getting entangled.

Rosemary sprayed a Sleep Cloud over its face, robbing it of consciousness, and smiled faintly.

“I’ll borrow your back for a bit.”

Magical strings extended from Rosemary’s left hand too. Taking over the entangled Storm Fang in the air with Puppet Strings, she straddled its back.

Bundling the Puppet Strings like reins in her left hand, she rode the Storm Fang as she pleased. In her right hand, she held the Wand obtained from the Blazing Fortress last time.

She lunged at another winged tiger. The targeted tiger barely dodged the attack from the tiger Rosemary rode, but then Rosemary swung the Wand.

A shockwave of light, like the trajectory of a slash, flew forth. Direct hit. Explosion. The struck winged tiger was sent flying backward.

“It’s quite easy to use, this one.”

Rosemary smiled faintly at the Wand’s usability. It was probably an easy-to-handle tool without quirks, suitable for a magician’s self-defense. She could leave the sphere of light there as is, using it for interception too.

“Irmhilt, to your right.”

“Yes!”

Irmhilt floated as if covering each other’s backs. Following Sheila’s warning, she aimed her Bow and fired an arrow. Without even looking, the fired arrow pierced the tiger’s forehead perfectly. Probably because she completely tracked the enemy’s movements with temperature sensing. So aim and shoot, and it hits. Against monsters slowed by the Defense Field, they couldn’t avoid Irmhilt’s arrows.

Sheila and Irmhilt kept a certain distance from the enemies. When one fought, the other rested, allocating awareness to detection.

They bore the role of staying alert for newcomers to the battlefield, checking if Basilisks or Cockatrices were among them. Seraphina, riding on Irmhilt’s shoulder, played a flute, and something like white wolves danced around the three. It was a flute that summoned and controlled guardian beasts. They bit into the limbs of Storm Fangs charging in, and either Sheila or Irmhilt delivered the Finishing Blow.

As for me—I was dealing with the swarm of Lesser Demons, dancing through the air. Some Storm Fangs charged up from below—but drawing large numbers was exactly what I wanted.

“Come—!”

I avoided a trident spear thrust from behind with a spinning Cartwheel. Balor, having become a Light Bullet, shot out from my shadow and pierced through the Lesser Demon’s torso. Maintaining momentum, I swung Ouroboros, scattering pale blue sparks, and swung it at the Storm Fang’s face as we passed. Its long canine teeth shattered.

We were outnumbered—but. I kept my stance ready to respond from any direction—using Nemea and Capella to fly left and right. Right beside my body, Balor, now a bullet of light, orbited like a satellite. Leaving behind the flames spat by Demons and the air bullets fired by Storm Fangs, it spun, and spun.

Shattering the attacking Lesser Demons and Storm Fangs with Ouroboros, piercing through with shockwave strikes, tearing with Nemea’s Claws. Then shooting through the downed ones with Balor.

Like insects swarming a moth-burning lamp and falling scorched, the monsters fell one after another.

There was a change in Grace and the others’ battle situation too.

Perhaps frustrated at having its attacks consistently repelled, the Troll tried to grab Grace with its bare hands. But that was probably a poor choice.

Grace shifted her stance to avoid it and erupted with Fighting Spirit from her entire body. Instead, she grabbed its wrist and slipped past its side. Running up into the air, using that momentum to snap the Troll’s arm off, she grabbed the wrist with both hands and swung it with a sharp cry. Where it landed—was the main corridor’s stone pillar.

“Take this!”

Using centrifugal force, she slammed the Troll’s skull from behind into the stone pillar. The shattering sound—was it from the pillar or the Troll? The Troll, sunk into a pile of rubble, didn’t get up.

Ignis too. Rosemary, riding a winged tiger, rushed over from behind and threw something from her Magic Bag, causing an explosion right in front of the Cyclops. It seemed fragments of a flask stabbed into its eyeball.

Leaping up at the staggered Cyclops holding its face, Ignis hooked its claws into it. A Pile Bunker detonated with the blast. It shattered the armor the Cyclops wore in one blow, piercing through its torso.

Hmm… The first battle in the Full Moon Labyrinth went reasonably well, I’d say. I moved around using Balor too, and it went pretty much as I imagined.

+++

# **324 – Golden Hunger Wolf**

After dealing with the monsters, I checked our situation.

“Any injuries?”

“We’re fine here.”

“Mm. No problems.”

“I’m alright too.”

Marlene also smiled when our eyes met. Yeah. Seems like there’s no problem.

The Storm Fangs had been charging recklessly regardless of our defensive positions due to their ferocity… but their movements had slowed and we managed to repel them well enough.

Now then… While having Sheila and Irmhild continue keeping watch, let’s start harvesting materials. Having repelled the first wave, we had quite a substantial amount of materials.

“What should we harvest?”

“For Storm Fangs, probably their fangs and fur. They’re materials that work well with Wind Magic, so I think they’ll fetch a pretty good price.”

From the Lesser Demons, we got a large quantity of fairly decent quality Magic Stones. We also extracted Magic Stones from the Troll and Cyclops. We collected the weapons the Troll and Cyclops had been using too. The Magic Stones from those two are of decent quality but…

“They’re still somewhat… lacking, wouldn’t you say?”

Rosemary said, looking at the Magic Stone in my hand.

“Yeah. Well… they’re not big catches like Flame Demons.”

We’ve obtained Magic Stones of sufficient Level to use in the Sonic Cannon, and they’re more than enough to contribute to the airship construction, so I shouldn’t be too greedy.

“What lies ahead from here?”

“For a while, it continues spiraling downward. We can’t avoid combat… but the structure is such that the Grand Corridor’s endpoint leads to a gate.”

When Grace asked, Claudia answered like that.

For now, let’s have the spoils sent outside.

And so, working quickly… after finishing the harvesting, as we proceeded further and further down, Sheila and Irmhild stopped.

“Enemies?”

“Probably enemies. They came out from behind the pillars. Not Basilisks or Cockatrices.”

“Humanoid… They’re slowly approaching us. This is—that monster we discussed.”

Irmhild took a stance with her Bow and, without hesitation, fired an arrow into space that appeared empty.

The sound of something kicking off the floor echoed. It must have dodged the arrow.

But before it could land, Irmhild’s second arrow, fired in rapid succession, caught it mid-air. The Light Arrow pierced the empty space, and a high-pitched scream rose.

An invisible monster. With an arrow in its throat, it revealed its form, tumbling across the Grand Corridor floor while scattering rainbow-colored bodily fluids. It writhed for a while but eventually stopped moving. A monster with skin possessing a strange, pearl-like luster.

It’s humanoid… but the shape of its arms is different. The parts from the elbows forward are like Katanas.

“Invisible Ripper. An invisible monster.”

The enemies requiring caution in the Full Moon Labyrinth aren’t just Basilisks and Cockatrices. For Full Moon Labyrinth countermeasures, we’ve prepared for other monsters we felt necessary to address.

Invisible Rippers possess the property of being unseeable during their activity. They’re quite nasty monsters that sneak up while transparent and slash you. They can’t fly but have high jumping power… even if you’re in the air, they’ll likely deliver Slash Attacks. That said, they don’t have much durability, and since we have Dragon Scale Armor, they probably can’t inflict serious wounds on us.

Well, Irmhild’s temperature sensing is effective, and it seems they can’t fool Sheila or Lavigne’s senses either. Even if someone else deals with them, there are countermeasures like generating mist or using wide-area attacks, so as long as we know they’re there, they’re not that scary of an opponent.

“What do you think about facing them? If they mix into a chaotic battle, can you handle them?”

Though we’re relying on Sheila and Irmhilt for detecting Invisible Rippers too.

“They have a unique smell. I’ll know even if they mix in.”

“They have body temperature but are invisible, so the incongruity stands out.”

Hmm. Seems like it won’t be a problem with these two.

“If there’s no problem, we’ll handle them.”

“Understood.”

The harvesting point from Invisible Rippers was those arms, huh? I hear if you channel Magical Power through them, you can create blades that become invisible. Ah—If we circulate them, that could be dangerous. Maybe it’s better to have the workshop process them and give them to Sheila.

As we proceeded downward while scattering the attacking Lesser Demons, Storm Fangs, and Invisible Rippers, Sheila and Irmhild stopped again.

Then, spreading their arms sideways to halt everyone’s movement, they said in tense voices.

“…Coming. Two large monsters…!”

“The shape of their body heat… probably a chicken. A lizard is coming a bit later.”

Just as Irmhild said.

From ahead in the Grand Corridor, a giant rooster’s comb peeked into view. Immediately, to block the view from high places, the dark Spirit Shade summoned by Marlene spread out a pitch-black space. The darkness created by Shade is one of our measures against Basilisks. We considered various methods like reflections and such, but ultimately, we just need to prevent eye contact. As the curtain of darkness spread, only the giant chicken feet and snake tail became visible near the floor level.

Slightly later, the Basilisk also seemed to appear from beyond the curve. The bipedal giant lizard’s legs and tail followed the Cockatrice. If it were just them, we could charge in and crush them as is, but—

“Invisible Rippers are coming too. Multiple of them.”

“We’ll handle them!”

As expected, they came along with other small fry. It’s better to have fewer uncertain elements in a battle against two major monsters. We’ll deal with the small ones first.

“Don’t go beyond the darkness. If there are too many to handle completely, it’s fine to let some flow over to us.”

“Mm.”

“Yes!”

“Then, Ignis will handle the Basilisk.”

Ignis, having received the order from Rosemary, charged into the darkness beyond. As Marlene raised her Ritual Rapier, Dullahan headed toward the Cockatrice.

Both have Resistance to Petrification. Ignis, being a Doll, is unaffected by petrifying gazes, and petrifying breath or petrifying beaks—poisons of that sort—don’t work on Dullahan. If necessary, I’ll have Balor fly out from here for support.

We can attack if we can see the foot positions, but we can’t have Balor open its eye… so we need to be very careful to ensure Ignis and the others aren’t in the line of fire.

“Grace, defend the Rearguard. Marie, don’t go to support Ignis either.”

“Yes!”

“Understood. I’ll focus on support from the rear.”

Marlene used the Lantern to create illusions of Ignis and Dullahan and had them charge at the Basilisk and Cockatrice.

For the third time, battle commenced in the Grand Corridor.

Sheila and Irmhild danced in the darkness. For the two of them, Shade’s darkness is no obstacle at all. Sheila glided flying low to the ground, wielding her Pearl Sword, and as Irmhild fired Light Arrows into empty space, Invisible Rippers fell one after another.

“Three! They slipped past to the rear!”

I know their positions. Because Ashley spread water on the floor. The Invisible Rippers stepped into the water surface. And there—.

“Grind Dust!”

A composite Magic of wind and earth. Hardened sand swirled into a war wheel, mowing down the general space where the Rippers probably were.

Rainbow-colored blood splattered around. Eclair’s Lightning Strike spread across the water’s edge, and one was scorched black. Two leaped and closed in on us. The Rippers, covered in fine wounds all over their bodies, were no longer invisible monsters.

“There they are.”

Grace’s Axe was unleashed with tremendous force, smashing the Ripper that was in mid-air.

The other one charged headlong into a Trap made of Rosemary’s Magic Threads, had its body sliced apart, and was then Penetrated by an ice bullet fired by Lavigne.

Next—the Basilisk and Cockatrice. Judging from the foot movements, Ignis and the Basilisk seem to be clashing with War Hammer and Claws. The scales are quite tough too.

The Cockatrice and Dullahan… seem to be flapping their wings and soaring into the air. Given that I can hear the sound of hooves galloping through the sky, they appear to be engaged in aerial combat. The Cockatrice’s beak seems to be quite strong too. I can hear the sound of Greatsword and beak colliding.

I charged Balor with Magical Power, increasing its power through circulation. The target should be—the Cockatrice. When it lands on the ground, I’ll blow its legs off before it crosses paths with Dullahan next.

“Wait. This is…!”

Then Claudia put a hand to her forehead and frowned.

“From below—a Guardian is climbing up at an incredible speed!”

Guardian… Coming here now.

“I’ll handle that one.”

Saying that, I fired the Magic Bullet without hesitation. Balor, transformed into a Light Bullet, Crushed the Cockatrice’s leg in a single strike. The Cockatrice, tumbling as it fell, had its chicken face turn this way. A face of shock. There, a Greatsword was swung down and its head was lopped off. I checked the foot positions of the Basilisk and Ignis. Balor drew a sharp-angled trajectory, reflecting off something to strike the Basilisk from the side. It’s the second shot, but—I don’t need to Penetrate. It’s enough if I distract the Basilisk for a moment.

Ignis’s step-in. Into the spot where Balor’s strike had landed, Ignis’s War Hammer blow was driven home. A sound like something shattering echoed, and the Basilisk’s legs stumbled.

Before I could confirm the Basilisk’s fall—something flew out from beyond the darkness, whipping up wind.

With golden shining body hair—it was a bipedal wolf. Tracking its movement with my peripheral vision, my eyes met its. I immediately charged toward it. It caught Ouroboros’s strike with its Claws wrapped in Fighting Spirit.

“Werewolf Origin (Origin) ——! Marlene! A Blessing!”

Claudia, having identified the Guardian’s type, said in a slightly urgent voice. As Marlene made a gesture of prayer, a Blessing enveloped our bodies.

Werewolf Origin. Those who were like that from birth. An ancient race said to have spread the Werewolf’s Curse throughout the human world.

In BFO, I heard information from a scholar NPC who deciphered Ancient Documents, but… is this that?

Using a Blessing is probably so that even if bitten, we won’t contract the Werewolf’s Curse. I see. With this, we can fight to our heart’s content.

The Werewolf showed movements as if trying to crush us with brute force, paying no heed to the Blessing.

I relaxed my strength, Parried, and performed a Form Shift. I flicked up the opposite end of Ouroboros toward its jaw, and the Werewolf, spinning greatly, leaped back to Dodge. It stayed airborne as if treading the sky.

It grinned. It bared its fangs and showed a ferocious smile. Excellent. A worthy opponent.

+++

# **325 – Claws of the Greedy Wolf**

We faced each other in midair, circulating and refining our magical power through continuous cycles.

Its grin widened further—it let out a long, drawn-out howl. A beast’s cry that stretched higher and higher. Mixed within it were joy and ecstasy. As if signaling the end of that howl, one of us moved—though it was impossible to tell who initiated first.

Combining Levitation with the power of Nemea and Capella, I stepped in at maximum speed from the initial movement. The gleam of magical power and fighting spirit left afterimages in the air as we crossed paths. Claws wrapped in fighting spirit clashed with Ouroboros imbued with magical power, scattering sparks.

I wasn’t deflected. The werewolf received the blow at a perfect angle, allowing its body to flow with the impact. Without resisting, it accelerated into a cartwheel. A moment later, a claw strike aimed at my neck left a golden trajectory in the empty air.

I immediately reversed direction, kicking off a Shield to rebound. We turned to face each other almost simultaneously. As we passed, we exchanged attacks.

We flew through the grand corridor, weaving through it as we crossed paths countless times along sharp-angled trajectories, clashing staff against claws and leaving sparks in our wake. This was high-speed combat without reducing velocity. Our encounters lasted only an instant. We traded slash attacks and strikes.

But I couldn’t let my guard down against just its fangs and claws. While it deliberately drew my attention upward by dramatically raising its right arm, a knee strike wrapped in fighting spirit shot up from directly below like a cannonball. I avoided it by a hair’s breadth with a Form Shift, simultaneously delivering a horizontal sweep with Ouroboros, but this was blocked by its free left arm.

We passed each other and faced off from a distance. The werewolf remained stationary as if standing firm on the air, now showing a stance like that of a Fighter—perhaps having decided there was no need to hide its capabilities after the failed ambush.

I had known since our initial exchange… it seemed to possess genuine intelligence and close-quarters combat skills. I had to be wary not only of its claw-based slash attacks but also strikes and throws.

What remained unclear was—the principle by which it remained suspended in midair. It wasn’t deploying Shields like me, nor was it flying like the demons. It simply ran through the air as if treating it as solid ground.

That was—similar to how Dullahan’s horse galloped through the air. Or perhaps it was closer to being a Spirit.

I stepped in. Unlike before, we didn’t pass each other but stopped to exchange techniques.

I deflected its attacks with my staff and Shield, then repaid the favor by sweeping with the Dragon Staff. It too parried the trajectory of my strikes with its fighting spirit-enhanced body. Right arm and left leg. It scattered my attention diagonally while launching consecutive claw-based slash attacks and kicks. The leg that should have passed by instead traced a right-angled path downward. A heel drop with enough power to shatter my skull if it connected.

But it cut through empty air. What the werewolf had caught was an illusion created by Mirage Body. I drove Ouroboros into its flank, but the response felt unnaturally solid for a flesh-and-blood body.

Its fighting spirit-enhanced body hair seemed to function as sturdy armor. Combined with its speed and physical strength, even a grazing touch became a weapon capable of shredding flesh. I avoided it by the thinnest margin, but my cheek was lightly cut by its body hair. Dodging too widely would reduce the power of my counterattacks. I accepted this as necessary.

At this rate, Nemea and Capella would struggle to land effective attacks. I also wanted to avoid taking damage from that body hair. I positioned the lion and goat as support for aerial mobility. Balor had also used up considerable magical power after firing at two large targets. There was no point in forcing them back—I would just have to see this through.

The second illusion wouldn’t work. Whether through smell or hearing, it accurately identified my position and launched a spinning back kick. I blocked the kick with a Shield while countering with a shockwave attack. But using the momentum of the deflection, it spun its body and brought its claws down from directly above in a high stance. Claws wrapped in fighting spirit couldn’t be blocked by half-hearted Shields, and retreating would prevent counterattacks. I drew it in until the last possible moment, evading by a hair’s breadth. A slash attack that embodied pure destructive power swept past right beside my body. Had its wire-like body hair grazed me again? A slight pain ran through me.

But I had closed the distance. The exterior was impregnable. Then the interior must be—

I concentrated magical power in my palm, twisting it into a spiral, and drove a magical shockwave into an area with thinner fur. The werewolf’s expression twisted slightly, and its massive frame was sent flying backward. I deployed a Magic Circle. It was at an unavoidable range.

“Solid Hammer!”

I slammed a mass of rock toward the flying werewolf. Seeing this, the werewolf took a deep breath and planted itself firmly in place.

Its upper body swelled. Then came the release of power. It was a roar. The roar transformed into a directional shockwave that collided with the Solid Hammer. They canceled each other out. We both charged through the finely shattered rock fragments.

Breath-taking distance. Ultra-close combat. Gripping the Dragon Staff midway, I launched strikes from both sides, while it responded to the short range with elbow strikes and knee strikes.

Then, perhaps showing why it was a werewolf, it opened its jaws wide as if to swallow my head whole and tried to bite down. The sound of fangs clashing echoed right by my ear. No problem. I avoided it.

Palm strike. But this time it seemed to have anticipated it, blocking with its upper arm concentrated with fighting spirit. Having expected the shockwave impact, it swept my arm aside forcefully, resulting in both of us being blown backward.

As if returning the favor from earlier, the werewolf pulled its arm far back. More fighting spirit than ever before swelled up, concentrating in its drawn-back right arm. A shudder. A chilling thrill ran through me along with goosebumps. I leaped high upward, matching its movement.

“Ooooh!”

A spirited shout that could tear silk. A claw strike that seemed to tear space itself apart. An enormous amount of fighting spirit became five overlapping giant slash attacks that roared as they swept through the space I had occupied moments before. The stone pillar behind was cleanly sliced through.

Tremendous destructive power—but an attack that misses is meaningless. Paying no mind to each other, we charged forward like arrows from our jumped positions.

I clashed with the Dragon Staff wrapped in lightning. A lightning strike that should scorch and paralyze any living creature it hits instead scattered across the fur covering its body surface. Fireballs and ice spears were equally ignored. It burst through explosions and shattered ice spears by concentrating fighting spirit. It emphasized durability, breaking through with brute force.

It attempted to crush me through sheer power, and when I deflected it with a Shield, it flowed with the motion without resistance, releasing a fighting spirit slash attack as we separated. I avoided it with a cartwheel. The sky and ground swapped dizzyingly as we were repelled left and right, clashing countless times. I landed several strikes. I hit it with numerous spells. There must have been damage, but it ignored everything and unleashed countless techniques as if determined to tear me apart if they connected.

High-level techniques, an unyielding instinct for combat, and durability that allowed it to get away with recklessness. Then—

I deployed multiple Magic Circles. Solid Hammer and Mirage Body. The illusion flew in the opposite direction from me, but it accurately pursued my true body. I launched rocks from the front, then stepped in using them as shields.

The werewolf showed its intention to intercept the incoming rocks with another roar. Fighting spirit in both arms—it probably planned to intercept my true body with the fighting spirit wrapped around both arms. The released shockwave shattered the rocks—it prepared to meet me as I broke through the shattered fragments—when a rock projectile flying from the side struck its temple directly. Only the rock carried by the illusion side was real (……..).

I had deployed multiple Solid Hammers for both the main body and illusion side, firing rocks in a cross pattern.

A trap made possible precisely because it could accurately discern my true position. I deliberately let the rock fired from the front be shattered. Sound and smell. A diversion against both senses. As a result, an attack from an unexpected angle connected. I had chosen a rock strike that could transmit shock to the interior more easily, even if blocked by the fur.

The werewolf widened its eyes in shock, still in its roaring posture. Before it could comprehend the nature of the attack from the side, I released another spell aimed into its wide-open mouth.

“Shatter!”

Fire and earth composite 7th-tier magic—Mine Explode.

An explosion erupted before the werewolf’s face. A composite magic of fire and earth. Generation of rock masses. And explosion. The blast and fragments swallowed and tore through its face.

It staggered and began to fall. Even while bleeding from the corners of its clenched mouth, the werewolf didn’t stop fighting. Its eyes still overflowed with fighting spirit. Even while falling, it released a giant claw attack from its right arm.

Was that—its final desperate effort? If I created distance, perhaps the werewolf would exhaust itself immediately. But I wouldn’t let it counterattack. I wouldn’t let it suffer needlessly either. I would properly—deliver the finishing blow.

I dove headfirst toward it. Slipping through the gaps between the five overlapping claw strikes, I closed in on the werewolf. I concentrated all my magical power into the very tip of Ouroboros’s horn.

“Pierce!”

My voice overlapped with Ouroboros’s roar. I thrust Ouroboros like a spear through the werewolf’s left chest. Spiral shockwave. The narrowly focused magical power pierced the werewolf’s heart. The werewolf and I fell to the ground as one mass.

Leaving behind a blue magical afterglow, we fell straight down like lightning. It effortlessly pierced through the sturdy exterior and stabbed down as if nailing it to the ground. Upon impact, cracks ran across the grand corridor’s floor.

I disengaged, spun once, and landed a short distance away. I had pierced its heart. Would it still stand or not? The werewolf stretched its claws toward me even while spitting up blood. But—the fighting spirit was fading.

The corners of its mouth twisted as the werewolf smiled. Its eyes closed, the strength drained from its outstretched arm—and it moved no more.

+++

# **326 – Original Species Magic Stone**

After confirming the defeat of the Werewolf original species, I let out a deep breath. As the battle ended, Ashley and the others approached.

“Theodore-sama, healing magic please.”

“Mmm… Thank you, Ashley.”

I returned a smile to show my injuries weren’t serious, and Ashley smiled back with some relief and nodded.

It seemed I’d gotten some minor cuts on my cheeks and such while dodging its attacks. And probably some light abrasions from the fur when I delivered the palm strike. They were indeed minor injuries, so Ashley’s healing magic would close them right up. They probably wouldn’t even leave scars. The glow of healing magic was applied to my cheeks and palms.

“Are you alright, Theo?”

“Yeah. I don’t think the wounds are that bad.”

“While it’s reassuring that you only suffered light injuries fighting that thing, watching it was still bad for my heart.”

Rosemary closed her eyes while hiding her mouth behind her feather fan. Ah. That’s probably because I charged right into its fighting spirit slash attacks.

“Well, I do feel bad about that part,” I said with a wry smile, and Rosemary turned away.

Now then. With my wounds healed, let’s proceed with the extraction.

First, I held my hand over the werewolf and deployed a magic circle. A dazzling glow gathered over its chest, growing increasingly brighter—until it eventually crystallized into a magic stone.

Huh? …Rather than extraction, it seems the Guardian’s entire body was converted into a magic stone…

“…It appears the Guardian responded to Theodore’s spell formula. Since the Werewolf original species is close to spirits, that’s probably within its capabilities,” Claudia said after seeing this.

“Hmm? Why would it respond to my spell formula?”

“Maybe it took a liking to you? Guardians by nature possess stronger free will than ordinary labyrinth monsters… Well, the Last Guardian is completely inflexible, so that’s a bit different though.”

…I see. Looking at the completed magic stone again… this is quite large.

It has the appearance of a crystal wrapped in golden phosphorescence. A magic stone’s performance is determined by its quality and size. Since capacity increases exponentially in some aspects, it’s not simply a matter of gathering more stones.

But with this, it should be more than sufficient for airship construction.

As for our spoils: Basilisk and Cockatrice. Plus numerous Invisible Rippers.

I feel like we have an excess inventory of Ripper arms… If we can’t find uses for them, we can always extract them later.

“I’ll handle the extractions from the Basilisk and Cockatrice too. Since the Evil Eye’s magical power is still active, I’d feel more at ease if Shade could cover them with darkness during the process.”

Marlene nodded firmly, and darkness gathered around the Basilisk, completely covering it.

Now then… let’s proceed with the extraction.

We’ve collected all the materials we needed. We cut short our exploration of the Full Moon Labyrinth at a reasonable point, and since we had surplus items from what we collected, we went to have the Adventurer Guild purchase them. Mainly Stormfang fangs and pelts.

“Um, this is… Stormfang pelts, I assume? Don’t tell me… the Full Moon Labyrinth?”

“That’s right. We had some extra so we brought them. We do have means to enter the Full Moon Labyrinth,” I replied to Heather, whose expression had stiffened and voice had grown quiet.

“Hmm… Well, given it’s something you all would do… I suppose I’ll just have to accept it. We’ll hold these in temporary storage and display them around the day after the full moon,” she said with a dry laugh. There were probably various points she could question, but Heather seemed to have decided to swallow her questions without asking about the circumstances. After shaking her head, she corrected her expression to a more serious one.

“While the Guild is grateful for the supply of valuable materials… please try not to get injured.”

“Thank you. Since there are many troublesome monsters, we’ll be careful.”

When I answered, Heather smiled and nodded.

We needed to wait a bit while they processed the material sales… so I let my gaze wander around.

The Guild interior was quite crowded with people. The reason was obvious—a dedicated counter had been set up with a long line forming. They seemed to be people buying theater tickets.

“With the theater and hot spring district established, it seems to have reached a state where customers attract more customers. We were handling ticket sales here too, but it started interfering with our regular operations, so we temporarily separated the service windows,” Heather explained with a wry smile.

“I see. It seems we’ve made things quite busy for you, sorry about that.”

“Not at all. Requests to the Adventurer Guild have increased too, and we’ve been able to secure capable newcomers, so we’re nothing but grateful.”

“That’s good to hear.”

“The current space is becoming somewhat cramped, so we’re making plans for an expansion and arranging the preparations. We’ll widen that area over there to create an entrance and establish a sales office.”

I see. So the current sales window is just temporary. While they could build the sales office outside alone, by keeping it integrated with the Guild office, they also have the purpose of having people incidentally place requests with the Guild.

Yeah. It’s good to see the Adventurer Guild is doing well.

After exchanging our items for money at the Adventurer Guild and leaving the Guild office, we headed straight to the workshop. Since these were the results of our Full Moon Labyrinth exploration, we needed to show Alfred and Old Sigmund our spoils and discuss how to use and distribute the magic stones we obtained this time.

“Welcome back, Theo-kun.”

“Hmm. You appear uninjured.”

“Welcome back. The young ladies also seem safe.”

“We’re relieved you’re all safe, Professor. Everyone.”

They each expressed their joy at our return in their own ways.

“We’re back,” I replied and began arranging our spoils on the table.

“We’ve gathered magic stones. I’d like to discuss how to use and distribute them for the airship.”

“This is…!”

Everyone’s eyes widened as Rosemary took it out from her bag.

The Werewolf original species magic stone. Even without any magic cast on it, it floated above the table, slowly spinning. It was clearly something extraordinary, wrapped in a golden radiance unlike ordinary stones.

“Well now… I’ve never seen a magic stone like this… what in the world did you get it from?” Alfred asked with a stunned expression.

“Werewolf original species. A Guardian.”

“A Guardian from the deep floors… That explains it.”

“What is an original species?”

Charlotte, who didn’t know about Werewolf original species, directed her question to Old Sigmund.

“It’s said to be the ancestor of the werewolves who brought the werewolf curse to the human world. I thought it was just a legendary existence, but to think it actually exists…”

“Yet another… major catch, I see.”

Valentina and Charlotte’s eyes widened at Old Sigmund’s response.

“It was a golden werewolf that used martial arts,” Sheila added as supplementary explanation.

“And these in order are Cyclops, Troll, Basilisk and Cockatrice magic stones. The slightly smaller ones are Lesser Demon magic stones. As for Stormfangs and Invisible Rippers, we have both materials and magic stones.”

“…Quite the hunting expedition. Looking at that lineup of monsters, one can only think of some demon realm… but still, an original species. I would have liked to see it in action, though that’s not exactly the place for such things.”

Old Sigmund shook his head with some disappointment.

“Stormfang fangs and pelts… and then Ripper arms. Have you decided how to use these?”

“Some parts I’m still undecided about. I think using the Ripper arms for weapons would be appropriate.”

“Understood. Then let’s discuss how to use the magic stones.”

We all drank tea while proceeding with our discussion about magic stone usage.

“Then first, let’s hear your thoughts.”

“I’m thinking of using the Werewolf original species magic stone for the ship’s power source, and allocating these four stones for ship control.”

“Using the most exceptional stone for the most critical part. Well, that’s only natural, I suppose.”

“Indeed… With this golden magic stone, it should be able to store plenty of magical power for armor conversion too. Magical power charging and supplying magic to the ship’s various equipment… it should even withstand overload. Being able to push limits should make various things progress smoothly.”

That’s right. The Werewolf original species magic stone is exceptional in many ways. Thanks to that, we’ve gained some room to push boundaries.

“What about the Lesser Demon magic stones?”

“Since there are many of these, I’m thinking of altering their properties and incorporating them into sonic cannons.”

“Hmm… I don’t see any particular reason to object. Wouldn’t it be fine to proceed while determining what can be done with the capacity of these magic stones?”

And so, the distribution of magic stones was decided rather quickly. Well, since we’re not trying anything particularly unusual and just allocating things appropriately, there was no reason for disagreement.

“Speaking of which, I think we should give the airship a name.”

When Valentina tilted her head, everyone looked at me.

“Is it alright for me to name it?”

“Theo-kun is making the most critical parts, after all.”

Saying this, everyone exchanged glances and nodded.

“Understood. Then…”

What should I do? After hesitating briefly, I answered.

“How about… the Sirius?”

Since we’ll be incorporating the Werewolf original species magic stone into the core.

+++

# **327 – Construction and Vacation**

“Alright then. I’ll start the work now. Please let me know early if maintaining the spell formula becomes difficult.”

“Understood. I’ll speak up when I start getting exhausted.”

After taking a sip of tea from the canteen I brought, I nodded at Alfred’s words as he psyching himself up to begin working, then deployed a Magic Circle on the deck of the Sirius. Following the spell formula, phosphorescent light spread across the entire Sirius.

“Well, we’ll be going then.”

“Excuse us.”

Talcott and Cindy said this.

It seems Alfred will start working from the right main wing first. Talcott, Cindy, and Rosemary’s Doll will apparently divide the work as assistants.

While Alfred, Old Sigmund and the others work, my role is to alter the state of the armor plates to make them processable and keep them fixed.

Since I’ll be controlling the spell formula throughout the work and it’s expected to be a long session, I won’t participate in training today and will focus on the airship construction instead. Looking from the deck to the square, I can see everyone following Elliot’s commands and practicing touching the stone pillars.

All the Party Members plan to spend time on the deck to match my schedule. We just went to the full moon Labyrinth the other day, and since we train regularly anyway, this will serve as a break too.

“Well then, shall we get our preparations done too?”

“Yes. Let’s.”

A rolled-up carpet was taken out from Rosemary’s Magic Bag.

We all divided the tasks – spreading out the carpet and laying it on the deck, taking out and arranging tea sets, packages containing baked sweets, containers filled with sandwiches, and so on, advancing our preparations.

It had a somewhat picnic-like atmosphere. Everyone moved efficiently, and once preparations were complete, tea was poured into teacups.

“Theo, preparations are ready. Tea has been poured too, so please help yourself.”

“Ah, thank you.”

So the plan was to lay a carpet on the deck like this, sit down on it, spread out boxed lunches and sweets, then spend time reading books or playing cards.

Lavigne was also lying down at the edge of the carpet, yawning and such. Balor was riding on her back. With her eyes closed and looking comfortable, I guess she’s sunbathing. Eclair remained on the bridge.

“Well then, we shall go install ours too.”

“We’ll divide the work and finish today’s tasks early.”

“We’re heading out.”

Old Sigmund, Valentina, Charlotte and the others also started moving after drinking their tea. They floated their luggage with Levitation and entered the ship’s outer hull. Some of Rosemary’s simple Dolls will accompany them as assistants too. I’ll have Caduceus go along to check on the ship’s interior.

Old Sigmund and the others’ work involves installing the core Magic Tools. The mechanism for making the airship float consists of three Magic Tools. They support at three points and adjust output, enabling ascent and descent, and can also adjust the ship’s tilt relative to the bow, stern, port, and starboard.

The Sirius is built so that the main wings themselves generate lift, allowing it to stay afloat even if it stalls, but we plan to install this mechanism made in Silvatoria as well. This has aspects of efficiency improvement and safety measures.

The idea is that as long as stall, main wing destruction, and destruction of the three core points don’t occur simultaneously, it should remain airborne. Since it’s something that flies through the sky, we want to ensure those aspects are properly addressed.

Old Sigmund seems to have started installation at the planned core installation site located above the keel. The installation locations were determined after flight tests with models investigated where support would provide the best balance.

While watching that work through Caduceus, as my awareness went to the spell formula controlling the outer hull’s state, something suddenly occurred to me.

“Speaking of which… even when fixing the outer hull’s state, there’s no need to cover the entire thing. I could just apply the spell formula to the areas being worked on.”

“Is the spell formula not capable of limiting its range?”

Ashley tilted her head.

“Seems that way. Well, unlike the outer hull, state fixation doesn’t require that much Magical Power though…”

“That’s probably because there was never a need to fix and process something of this scale all at once, don’t you think?”

Rosemary gave a small shudder.

“Meaning?”

“Originally, each armor plate should be much smaller, right?”

“So there was no need to limit the range either.”

“In other words, the problem occurred because Theodore is exceptional.”

“To put it bluntly, I suppose so.”

Rosemary gave a wry smile at Sheila’s words.

So basically, processing something of this size wasn’t anticipated. Well… it seems like I should be able to limit the effective range to the work areas by adjusting the spell formula a bit. Since just maintaining the spell formula would leave me idle, I’ll try improving the spell formula simultaneously too. The work of installing Magic Tools on the airship won’t finish in just one day anyway.

“Still, as Theodore said, it was good we brought the carpet.”

“Because the deck being pure white is a bit dazzling, right?”

Grace agreed with Claudia’s words. Relaxing on the deck while working is nice, but since the material is white, spending long periods here isn’t great for the eyes, hence preparing the carpet. The surroundings are white too, but Marlene has summoned Shade to reduce the reflected glare.

Claudia, Marlene, Sheila, and Seraphina were enjoying card games. Irmhild was cheerfully playing her Lute as usual, so it’s quite a relaxed atmosphere.

“We’ll need to either paint the deck later or lay down planks. Having glare that’s dazzling could potentially cause problems.”

While some aspects are unavoidable due to the armor material, that’s something we’d like to address by covering it in some form or another.

…And with that, I managed to modify the spell formula used on the Sirius, narrowing the effective range for efficiency. Hmm… With this level of Magical Power consumption, maintaining it all day shouldn’t be a problem.

Eventually, the Demon-Slaying Knight Order’s training ended, and as Alfred and Old Sigmund’s work reached a stopping point, Elliot appeared on the deck coming up the gangway.

“Good work, everyone.”

“Good work, Elliot-san.”

We exchanged greetings.

“We’ve decided to go out to the hot spring town together again now. Before that, there are some decisions regarding my wedding with Camilla, so let me report.”

“Yes.”

I poured Elliot a cup of tea, offered him some sweets, and listened while he spoke.

“After consulting with His Majesty Melvin, we’ve decided to hold the wedding in the Barony of Silun. At that time, Her Highness Stephania and Her Highness Adriana have graciously agreed to attend as well.”

“Both of them?”

“Welcoming such distinguished guests is unusual for the Barony of Silun… but there’s no problem with holding the wedding itself. We’ll have to send out notifications and invitations everywhere starting now.”

…I see. By having royalty attend personally, they’re demonstrating to the people of the Barony of Silun that King Melvin supports Elliot and that there are strong ties with Silvatoria too.

Since there’s a promise to later install Elliot as lord, from King Melvin’s side, they probably want Princess Stephania to explicitly state that in the Barony of Silun. Making it clear beforehand also serves as a measure to avoid trouble.

“Well then, I’ll contact the butler from my side.”

Ashley smiled.

“Ah. Thank you, Ashley.”

“If the Sirius’s completion and trial run are finished in time, heading to the Barony of Silun with it might be good too.”

“That would be quite flashy. For protecting Her Highness Stephania and Her Highness Adriana, I think it would be perfect.”

Elliot gave a wry smile and nodded.

Considering the timing, the Sirius’s completion might end up being slightly earlier.

We also need to visit Gartner County and the Barony of Silun to increase our transferable bases. If the Sirius is completed, we can use it to travel there. As Elliot said, that would also solve the issue of protecting the two princesses.

Additionally… arriving by airship at the barony for the wedding ceremony would establish appropriate justification both internally and externally for the Demon-Slaying Knight Order Commander’s wedding. And having the trial run be for the wedding ceremony probably has good auspicious connotations and would be favorable, wouldn’t it?

+++

# **328 – Bridal Attire**

Since it’s about Elliot and Camilla’s wedding, I contacted Kennel via communication device to inform him of the date and attendee details, and had him prepare the banquet arrangements on the Barony of Silun side as well.

“Judging from the message on the communication device, the old butler seems quite enthusiastic. I think he’s happy about Elliot-sama’s wedding.”

“I’m sure he is. In the Barony of Silun. And with those two, of all people.”

For Kennel, this might be a scene he’d only dreamed of. Especially since he once thought Elliot had died, his joy must be all the greater.

We’re also progressing with the airship construction to make it in time for the wedding date.

Since we’ve managed to optimize the state-fixing spell formulas, I can help with training for Party Members and the Demon-Slaying Knight Order while working without any issues… The construction is proceeding smoothly.

Meanwhile, Elliot is busy supervising the Demon-Slaying Knight Order’s training and sending out invitations. When I mentioned this, he gave a wry smile and said, “I’m not as busy as you are, Theodore-san. I need to work hard too.” From my perspective, since much of my work involves using magic, I don’t feel as busy as it might appear to others.

And so today’s work also came to an end. As evening fell and I was relaxing in the game room, Cecilia came to inform me of visitors.

“Master, we have guests. Lady Miriam and someone called Lady Daisy.”

“Ah, understood. I believe they’re here for Elliot-san and Camilla-san. Please show them to the reception room.”

“Certainly.”

Cecilia bowed slightly and returned.

“Is it about the bridal gown?”

“Most likely. Could you both come with me to the reception room?”

“Yes.”

I headed to the reception room together with Elliot and Camilla.

Daisy is an acquaintance of Miriam, the owner of the Labyrinth Trading Company, and runs a tailor shop in Termwills. She’s the one we placed the order with for Camilla’s bridal gown.

We’ve had Daisy make coats and dresses for us several times before. Therefore, when Elliot asked us if there were any good shops in Termwills, it automatically meant Daisy’s shop.

When we approached the reception room, Cecilia was waiting outside. She knocked to inform Miriam and Daisy inside that we had arrived, then we entered the reception room.

“Good evening, everyone.”

“Good evening, Miriam-san, Daisy-san.”

“Good evening. The requested item has been completed, so I’ve brought it for you to see the finished product.”

After exchanging greetings, Daisy smiled and bowed slightly.

“I went to visit Daisy, and when I learned the dress she’d been commissioned to make was finished, I volunteered to act as escort for the journey. It was getting dark, and the delivery item is precious.”

“Is that so? Thank you.”

At Miriam’s words, Elliot expressed his gratitude. Perhaps Miriam’s visit to Daisy led to the decision to bring the completed dress right away.

“May I show you the finished product now?”

“Then I shall excuse myself for a moment.”

Elliot stood up. There’s something of a tradition that it’s bad luck for the groom to see the bridal gown before the wedding day.

“Then, please take care of this.”

Elliot temporarily left the room.

In response to Camilla’s words, Daisy carefully took out a pure white dress from its wrapping. The luster of silk thread. Delicate frills and embroidery… One could see Daisy’s meticulous workmanship.

Camilla’s eyes widened, and as she gently received it, she lightly ran her hand over it and narrowed her eyes.

“…Such delicate embroidery. It’s amazing.”

“Are you pleased with it?”

“Yes, very much.”

“Please, try slipping your arms through the sleeves.”

“Is that alright?”

Camilla smiled happily. There are probably aspects you can’t know without trying it on.

“It seems better if I step out too. I’ll go to the game room as well.”

“I shall also leave the room until you’ve finished changing.”

“Then once preparations are complete, Lady Camilla and I will come to you.”

And so, I decided to leave the reception room for now and kill some time.

“Has Lady Camilla’s dress been completed?”

When I returned to the game room, Ashley asked.

“Yeah. She’s changing into it now.”

“I think she’ll show us once she’s finished changing… um, that’s right. Sir Elliot—”

“Then, if you’ll permit me, I think I’ll go to the guest room for now. It would be better for the ladies to see it in a bright, spacious place like the game room.”

Elliot said with a wry smile, then was guided to the guest room by Cecilia.

“Elliot-sama looks somewhat disappointed.”

“Hmm. I suppose so.”

I answered Ashley, who was smiling wryly.

“We should keep food and drinks away. It would be terrible if they got stained.”

“I’ll help, Grace-sama.”

At Grace’s words, everyone divided tasks to move teacups, pots, and such away from the entrance, carrying them to the back of the game room. With Camilla about to make her appearance wearing the bridal gown, the female members seemed quite excited.

“A bridal gown, huh. When it comes to marriage in the Labyrinth Village, the Arachne make them. Weddings become village-wide festivals.”

“That’s… I’d kind of like to see that.”

At that time, the Labyrinth Village residents would probably remove their emotion-suppressing magic tools, and Claudia would suppress the labyrinth’s movements.

The Labyrinth Village residents are probably honing their singing, dancing, and musical instrument skills for that day. Cyrille is like that too – the villagers being skilled in arts probably has reasons connected to that.

“Recently, since they don’t need to suppress emotions anymore, we have more flexibility with wedding dates. Eventually, I’d like to try having a festival outside.”

Claudia smiled gently. I see. They might be coordinating things like deciding wedding dates while considering Claudia’s magical power consumption.

While we were talking like this, Camilla arrived at the game room wearing the bridal gown, with Miriam and Daisy supporting the long hem. Everyone’s gaze gathered on Camilla in her pure white dress and veil.

“How… is it?”

“You look beautiful, Lady Camilla.”

“Thank you, Lady Ashley.”

“If there are any areas needing adjustments, I’m ready to accommodate.”

“Thank you. It seems comfortable to wear too.”

The female members’ reactions were positive. Marlene’s eyes were sparkling, and Rosemary was watching with interest while hiding her mouth with her feather fan and nodding.

Since it wouldn’t be good to keep Elliot waiting too long, and we’d be in trouble if it got dirty, after everyone had a good look at Camilla’s wedding dress, Camilla returned to the reception room to change again.

“I must tell Elliot-sama that it was a truly wonderful finished product.”

“That’s right. Perhaps it would be better not to say anything too specific, to increase the anticipation?”

“Yes.”

After Claudia answered, Ashley nodded with a happy expression.

And so, it seems another preparation for the wedding has moved forward. A wedding dress, huh. I too… when I marry everyone, I’ll need to prepare something proper.

Well, that aside… if we’re heading to the Barony of Silun, there’s a matter that’s becoming timely.

“I think the pumpkins we’re growing with the Evil Weeds should be ready around this time, so if the results are good, we might consider introducing them to the Barony of Silun too.”

“Ah. That’s right. Probably before the wedding, I suppose?”

“The pumpkins in the back have gotten quite large, haven’t they?”

Yes. They had become monster pumpkins large enough to hold in both arms. The Evil Weeds showed no change either.

I’ve heard that Evil Weeds become somewhat more aggressive when they hold seeds around early autumn, but the Harvesta placed in pots by the sunny window of the game room remained quite docile even with Seraphina and Balor sitting nearby.

“Indeed… it might be almost harvest time.”

“I’m quite looking forward to pumpkin pie.”

Said Sheila. Yes. It had been decided that if the pumpkins bore fruit, Mihaela would make pie for us.

“With pumpkins that size, cooking them might be quite challenging.”

“Shall we divide the cooking among everyone?”

At Irmhild’s words, Grace smiled wryly.
