# **336 – Towards the Count's Territory**

“So this is the Harvesta… I saw them in the back field too, but they really are docile, aren’t they?”

Michelle stared intently at the Harvesta placed on the desk, then cautiously extended her palm as if reaching out. The Harvesta slowly turned its head but made no attempt to bite. The distance between them felt like they were confirming neither had any intention of attacking.

After gently stroking the Harvesta’s head, Michelle tickled its neck—or rather, stem—with her index finger, much like one would stroke a cat’s throat.

The Harvesta, which had been looking slightly downward, tilted its head upward as if exposing its throat. Michelle looked delighted. Hmm. She seems like someone who could get along well with the Noble Leafs too.

“Excuse me.”

At that moment, a servant brought in a dish made from monster pumpkin—pumpkin soup.

“This is a dish made from giant pumpkins grown alongside the Harvesta. Please try it first.”

After this explanation, Michelle’s eyes widened, then she broke into a smile.

“Then, I’ll have some.”

It had been well-received during our home tasting sessions and yesterday’s banquet… but what would Michelle think? She scooped some with a spoon and brought it to her mouth. She savored it carefully with one, then two bites, and gradually her expression brightened.

“It’s delicious. I also saw the crops growing in the back field, but this… is amazing.”

“It’s been proven that they grow large and taste good. Some people said Evil Weed might not be appropriate, so there’s talk of renaming it to Noble Leaf.”

“That’s a good name.”

“Thank you. However, there are still several experimental items we need to test.”

“Is it about whether the soil’s power might be depleted…?”

Impressive. She truly lives up to her reputation as someone researching how to apply magic to agriculture.

Using Earth Magic or Wood Magic recklessly to increase short-term harvests is easy, but that only rapidly depletes the nutrients in the soil. If done carelessly, future harvests will gradually decline. That’s why I’ve heard magicians specializing in this field research various methods to prevent magical side effects.

Therefore, we need to continue observing whether Noble Leaf might cause similar issues.

“That’s right. We want to observe not just with pumpkins, but also what happens when planted alongside wheat, our main focus. After assessing the impact, if there seem to be no problems, we’d like to promote it as a farming method.”

“That’s why Theodore-sama and I were discussing the possibility of conducting experiments and observations in the Barony of Silun.”

To gain the farmers’ understanding, showing them the farming method in practice would be best. The Barony of Silun, being a grain-producing region, is perfect for this.

“I see… So that’s how it is.”

“If you don’t mind, I’d like to ask about the magic you specialize in, Michelle-san.”

“I can use Water and Earth Magic to some extent. Given my profession, you could say… I can create Golems to help with farm work.”

Ashley and I exchanged glances and nodded. She’s probably the best candidate we could hope for.

“If you’re willing, we’d very much like to ask for your cooperation in the experiments.”

“Really!?”

Michelle’s expression brightened, and she half-rose from her seat. Yeah. Michelle’s motivation seems high too.

“Yes. We look forward to working with you.”

We shook hands with Michelle, each in turn. With the decision to enlist Michelle’s help… we proceeded to discuss specific details like employment conditions for her participation in the experiments and how to change the properties from Evil Weed to Noble Leaf.

“Growing from seed state using Water Magic in pots… selecting beneficial and harmful insects… Taking those planted in the field, potting them, and returning them to a warm place to entrust them with seeds… Hmm. I see…”

Michelle was taking notes on what appeared to be a notepad-like stack of papers. Probably for record-keeping.

“I’d like to research the Harvesta’s subsequent generations too. Monsters have their properties fixed by the magical environment during their childhood. They can become more ferocious or more docile, for instance.”

“Is that… like Sirens or Lamias?”

“Yes. There are inherently aggressive species, but Noble Leaf seems different. They appear intelligent enough to consider building symbiotic relationships with humans… so it’s possible changes could occur through learning alone.”

The former Evil Weed, now Noble Leaf, isn’t inherently a ferocious species.

Therefore, it’s conceivable that subsequent generations of Harvesta could learn through observation of their surroundings that maintaining a symbiotic relationship with humans is beneficial, and thus refrain from attacking… even without being raised with Water Magic.

That aspect requires continued observation before we can say anything definitive. Since property changes occur generation by generation, we currently know that using Water Magic makes them docile, but that’s it.

When I shared these thoughts, Michelle nodded appreciatively.

“Indeed… Gradually changing conditions and making comparisons is important.”

“Considering the possibility of wild species mixing in during experiments, wouldn’t it be good to mark them somehow?”

Suggested Ashley. Definitely. It would be problematic if they got mixed up and became indistinguishable.

“Then, how about putting decorative markers on the individuals raised with Water Magic?”

“That might be a good idea.”

Ashley and Michelle continued their conversation in a warm, friendly atmosphere.

Hmm. So like putting ribbons on them to distinguish them from wild species? Well… it probably wouldn’t look bad on them.

“But with winter coming, the experiments will halt, won’t they?”

“In that case, let’s build a greenhouse. Though it won’t suit wheat.”

Considering our next visit to the Barony of Silun using the stone monument, we should prepare materials and such in advance.

Greenhouses are fine from autumn to winter, but working in them during summer is tough. Maybe we should prepare magic tools that can generate weak cold air. I’ll consult Alfred about this later.

We reached an agreement that Termwills would bring Noble Leaf and its seeds to Michelle at a later date.

After that, we had lunch at the Silun Baron’s house, leisurely drank post-meal tea, and then prepared to depart. Father and Malcolm and the others are also boarding the Sirius, so we loaded luggage onto the Sirius. Since everyone is equipped with Levitation Magic Tools, the loading was completed easily.

Seraphina also has high magical power, so she used Levitation Magic Tools to float luggage larger than herself onto the airship, looking quite pleased with her accomplished task.

“Patricia’s house and the tomb, huh?”

“It’s a beautiful spot by the lakeside.”

Grace responded happily to Old Sigmund’s murmured words.

“That sounds delightful.”

“Lady Patricia’s mansion… I’m curious about it.”

Old Sigmund and Valentina nodded. Charlotte wore a serious expression, likely because it’s the former Sealing Shrine Maiden’s house.

“I’m looking forward to it too. From what Theo-kun says, it sounds like a house that might appear in a story or something.”

“I wonder what kind of house it is?”

When Alfred spoke, Princess Stephania reacted.

“A house made by hollowing out a giant tree created with Wood Magic. I like the smell of wood.”

“The bathroom is particularly wonderful. You can see the entire view.”

…These comments came from Sheila and Irmhild. Marlene was also nodding vigorously.

“Creating such a giant tree with Wood Magic is quite impressive.”

“Moreover, that tree is still alive, right? The leaves are lush too.”

“You can gather fruits in early autumn.”

I added supplementary explanations to Claudia and Rosemary’s remarks.

“That sounds delightful. As expected, things are never boring when Theodore is around.”

Princess Stephania looked happily at the excited group, while Princess Adriana crossed her arms, closed her eyes, and nodded.

Seeing everyone’s enthusiasm, Ashley also smiled gently, then turned to Elliot and Camilla to exchange words.

“Well then, Elliot brother, Camilla sister-in-law, we’ll come pick you up on our return.”

“Yeah. If anything happens, contact us via the Communication Device.”

Elliot smiled gently. Yeah. I hope the two of them can enjoy some peaceful time together as a couple in the Barony of Silun.

“Then, Ashley-sama. Please take care.”

“Yes, old man. We’re off.”

After exchanging words with everyone at the Silun Baron’s house, we boarded the Sirius. I sat in the pilot’s seat, held my hand over the crystal, and made it ascend.

Reflected on the crystal panel were Elliot and Camilla standing close together, along with Kennel and Donato and the others. They seemed to have stood there seeing us off until the Sirius became too small to see.

The town’s atmosphere… still seemed to carry last night’s celebratory mood.

People dressed in finery and windows decorated with flowers. Citizens and adventurers waving enthusiastically toward us. I could see Ashley, Princess Stephania, and Princess Adriana waving from the deck toward the barony’s people.

Well then—let’s head to Count Gartner’s house.

# **337 – Autumn Forest**

“Port side aft here. Can you hear me?”

“Yes, I can hear you, Steph.”

Princess Stephania’s voice came through the speaking tube from the bridge. The one responding was Princess Adriana. Since they wanted to look around various parts of the ship, I thought we might as well test the speaking tubes while we were at it. As a result, Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana were touring the ship during our journey to the Count’s territory.

Marlene was listening to her sister’s voice coming through the speaking tube together with Princess Adriana, smiling happily. Rosemary occasionally glanced their way, covering her mouth with her feather fan while maintaining a composed expression… but she also seemed to be in a somewhat cheerful mood.

Rosemary, Valentina, Charlotte, and Tephra were sitting near the pilot seats, observing my piloting. We were proceeding while occasionally taking turns to learn how to operate the ship through hands-on experience.

Grace, Ashley, and Claudia were doing needlework, while Alfred, Old Sigmund, Father, and Malcolm were playing cards while discussing Noble Leaf and farmland development, each spending time as they pleased.

In this relaxed atmosphere, the Sirius advanced while Irmhild and the others played gentle music. Eventually, Mother’s house came into view in the distant landscape.

“It’s coming into view. That particularly large tree,” I said, and everyone’s gaze gathered on the scenery visible through the crystal panel.

“Steph, I can see it. Can you come back to the bridge?”

“I’m coming now.”

After this exchange, Princess Stephania came up to the bridge with Mercedes a short while later.

Princess Stephania seemed captivated by the sight of Mother’s house.

“…It really is a big tree.”

It was tall enough to be immediately obvious without explanation, with a thick trunk. While glancing at Mother’s house from the corner of my eye, I parked the Sirius in an open area right by the lakeside, marking our arrival.

After descending and parking the ship, we decided to first unload the luggage and carry it into Mother’s house. While bringing the luggage out onto the Sirius’s deck, I asked Father.

“What will you be doing, Father?”

“You’ll be heading to Lisa’s grave first, I suppose? I have arrangements to make as well, so I thought I’d return to the mansion afterward,” Father said, looking at the bouquet in my hand.

“Understood.”

“I’ve also made preparations to welcome Her Highness and Marquis Broderick… hmm. Given this situation, Lisa’s house might be more suitable for hospitality than my mansion.”

“Perhaps so. If you have anything prepared, shall we do it at Mother’s house?”

Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana had been quite excited ever since Mother’s house came into view.

“Then I’ll have the food brought here.”

“In that case, we’ll take it easy here.”

“Indeed.”

So we wouldn’t need to prepare meals and could all relax together.

“I plan to stay at Count Gartner’s mansion. There’s talk of technical cooperation, and I have some matters I’d like to discuss,” said Malcolm. That would be about farmland development and mine development, I suppose.

Apparently, there’s been discussion about mutually providing technical cooperation and coordinating with each other. The relationship between House Gartner and House Broderick seems to be good.

Had the previous heads of both houses also coordinated with each other? Rather than saying things have returned to how they were, it might be more accurate to say the trade has become proper.

As we were unloading luggage from the deck, the tomb keepers Harold and Cynthia appeared from among the trees. They must have heard about the wedding date from Father. When they made eye contact with me, the two smiled and greeted me.

“Good afternoon, Theodore-sama.”

“It’s been a while.”

“Ah, it’s good to see you both after so long.”

Harold and Cynthia not only tended to Mother’s grave but also seemed to consistently maintain the area around the house. The grass was properly cut, and fallen leaves and branches had been cleared away.

“It’s a great help that you always keep it so clean.”

“Thank you.”

“It’s our job.”

The siblings smiled happily.

“More importantly, that’s an amazing ship.”

Having spotted the Sirius from within the forest, Harold’s eyes were wide with amazement, and Cynthia was nodding vigorously.

“Thank you. Things are a bit hectic today, so I’ll give you a tour of the ship tomorrow or so.”

“Really!?”

“As thanks for tending the grave,” I answered, and the siblings’ faces lit up.

When we reached the base of Mother’s house carrying our luggage, those who were visiting for the first time looked up with admiration.

“This is—amazing. Just as Alfred said.”

“Truly… What a wonderful house.”

Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana had shining eyes. I thought they might like this sort of thing, and I’m glad they seem to appreciate it.

“Yeah. It looked impressive from above too… but seeing it up close is something else. I heard about it from Theo-kun, but I’m glad I came.”

Alfred was also smiling happily.

“So this is… Patricia’s ideal house, I see. Indeed, the atmosphere around here is somewhat similar to the promenade at the Sages’ Academy.”

Valentina narrowed her eyes as she looked up at Mother’s house. That must be referring to when I spoke with Valentina at the Sages’ Academy.

“It’s a good place. The magical power is well-ordered, and there’s a cleansing air.”

“Being in this house makes me feel better.”

Tephra and Seraphina also seemed to approve.

“There appears to be a barrier set up.”

“…Indeed. That its effectiveness shows no decline whatsoever is likely due to it being the work of the Sealing Shrine Maiden. She laid multiple spell formulas from the construction phase onward, utilizing the terrain to reinforce the barrier.”

Old Sigmund nodded at Charlotte’s words.

The barrier around Mother’s house, combined and synchronized with contract magic, only permits entry to those invited by me, Grace, or Father. It’s similar to the barrier Claudia set up in the basement of Ashley’s mansion.

We climbed the stairs arranged to wind around the trunk, where a slightly wider landing had been created before the door. Opening the door, we entered inside. After setting down our hand luggage, visiting the grave was our first priority.

We passed through the forest path, all heading toward Mother’s tomb. The autumn colors would probably be at their peak a bit later… but they were already starting to show here and there, making it quite beautiful even now.

Seraphina, Balor, and Eclair were flying around, weaving through the trees and chasing each other in the air. Lavigne and Alpha were running after them.

“Don’t go too far and get lost, okay?”

“Mm-hmm!”

Seraphina seemed to be thoroughly enjoying the early autumn forest. Marlene was watching them with delight.

“This place is wonderful whenever I come.”

“Yes, I agree. I like it too. The autumn colors become very beautiful a bit later.”

As Ashley spoke while looking at the forest, Grace nodded happily.

“When we came in summer… the greenery and the lakeside were beautiful too.”

Claudia narrowed her eyes peacefully.

“Must be the season for mushroom picking. Mushroom gathering tomorrow might be nice.”

“That sounds lovely. We might be able to gather materials for magic potions too.”

Rosemary seemed quite enthusiastic. Magic potions, huh? Now that I think about it, I remember Mother saying things like “You can’t eat this mushroom, so don’t pick it,” yet she still collected poisonous mushrooms too… She must have been using the large cauldron in the hidden room to mix magic potions and such.

“Mushroom soup…”

Sheila seemed to be looking forward to mushroom dishes. Sheila was her usual self. Irmhild was smiling as she watched Sheila.

Eventually, we arrived at Mother’s gravesite. A well-maintained clearing with a gravestone enshrined in the center. The previously cheerful atmosphere changed somewhat, becoming serene while still retaining a certain warmth.

“I’m home, Mother.”

Placing the bouquet before the grave, I offered a silent prayer. One by one, everyone quietly offered their silent prayers.

“It’s been a long time. That day, I admired Lady Lisa whom I saw on the ship, and have lived until today with that as my ideal of how royalty and nobility should be. Please rest in peace. I too intend to fulfill my duties as royalty to the best of my ability. Please watch over Verdgar from now on.”

Saying this, Princess Stephania bowed to the gravestone and offered a silent prayer.

…That’s right. Princess Stephania had met Mother too.

“Indeed. This is… a good place, Patricia.”

Old Sigmund said this with a somewhat lonely smile.

“Your magic… brought Theodore-kun to us. It restored our memories. Thank you, Patricia.”

At Valentina’s words, spoken with a smile before she offered her silent prayer, Princess Adriana and Charlotte also seemed deeply moved.

For Princess Adriana, Mother was the person who left behind one half of the magic to解除 the memory seal she was holding. For Charlotte, she was the previous Sealing Shrine Maiden. They must have various feelings toward Mother.

Yeah. Having this many people come… makes me happy, I think. When my eyes met Grace’s by chance, she too returned a gentle smile.

+++

# **338 – Memories of the Eastern Country**

The magical lights hanging from the ceiling illuminated the dining table in Mother’s house with a warm glow. We all gathered around the large wooden table, where dishes brought by the Count’s servants were arranged. White bread, salad, and stew. Pasta, herb-stuffed turkey, and salt-grilled river fish. And since we had harvested fruits from Mother’s house, they were also placed on the table.

“Quite sweet. Delicious.”

Sheila shared her impression after tasting the fruit.

It was a fig fruit, black or rather dark purple in color.

In short, Mother’s house was a giant fig tree. She must have put a lot of effort into it – using Wood Magic to accelerate its growth, creating living space inside…

“We harvested at just the right time. Any later and the birds would have eaten them.”

“With this much sweetness, they’d make good jam.”

“I used to make it in the past. Shall I make some jam for you to take back later?”

Grace smiled at Ashley’s words.

“This fruit seems to contain magical power. It could probably be used as material for Magic Potions.”

Rosemary murmured with admiration after tasting the fig.

“Hmm. I never noticed before, but you might be right.”

It was similar to Tephra’s hot spring and the pumpkins grown with Noble Leaf. They probably had effects like enhancing natural healing ability or replenishing magical power.

“At this rate… wouldn’t it only be a matter of time before it awakens as a powerful wood spirit?”

Tephra, with Seraphina perched on her shoulder, laughed cheerfully.

“It certainly meets the conditions for a spirit to gain power and manifest.”

Claudia closed her eyes and smiled quietly. …It was a plausible story. Coming from Tephra, a spirit herself, it had high credibility. With a core symbolic great tree and everyone holding images of it, a spirit could manifest.

The dinner was in full swing. Dominique the Harpy, having tasted the fruit wine, sat by the window and began singing cheerfully. The dining table was filled with a harmonious atmosphere.

“A spirit… it would be wonderful if one appeared.”

Marlene nodded happily at Princess Stephania’s words.

“The bathroom also has a view of the starry sky, this house is delightful.”

“The view from the guest room was beautiful too. With the skylight.”

“The beds are insufficient, aren’t they? I thought staying overnight on the ship docked at the lakeside would be nice… but it’s quite difficult to decide.”

Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana were consulting with serious expressions like this. Well… it’s good that Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana were thoroughly enjoying their travels.

With so many people, Mother’s house alone couldn’t accommodate everyone. Some would have to sleep crowded together, so it was decided that someone would stay overnight on the Sirius, also serving as night watch.

We were going to decide later who would stay, but both Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana seemed torn, unable to choose between the options.

“In that case, how about postponing the day we head to the Marquisate of Broderick?”

Malcolm, who had been listening, made the suggestion.

“Will that be acceptable with Marquis Broderick’s schedule?”

“A delay of one day would be no problem at all. Rather, since we didn’t know the airship’s speed, we’ve prepared to be ready to welcome you whenever you arrive.”

Hmm. From Marquis Broderick’s perspective, since he didn’t know the airship’s speed, he had made arrangements to allow for some flexibility. I see.

“Then… if you don’t mind, let’s delay our departure slightly.”

It was a minor schedule change… just spending a little more time at Mother’s house. It shouldn’t be a problem for us either. Since Malcolm had offered, it would be rude to refuse his consideration.

“…Well. We’ve overstayed quite a bit. Before it gets too late, we should return to the mansion.”

Father quietly stood up, apparently judging it was about time to leave.

“Count Gartner, thank you for the delicious meal.”

“You honor me too much.”

“Let me escort you on your way.”

After exchanging greetings with Princess Stephania, I followed Father toward the doorway.

“That’s reassuring.”

Father smiled wryly.

“Haa…”

I soaked in the bath up to my shoulders, looking up at the steam rising toward the starry sky, and let out a deep sigh.

I had escorted Father and Malcolm to the Count’s residence and returned to take a bath.

The bathroom in Mother’s house was characterized by being able to see the starry sky and distant scenery while soaking in the tub. Since you could see the lake from the high elevation, the view was beautiful even during daytime baths.

Right now—I could see the Sirius docked by the lakeshore. Even at night, the white hull stood out.

“Excuse me.”

While I was relaxing, Grace entered after changing into her bath robe in the changing room. Today it was Grace’s turn to bathe with me.

Her white skin and bath robe were softly illuminated by the magical lantern. Her lustrous golden hair and blue eyes seemed to reflect the light, sparkling.

Hmm… Still as devastatingly effective as ever, that bath robe. Grace’s development recently has been, well…

…Yeah. Better not think too much about it.

“Let me help you.”

“Thank you.”

I washed the largely exposed back area and slowly poured warm water over her with a bucket.

After washing her hair, I entered the bath again with Grace… and let out a quiet sigh at the warmth of the water.

“The stars are beautiful.”

“Yeah.”

Because the air was clear, the starry sky was very beautiful. Countless stars spread across the night sky. When I dimmed the magical lights, they became even more visible.

Quiet water sounds tickled my ears. The faint sound of Irmhild and the others playing music from downstairs, along with the chirping of insects, seemed to enhance the quietness of the night, or rather, the peaceful atmosphere.

“Being like this brings back memories. It reminds me of bathing with Lady Lisa and Theo.”

“That… I don’t remember much…”

“It’s from when Theo was little.”

Grace smiled under the moonlight. Then she looked with slightly distant eyes. So I asked suddenly.

“Grace… are you okay with going east?”

“To the Marquisate of Broderick? I’m fine. Thinking back now, after entering the Kingdom of Verdugal, I was always running away, keeping my distance from human settlements, so nothing particularly happened to me in this country.”

The place where Grace first met me and Mother was in the forests of Gartner County… but she had fled from further east. Everything that happened to Grace before meeting Mother took place outside the country…

Grace said her memories were somewhat vague since she was young at the time, but apparently she had been fleeing westward.

“My father was a Vampire, but he fought other Vampires to let my mother escape—and lost his life doing so. I was young so I don’t remember much about my father… but I do have the memory of him disappearing while still holding my mother’s hand.”

…Virginia, the Vampire I encountered when fighting Gardinis, had shown considerable hostility toward Grace too. For Vampires, mixed-blood children are enemies, and Grace’s father, who tried to protect her, was probably treated as a traitor.

“Sorry. Did I make you remember something painful?”

When I asked, Grace shook her head and smiled.

“No. I know you’re concerned about me… and that makes me happy. Now I have Theo and everyone else with me.”

“…Yeah. That’s right.”

“Yes.”

Saying that, she leaned against me lightly, as if drawing close.

I reached around Grace’s shoulders and head, pulling her closer. The feel of her soft hair and Grace’s body temperature.

Grace had lived hidden in the mountains with her mother… but eventually their existence became known to the nearby village, and they were driven from their home.

Even as a mixed-blood, or perhaps if they were Termwills, they might have been accepted. Grace’s mother had apparently headed west with that hope.

In the end, since Grace met Mother and Father allowed her to stay in the territory on the condition of the Cursed Tool, it was probably the right choice.

Additionally, considering the current situation, King Melvin granted Grace a knightly rank knowing she was a Dhampir. That could only mean Verdugal would accept her as long as the problem of bloodthirst was resolved.

Both King Melvin’s stated policies and my personal views… and even from the perspective of being the Otherworld Ambassador, our goals aligned. You could say the environment to protect Grace was in place.

So if… something harmful were to come to Grace because of her origins or past. And if Vampires became enemies. I would simply stand ready to face them all.

Looking up, the yellow moon shone in the night sky. Staying close to the peacefully smiling Grace, the night quietly deepened.

+++

# **339 – Mushroom Hunting**

The next day. As planned, we all went mushroom gathering. Clear skies. Combined with the autumn coolness, it turned out to be quite a nice day.

Grace was her usual self. When our eyes met, she smiled at me. Hmm.

Since we were in a nearby forest, there was little worry about getting lost, but if anyone got separated from the group, we agreed to head toward the Sirius.

“Mushroom gathering… It’s been since the Dusk Forest, but this is my first time properly gathering edible mushrooms,” Mercedes said with a distant look in her eyes. Mercedes had descended into the labyrinth to search for the seal’s gate and had quite a tough time surrounded by Whisper Mushrooms in the Dusk Forest, hadn’t she?

“Hmm. It seems some people are doing this for the first time, so let me go over a few precautions. Many mushrooms are poisonous, so we’ll operate on the principle of not picking anything that looks ambiguous from the start,” I said, using Earth Magic to create models of the target mushrooms. Shiitake, truffles, matsutake, porcini, maitake, shimeji, and wood ear mushrooms, among others.

“Depending on the type, mushrooms tend to prefer tree roots, trunks, and humid areas. Try searching by brushing aside fallen leaves. If you find one, you’ll often find more nearby. Also, if you leave a bit of the base behind, it’ll be easier to gather mushrooms there again next year,” Grace added, explaining tips for finding mushrooms.

“By the way, these are the poisonous mushrooms,” I said, also using Earth Magic to create models to show everyone. Particularly dangerous ones like Fire Mushroom, Death Angel Mushroom, and Poisonous Sasa Mushroom.

“If you eat them… what happens?”

“Ah. With these, you should assume you won’t survive without Clear Blood. There are magic tools for detoxification too, but it’s best not to eat them at all. Some won’t kill you, but there are mushrooms that cause excruciating pain after a few days, or poisonous mushrooms that bring severe pain lasting for weeks, so absolutely don’t touch any mushrooms other than the edible samples.”

When I emphasized this with specific examples, everyone nodded with solemn expressions. Well, as long as they understood that poisonous mushrooms are dangerous, that’s fine.

“Some are used as ingredients for magic potions. This mushroom… I read in texts that it’s dangerous to even touch with bare hands, so if you find it, just let me know,” was Rosemary’s opinion. The one dangerous to touch must be the Fire Mushroom. Well, it’s red and has a poisonous-looking shape, so avoiding it should be easy enough.

To avoid confusion, I kept only the edible mushroom samples and returned the poisonous mushroom models to lumps of earth.

“Well… if you find any mushrooms not covered in the explanation, don’t pick them; just let me, Grace, or Marie know.”

“Mm, understood.”

“I’ll do my best. I owe mushrooms a debt,” said Sheila, nodding calmly, and Mercedes, who seemed fired up, clenching her fist.

…And so, mushroom gathering in the autumn forest began. We walked through the forest searching for mushrooms.

“Found some,” said Sheila, who had quickly located mushrooms. Partly due to her sharp senses, but apparently she gained experience during her time in the Thieves Guild, fishing and gathering mushrooms around Termwills.

She left the easily found mushrooms to the others and seemed to be aiming for big catches like truffles with Lavigne and Alpha. Well… being able to search by scent is quite an advantage.

“Over here too!”

Harold and Cynthia were putting up a good fight. Having maintained Mother’s house and the area around the grave as gravekeepers, they seemed quite familiar with mushrooms, perhaps from frequently entering the forest. Cynthia smiled as she found shiitake, while Harold skillfully cleared small branches with a mountain knife and gathered wild vegetables. You could really tell they had plenty of experience.

“You two seem quite accustomed to gathering mushrooms.”

“It doesn’t cost anything upfront, and it helps save on food expenses,” Harold said with a laugh.

“This forest is lovely,” said Rosemary in high spirits. It seemed like a place where medicinal herbs, aromatic herbs, mushrooms, and more were free for the taking. She seemed to have found a fly agaric and was quite pleased, stuffing it into her magic bag.

“This is a medicinal herb with analgesic effects. Crushing it and applying it to wounds improves recovery, and it can be eaten too,” Claudia said as she gathered various items with Marlene, Irmhild, Justia, Dominique, and Tephra. Apparently, wild plants and mushrooms grow around the Labyrinth Village too, so she seemed knowledgeable about them. Marlene nodded seriously at Claudia’s words.

“Is this an edible mushroom?”

“Yes. That’s true shimeji. There’s a somewhat similar poisonous mushroom, so Theo omitted explaining it earlier,” Grace said as Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana immediately began asking about mushrooms.

Ashley also seemed to be searching for mushrooms with the two princesses.

“Ah, this is fun. Lately, it’s been all about making magic tools.”

“Indeed. Building airships has been quite taxing too,” Alfred said cheerfully, using Wind Magic to scatter fallen leaves and search for mushrooms. Old Sigmund, Valentina, and Charlotte were also using Wind Magic with Alfred. Having worked together in the workshop and shipyard, they seemed to have grown close.

Hmm. Everyone seemed to be doing various things. I’ll have Caduceus skim the ground over a wide area and gather mushrooms, being careful not to overharvest.

…We continued mushroom gathering in this manner, and as noon approached, we decided to wrap up and return to the lakeside. Since we could view the lake from a high place with a good outlook, we planned to have lunch on the deck of the Sirius. I also promised to show Harold and Cynthia around inside the Sirius.

“Worked hard,” said Sheila, as usual, but I sensed a hint of pride in a job well done.

The basket brought from Mother’s house for gathering was piled high with mushrooms and wild vegetables.

We had ingredients brought from Termwills too, and we’d gathered a fair amount of truffles. Irmhild had even taken down a wild boar… Today’s lunch seemed likely to be quite lavish.

I should check that no poisonous mushrooms have mixed in before cooking. It would also be good to remove dirt and such at that time.

Using Wood Magic, I quickly made a cooking station, and with Earth Magic, a hearth. Everyone divided tasks and started cooking.

“Hmm. Cooking outdoors like this is quite enjoyable.”

“Yes, indeed. The Verdgar Knight Order also used to camp in the forest during training and monster subjugation, so this reminds me of that,” Elmer and Mercedes exchanged words while cutting vegetables. Elmer… seemed quite adept at handling a kitchen knife. I got the impression that the two from the Demon-Slaying Knight Order were accustomed to cooking outdoors.

“We have quite a few truffles. They’ll add fragrance, so let’s try making a sauce and pouring it over sautéed chicken.”

“Hmm. For the boar meat, it would be good to remove the gaminess with herbs and put it in mushroom soup.”

After confirming no poisonous mushrooms were mixed in, we washed them, removed any remaining stem bases, and other prep work, then passed the prepared items one after another to the cooking team. Those cooking were also checking for any poisonous mushrooms, so it should be safe.

An appetizing, savory aroma drifted through the air. We set up tables and chairs on the deck of the Sirius, and our meal began with the truly beautiful scenery of the lake reflecting the landscape like a mirror, the forest beginning to show autumn colors, and the blue sky.

White bread, chicken sauté, mushroom soup. There was also various sautéed mushrooms. Eating under the open sky felt liberating and pleasant.

“This is delicious… It rivals the royal castle’s chefs.”

“Truly. I’d want to welcome you to Silvatoria’s royal castle,” Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana beamed after tasting the chicken sauté.

Hmm. Grace’s cooking skills seem to incorporate techniques from the royal castle’s chefs too. When you put the chicken in your mouth, the truffle’s aroma spreads. The right amount of saltiness and meat juices stimulate the appetite.

…This is really good.

“The mushroom soup is warming.”

“Marie and I made several varieties, so there’s seconds,” Claudia said with a smile, and Rosemary closed her eyes, covering her mouth with a feather fan.

There was a spicy one using spices and a creamy one like white stew. The spicy one seemed to be seasoned by Rosemary. This kind of complex blending must be her specialty. She seems to have researched it well.

“Delicious… I’ve never eaten anything this tasty before.”

“This bubbly drink too… It’s sweet and delicious, Harold,” Harold and Cynthia widened their eyes with each bite. Hmm. Both the mushroom dishes and the carbonated drink seemed to be well-received by the two, which is great. After the meal, I’ll let them rest a bit, then I should show them around inside the ship.

# **340 – The Fate of the Bloodline**

After finishing our mushroom-filled lunch and relaxing for a bit, I took Harold and Cynthia on a tour of the Sirius. As expected, their main interest seemed to be the bridge with its various equipment like the speaking tubes and crystal panels, but I decided to show them the cabins and corridors first.

“Theodore here. Currently in the starboard forward corridor. Can you hear me, Your Highness Stephania?”

“Yes. I can hear you, Theodore. This is the bridge. How are things going?”

“Quite smoothly.”

We exchanged conversations with Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana on the bridge using the speaking tubes installed throughout the ship. Since I was guiding Harold and the others, I had the two of them stay on the bridge to respond via the speaking tubes. As expected, both of them happily accepted the role. I could also hear Irmhild and the others’ performances and singing voices.

“This is fascinating!”

My sister Cynthia’s eyes sparkled at the conversation through the speaking tubes.

“Amazing… It’s like a mansion floating in the sky,” Harold said, his eyes widening as he peeked at the interior and cabins.

After making a round of the ship, we returned to the bridge.

“Shall we take a lap around the lake like this?”

“That sounds lovely. The scenery is beautiful too.”

When I placed my hand over the crystal orb to project the outside scenery onto the crystal panel, the siblings’ eyes widened in amazement.

I lifted the Sirius and began circling the lake at a leisurely pace. Watching the passing scenery, the siblings seemed to be enjoying themselves. I decided to continue slowly circling while relaxing.

“By the way… are monsters in this forest area not a problem?”

As the flight was stable, I was steering while sipping tea from a wooden cup when Alfred asked me.

“They rarely appear around here. Since this is Father’s direct territory, the Count’s knights patrol regularly.”

The forest near the Barony of Silun was indeed a place where monsters frequently appeared, but perhaps because of that. They had forest garrisons stationed in the woods anticipating monsters flowing in from that direction, and also had patrols from the County side.

“Is that so? Well, since these two are gravekeepers and work in the forest, I thought it would be good if they could escape from monsters using magic tools.”

“Ah, that’s true. There are barriers for monsters around Mother’s house too, but having one just in case would be reassuring. Do you have Levitation Magic Tools?”

“I brought enough for both of them as spares. I anticipated we might have someone ride the Sirius. If we run out, I can make more.”

“I see.”

Alfred came prepared with work tools, it seemed.

Anyway, if he had spares, we might as well give them to the two.

So after making several laps around the lake, I parked the Sirius again and gave Harold and Cynthia the Levitation Magic Tools, also giving them instructions on how to use them.

The Levitation Magic Tools Alfred brought seemed to be belts with magic stones embedded in them.

“Could you wear these when working in the forest?”

“This is… what is it?”

“It lets you use magic to float things. Magicians use Levitation in various convenient ways… well, you can also fly to escape in emergencies.”

Showing an example would be faster than explaining verbally. I used Levitation to jump.

I flew a considerable distance from the lakeshore, grabbed onto a branch, and leaped up into the treetops. Then I moved from tree to tree through the canopy. It requires some practice, but it’s significantly faster than running away, and by moving at height you can create distance from enemies.

“That brings back memories. When I learned to use Levitation, I was also taught to use jumping to escape.”

Princess Stephania smiled seeing this, and Rosemary seemed to nod slightly.

It’s a fundamental technique, you could say. Rosemary also used Levitation for evasion when she fought me before… So the Verdgar royal family teaches Levitation usage that way.

“Th-this must be expensive, right?”

“We made them ourselves, so the materials didn’t cost much.”

“For now, rather than considering it a gift, think of it as providing work tools to help you continue your gravekeeping duties for Mother safely.”

“Work tools…”

Harold murmured while holding the magic tool. It’s just like the mountain knife hanging from Harold’s waist. These two do their work properly and wouldn’t treat it as a toy or show it off.

“Actually, you can use it even outside of emergencies. Like using Levitation to move fallen trees.”

“Though you’ll use up magical power accordingly.”

They’ll learn to gauge that and get used to it as they use it more.

“Understood. In that case, we’ll gratefully make use of it.”

“We’ll take good care of it!”

I smiled and nodded at the siblings’ responses. They immediately began practicing with the magic tools. Well then, I should explain the usage a bit more.

“First, practice jumping and landing in an open area to get used to the sensation. Once you’re comfortable, practice jumping to grab tree branches. After that, try moving from branch to branch. When your magical power runs low, you’ll feel a unique sluggishness, so you’ll know immediately. When that happens, refrain from using it that day.”

Since the magic tool responds to your will, it’s surprisingly intuitive to use. Things like cutting Levitation during descent and falling straight down won’t happen unless you intentionally do so.

“Understood.”

“Amazing, I’m jumping so high!”

After finishing the explanations, Harold and Cynthia immediately began happily practicing their jumps.

When considering where would be most suitable to create the stone monument for teleporting to Gartner County, the hidden room in Mother’s house would be best.

Since it’s originally covered by a barrier and no one can enter without me, Grace, or Father being there, and with it being a hidden room inside that, you couldn’t ask for better security.

I went to the study with Claudia and decided to have her install the stone monument in the hidden room downstairs.

Claudia raised her hand, and as green light gathered, a stone monument was created.

“It’s done.”

“Yeah. Now we can come to the County too.”

Next is the Marquisate of Broderick. I heard there’s a temple of considerable size there, so it shouldn’t be a problem.

“Hmm… Patricia’s study, is it?”

Old Sigmund closed his eyes while touching the table installed in Mother’s hidden room, as if pondering something.

“Was there a large cauldron set up here?”

“Yes. Mother’s notes were also here.”

“I see…”

Valentina also had a distant look in her eyes as she said that. Perhaps she was imagining Mother in her day, doing research here and such.

After gazing around the hidden room for a while, we returned to the living room where everyone was.

Then—a communication came through on the communication device. From Auria, the Guild Master of the Termwills Adventurer Guild.

“‘Tis Auria. Is this communication working? Regarding the vampire incident in the eastern countries, I investigated the information available at the Guild and wish to report the results.”

Auria sometimes attends meetings with adventurer guilds from various regions, and adventurer guilds record and share information about what kind of monsters appear where, especially for significant ones.

So I had contacted Auria to see if she could investigate the vampire incidents east of the Marquisate of Broderick. Partly as a precaution before visiting, and also because if any vampire-related incidents occurred in the east, they might be connected to Grace’s parents.

When we stopped by the Barony of Silun, I could have asked Beryne, but investigations take time, and in that regard, Auria, who has a communication device for coordinating against demons, doesn’t have such limitations.

“Yes, the communication is working fine.”

After I replied, the response came back after a short while.

“Hmm. Then… let us get to the main point. To conclude, it seems there was quite a powerful vampire in the eastern countries. There have been many vampire disturbances since ancient times, and most importantly, records from over a decade ago mention that a noble family was involved with vampires…”

…A noble involved with vampires.

“May I hear the details?”

“One day, the family head, his wife, and even their newborn daughter suddenly went missing. When officials and retainers searched for them, they discovered the basement of the mansion. Unfortunately, they encountered the vampire who had returned and suffered significant casualties. According to survivors… the vampire was the spitting image of a portrait of a family head from many generations ago displayed in the noble house.”

“Was the original missing family head a vampire?”

“I know not. The Guild investigated that point as well. Some had seen him out in the sunlight. But according to testimonies, around the time of his marriage, he became sickly and no one saw the family head outside. The vampire that attacked the search party disappeared along with a coffin from the basement, and since then, the number of vampire disturbances in the eastern countries has visibly decreased.”

That family head from many generations ago was probably the true master of the house. Having a noble family title would make various activities easier.

But isn’t this story connected to Grace’s origins? There are too many matching elements.

The decrease in vampire incidents… probably means they fled with their entire colony after their identity was exposed. Also because they let Grace and the others escape. We don’t know how much information was leaked.

But if that’s the case, there shouldn’t be any concern about approaching the east now.

The remaining question is… where that vampire fled to—

“Were there no increases in vampire incidents in the southern regions afterward?”

I asked through the communication device.

“The south? I shall investigate.”

“Thank you. There’s no hurry.”

“Hmm. Leave it to me.”

…Somehow, it’s just a hunch, but it’s possible they fled to the south and connected with Gardinis’s cult. Virginia also seemed to be a vampire with considerable power.

# **341 – The Spirit's Wish**

“That’s quite a catch.”

Sheila returned from the lake with a fishing rod in hand. Her catch seemed plentiful, with a decent number of fish in her bucket. Sheila looked somewhat proud. Having mushrooms and fish has been making our meals quite satisfying, which I’m grateful for.

“Well then, dinner will be mushroom and fish dishes, I suppose.”

“How about steaming them together?”

Everyone began discussing today’s menu. The atmosphere was warm and cheerful.

…Now then. With things as they are, I don’t have enough information. Even if I were to give Grace more detailed information about my earlier exchange with Auria, it would be better to wait until the investigation has progressed a bit further.

I should probably wait until I have some leads on the noble families that might be connected to Grace, as well as where the Vampires fled to. Without knowing those things, the information would be incomplete, making it difficult to decide how to proceed. Time to shift my thinking.

“Your Highness Stephania and Your Highness Adriana, will you be staying on the Sirius today?”

“For lodging, yes. But I’d like to have dinner with everyone.”

“Understood.”

There’s still time before dinner. Since I’ve mostly finished what needed to be done in Gartner County and what I had planned, I can relax for a while, but I don’t want my magic senses to dull from taking too long a break.

There were also some experiments I wanted to try based on Mother’s notes, so I decided to go out in front of the house to practice magic.

“I’ll be outside practicing magic for a bit.”

“Understood.”

“Hmm. I find myself interested when it comes to your magic practice.”

Grace nodded, and Old Sigmund spoke. Rosemary, Charlotte, Princess Stephania, and Princess Adriana also seemed interested as they looked my way.

“Feel free to watch. I’m researching the magic my mother left behind. I thought it would be a good opportunity to continue that work here.”

I answered with a wry smile.

“That makes it even more intriguing.”

Old Sigmund nodded. In the end, everyone ended up coming outside… but I suppose it’s fine.

I moved to a spot a little distance from the house and took up Ouroboros in my Stance.

What I’m practicing is the magic Mother was researching. It’s a Technique whose ultimate goal is to neutralize the Magical Power present in the natural environment and absorb it into oneself. It draws on our previous discussion about the origins of Spell Formulas with Old Sigmund and the others, but I’ve been gradually building the Spell Formula by gathering usable parts from various other Techniques.

“Well then…”

I gripped Ouroboros, raised my Magical Power, and released it outside my body, wrapping it around Ouroboros. The released Magical Power took on a snake-like Form, emitting a pale blue glow as it spiraled around the surface of Ouroboros and my own body.

Releasing Magical Power outside the body and keeping it under control to handle more Magical Power than the body could normally contain… that’s a method I’ve used before in battles with Demons.

The theory is to treat the Magical Power spiraling around my body as a pseudo-representation of the Magical Power inside a human body, gather the surrounding Magical Power here to assimilate it, and by skipping the neutralization part, enable the handling of large amounts of Magical Power.

The spiral of Magical Power gathered at the tip of Ouroboros, forming a vortex. This part references the Spell Formula I used when assembling the Sirius’s outer hull.

“That Magic… it’s a Spell Formula I haven’t seen before.”

“It’s Magic my mother was researching. It was apparently a Spell Formula meant to overcome her own constitution by gathering and neutralizing Magical Power from the surroundings… but I thought if applied, it might allow me to use more Magical Power in battle.”

“…I see. Yes, Patricia was indeed like that.”

“The glow of the Magical Power… it’s beautiful.”

While answering Old Sigmund, I gave myself plenty of leeway to maintain control, gradually drawing in the surrounding Magical Power as I enlarged the vortex. I gathered minuscule amounts of Magical Power from the surroundings, swallowing them in the vortex. Small particles of light were swallowed by the vortex, eventually forming a glowing orb of Magical Power. When I activated a Spell Formula using that Magical Power refined outside my body, it created a wind that swept up fallen leaves.

Hmm. This might be practical? I scattered the unused Magical Power back into the surroundings, as if reversing the Spell Formula.

“Hmm…?”

It was Tephra who made that sound. Seraphina and Alpha also seemed to sense something as they looked around. Their gazes were directed toward Mother’s house.

Something—a mist-like substance—emerged from the giant tree. It was… gathering the Magical Power I had scattered?

Simultaneously, I sensed a Magical Power presence. Is this… a Spirit? It doesn’t seem to have fully materialized yet.

“Hmm? It doesn’t seem to be anything to worry about. Theodore gathered Magical Power from the surroundings, so it was probably stimulated by that. My presence here likely had some influence too…”

“…I see.”

Just as the Miasma Orb affected Seraphina, perhaps Tephra’s stay has activated the Spirit.

In a combat situation, I would have used up all the gathered Magical Power in Spell Formulas, but this time I had no target. As I directed the Magical Power scattering into the surroundings toward it, the Spirit absorbed it, and its presence grew stronger.

It was probably an entity that originally accumulated power by storing the Magical Power of this area. That’s why it has high affinity with the gathered Magical Power and might find it easy to absorb as a Spirit.

From the Spirit’s perspective, it’s as if high-quality nutrients suddenly appeared nearby.

Like roots absorbing nutrients, the Spirit stored Magical Power… and the indistinct mist gradually took on a more human-like Form.

The light enveloping the Spirit intensified, and a glowing silhouette slowly descended to the ground. The figure of a girl with green hair. Her sweet scent was that of figs.

The ends of her limbs resembling branches and roots made it immediately clear she wasn’t human. Once she fully materialized, something like clothing wrapped around her body.

It’s… a hat and Robe like what a Witch wears. Probably influenced by the fact that Mother’s house was called a Witch’s house? A Witch’s hat with a fig decoration attached.

Hmm… at this point, there’s no doubt. A tree Spirit—a Dryad. Tephra did hint at its existence, but I didn’t expect to trigger its manifestation.

The Dryad opened her eyes slightly and smiled at me.

“That was really delicious just now, Theodore.”

“Well… I’m glad to hear that.”

So she understands human speech from the start and even knows my name.

I understand that Tephra, who has been active as a Spirit for some time, and Seraphina, who as a Brownie has been closely connected to human settlements from the beginning, can speak human language… but for one who just manifested to be like this is probably because Mother’s house serves as its core.

The clothing she wears is likely based on the image held by the local residents. I get the feeling various elements are mixed in.

“To think a magic experiment would lead to witnessing a Spirit’s manifestation. We got to see something quite rare.”

Rosemary laughed cheerfully.

While preparations for dinner progressed, a discussion took place about what to do with the Spirit. This was because we have plans to depart for the Marquisate of Broderick soon, and leaving behind a Spirit that just manifested was somewhat concerning.

The Dryad herself was sitting by a sunny window, with Seraphina on her lap, basking in the sunlight together with Harvesta, looking perfectly content. It seems she’s taken a liking to Seraphina and Harvesta.

“Hmm. For one who just manifested, she seems to be quite a powerful Spirit, so nothing major should happen… but if you’re worried, wouldn’t it be good to do the same as with me?”

“So the process would be to prepare something connected to the Spirit at Termwills and have her form a contract with me?”

“Indeed.”

Tephra nodded at Claudia’s words.

“In that case, it would be a fig from this house… or perhaps a young fig tree growing nearby. I think it would be fine if we planted that at Theodore’s house. Well, if she herself says she wants to stay here, we won’t force her.”

When Claudia broached the subject, the Dryad responded cheerfully.

“Hmm. I don’t really understand… but I’d rather be with everyone than be alone. It’s been a long time since everyone came, and it’s been lively and fun.”

…Ah, I see. That’s probably why she seized the opportunity presented by Tephra’s visit and my Magic. She prefers it lively… Well, the house is her core.

“…That settles it then. If the Dryad can travel between Mother’s house and Termwills, not only the Dryad herself but also Harold and Cynthia would feel more at ease.”

“Then let’s proceed with the contract. Do you have a name?”

The Dryad shook her head and looked at me. So I’m to name her.

“…How about Floria?”

“Mm. It’s a good name.”

The Dryad—Floria—floated a smile and spoke with a cheerful voice.

It was decided that they would enter the capital city grandly from the main entrance.

Or rather, the moment they used the Griffin delivery, their tracks would surely be followed, so sneaking was already out of the window.

Normally, the Griffin delivery service handles documents and small packages; carrying people requires reporting to various authorities.

The one Yoichi and the others used belonged to the Adventurer’s Guild, but that didn’t exempt them from reporting obligations to the kingdom.

“Well, there’s no need to dutifully report the exact number of people, though.”

“Hmm, that’s true.”

In the first place, the Griffin delivery service could barely fly carrying three adults.

Since it flew the route faster than usual, they weren’t suspected of being overweight.

In the end, it was handled without issue by claiming that only Yoichi and Alana had boarded, they used magical assistance, cut down on rest time, and compressed the travel time.

“Still, it’s as lively a place as ever.”

Yoichi, who had alighted from the carriage, let out a voice of admiration as he surveyed the scene at the capital’s Central Terminal Station, which was bustling with people, carriages, and rickshaws.

Boasting an area of approximately 200,000 square meters, this vast station was a facility like those only seen in international major cities even in his original world.

“Speaking of which, Lord Yoichi, you’ve been here before, haven’t you?”

“Ah, yes. During the Demon invasion, and I was guided by Greta.”

As they could not enter the royal capital or large towns from the sky due to security reasons, the two of them had switched to a carriage from the nearest town.

This carriage heading directly from that town to the Central Terminal Station was something their butler, Vista, had arranged in advance.

“Alright, to get to the Salis family’s mansion… which carriage number should we take, I wonder…”

The street carriages running freely throughout the vast royal capital had countless routes set up, like the subway or bus lines in a big city.

If you took the wrong stop, you could be dropped off somewhere you couldn’t return from, even after walking for several days.

“Maybe someone with a rickshaw would know?”

“Umu, we can ask them.”

Because there were so many routes, the desired boarding area could sometimes be quite far.

Because of this, walking for several dozen minutes was a common occurrence.

That’s where the rickshaws came in; they traveled between the boarding areas like shuttle buses or taxis.

“Hmm?”

As the two were about to walk towards a place where rickshaws were likely to be, their path was blocked by three soldiers.

They were lightly equipped, wearing uniforms with metal gauntlets, metal boots, and a saber at their waist, but you could tell from the bulk of their clothing that they were also wearing chainmail or similar armor underneath.

“You’re Alana and Yoichi of TOKOROTEN, aren’t you?”

The tall man standing on the right stepped in front of Alana and questioned her while ostentatiously looking down on her.

“When you ask someone’s name, it’s proper etiquette to give your own first, isn’t it?”

Such etiquette, at least, did not exist in this kingdom.

This was a line Alana had learned from Japanese historical dramas she watched.

“You bastard, can’t you tell by looking?”

The man, whose eyebrow twitched, puffed out his chest and replied that way, as if to flaunt the embroidered family crest on the chest of his uniform.

The remaining two men held down the one who was trying to draw his sword.

One was around forty, stout but moved without a wasted motion, while the other man appeared to be in his mid-twenties, a slightly smaller young man.

With how I am now, I could probably go for a dual-wielding style with a launcher and machine gun, and if I use my skill, reloading ammo and maintaining the main body takes just a second, so I can attack without rest.”

Should they fear the words about destroying the capital, be dumbfounded by the sheer scale of the talk, or should they feel anger towards them for speaking so nonchalantly about trampling over the capital?

In the midst of that, the first one to react was the tall man.

There was fear on his face, but it seemed to be overcome by anger.

To that man, Alana turned an emotionless face.

It was a bewitching smile, both beautiful and at the same time terrifying.

Her words, calmly spoken, seemed to represent established facts, leaving all three men pressured and their faces contorted.

—the stout man knelt on the spot.

“Hm…”

“I beg you at the cost of my life! Lady Alana Salis! Please accept my master’s invitation…!”

The stout man who introduced himself as Giles was in a posture that seemed to practically say, “Use my own sword to sever my head.”

“A Plea for a Severed Neck…”

It was one of the customs passed down among the Kingdom’s nobility, and as the name and his posture indicated, it was an act of having one’s wish granted in exchange for one’s own neck.

Upon accepting this ‘Plea for a Severed Neck,’ if one severs the supplicant’s head, the recipient must grant that wish.

If it becomes clear that the head was severed and the wish ignored, the person will be charged with murder and usually sentenced to death.

However, if the wish is granted, even if the head is severed, no crime will be charged.

“Hmph… What a bother…”

After blinking as if bored, Alana took the offered sword. And, with the sword still in its sheath, she lightly tapped Giles’s neck.

“Thank you very much!”

Tapping the neck with the sword still in its sheath.

By doing this, it serves as a reply meaning, “I will not take your life, but I will grant your wish.”

“Leave the neck price at the Adventurer’s Guild or somewhere similar.”

“Understood…!”

A supplicant whose neck has been tapped will not have their life taken, but they aren’t spared without compensation either.

Instead of having their neck severed, they must pay a sum called the ‘neck price’ to the other party.

That was money in place of his neck, meaning his life, and he had to atone for it with his entire fortune.

Therefore, from now on, he would undergo an investigation of his assets by the appropriate department in the royal capital and would have to pay the calculated sum to Alana.

Not only cash, land, and houses, but also family members and servants would be assigned a value, and he would need to pay the equivalent amount.

If he couldn’t prepare the money, he would have to sell land and houses, and if that was still insufficient, he would have to prepare the money even by enslaving himself or his family.

“Receiving such a pittance wouldn’t make me happy at all, you know.”

“I am truly sorry…”

Giles lowered his head deeply once more, holding up the sword that had been returned to him.

Although he was the Head Knight, he was, after all, only a quasi-noble for one generation.

While his entire fortune would be enough money for a commoner to live a life of leisure, for Alana, who had made a hefty profit from past activities, the Monster Stampede, and the Demon Invasion subjugation, it was truly nothing more than a pittance.

“In that case, these men will guide you, so please board that carriage.”

Buckling the returned sword at his waist, Giles stood up and tried to usher Alana and Yoichi towards the carriage.

“Hm, was it Giles? Aren’t you going to accompany us?”

“My apologies. I have other duties that require me to leave the royal capital urgently… Of course, if you insist, I will accompany you.”

The tall man revealed his displeasure at the exchange between the two, while the young man seemed slightly flustered.

The tall one seemed like he wanted to complain about something, but perhaps because he had witnessed the plea of neck-severing earlier, he endured without opening his mouth.

“You two, is it alright to leave the guidance of Lady Alana and Sir Yoichi to you?”

“Yes, of course!”

“Um, I… yes, it’s fine.”

“Umu…”

Giles felt that the attitude of his two subordinates was a little strange, but he didn’t take it too seriously, assuming it was due to the exchange between himself and Alana that had just taken place.

“Mister Yoichi, what do you think?”

“Hmm… the old stout man is white, the young one is gray, and the tall one is pitch black.”

“Heh, is that so?”

When Giles, who had finished his exchange with his subordinates, turned his gaze back to Alana, the pair of them were whispering about something, causing him to frown slightly.

“Um, is there some problem?”

“Well, about that, Mr. Giles.”

Alana did not answer Giles’s question; instead, Yoichi stepped forward.

“Is it really okay to leave it to those two… to this Kenneth and Leonard?”

“Hmm, I think I haven’t mentioned their names before?”

To Yoichi’s question, Giles asked back, clearly showing a displeased expression.

While he himself had given his name during the plea of neck-severing earlier, he didn’t recall the other two having introduced themselves.

Normally he wouldn’t care, but perhaps because Alana’s first words to him were something to the effect of “You should introduce yourselves first,” he was bothered by the fact that they had failed to introduce themselves.

Kenneth, the tall one, and Leonard, the young one whose names had been suddenly spoken, were surprised and widened their eyes.

Those words served as a check against Giles, who had anticipated Yoichi’s group’s route beforehand and ambushed them.

Of course, Yoichi had used [Appraisal+] on the spot just now, but to them, who didn’t know Yoichi’s skill, they would probably think he had investigated them in advance.

“In that case, there are no problems. Kenneth, Leonard. I’ll leave the rest to you.”

In response to Giles’s words, Kenneth and Leonard bowed their heads in unison.

### **Chapter 6 – A Glimpse of the Past**

About 30 minutes had passed since Yoichi and the others got on the carriage.

As expected of a vehicle owned by a count’s family, there was no shaking, and the temperature and humidity were kept at a comfortable level.

It felt like staying in a reasonably high-class cottage; you wouldn’t think you were riding in a carriage driving through the town at all.

“Well then, it should be about time.”

Yoichi murmured, looking out the coach window.

Both Yoichi and Alana were quite unfamiliar with the geography of the royal capital, making it almost impossible to figure out their current location just from the view outside.

Added to the fact that it was a world without smartphones or GPS, making their geolocating harder than usual.

“How much longer will it take?”

“If we go straight down this road, we’ll reach the Count Colborn’s mansion in less than 5 minutes.”

Then again, Yoichi had [Appraisal+], which allowed him to accurately know not only his current location but also the location of their destination, Count Colborn’s mansion, the route to get there, and even the estimated time required.

“Senior, are we really going through with this?”

“Of course.”

Just as they were about to reach their destination, the two on the driver’s seat started such a conversation.

Inside the carriage, which was equipped with a soundproofing effect through magic, the voices from the driver’s seat would normally not reach.

However, by using [Appraisal+], Yoichi was also able to know this in real time, rendering the soundproofing measures useless from the getgo.

“Will it work out?”

“A report came in just now, and preparations are complete. From what I heard of the plan, there’s no way it can fail.”

“But, it failed last time, didn’t it?”

“That was because that man called Yoichi interfered. If we lock them both up at once and cut off rescue from the outside, success is certain. Don’t worry.”

“……Maybe we should stop after all? What about the Captain, didn’t he too―”

“I’m sick of working under an incompetent old man whose only good point is being serious!! Listen up! If this plan succeeds, we’ll get a lot of money! Maybe the Count will take notice of us, and our treatment might even get better than it is now after this. Don’t you want that?”

“I’m not saying that I don’t, but…”

“You need money too, don’t you? Or are you saying you’re willing to abandon your sister now? Huh?!”

“Ugh…”

While they were talking like this, the carriage passed their destination.

“I see, the younger one did try to stop it, at least,” Yoichi explained the situation once the conversation on the driver’s seat had finished.

“But, what about his sister?”

“Leonard’s sister was caught and accused of being a honey trap and is currently in custody. If the settlement money isn’t paid by the deadline, it seems she’ll be reduced to slavery.”

“A honey trap? How can I say this… it’s kind of like there’s no helping her…”

“Apparently, she was originally a serious and good girl. But she got caught up with a nasty man, and after that, she got involved in various things, it seems.”

And Leonard’s sister, as usual, lured in a man who looked like he had money, but the target that day was a nasty noble’s spoiled son.

Her boyfriend, who had stormed into the room to threaten the man, was burst in upon by guards waiting in the next room and had his head taken off right there and then. The man was already in too deep for his crimes that the authorities had him killed on site.

The sister too was already a repeat offender by this time, and it seems that the hand of investigation was closing in on her.

With such circumstances, the spoiled noble’s son, of course, was found not guilty.

Leonard’s sister was hit with a high settlement amount.

But for some reason, the spoiled noble took a liking to her and offered a condition to exempt her from paying the settlement money if she became a domestic slave.

“And what are the conditions of being a domestic slave to him?”

“The one with no labor restrictions of course—”

Hearing “no restrictions,” Alana’s expression clouded over slightly.

Just because someone is a slave doesn’t mean the master can treat them however they want.

For example, a domestic slave in this country, as the name suggests, is a slave whose sole responsibility is household chores.

For instance, it is not allowed to make a domestic slave work in places unrelated to housework, such as taking them to a coal mine or having them work on a fishing boat.

Furthermore, in many cases, slaves have labor restrictions imposed on them.

Even among domestic slaves, restrictions vary; for example, they might be allowed to clean but not cook, or allowed to do minor tidying but not carry heavy loads.

Of course, forcing sexual relations on them against their will is also prohibited.

In this kingdom, by determining categories of slaves and imposing further detailed restrictions, they protect their human rights to some extent.

And having no labor restrictions means they can be made to do some heavy labor related to household chores, and sexual service is also included in housework.

“So, in order to save his pitiful sister, the kind big brother is going to trap us, huh?”

“Hmm… it doesn’t seem like there’s any room for sympathy.”

“Oh, by the way, the tall one is just scum who wants money and status the easy way, so you don’t need to worry about him either.”

“Is that so? To hire such a person as a knight, the people of the Colborn family have no eye for judging people.”

“It seems he’s only good on the outside. There exist those kinds of people, you know?”

Kenneth, the tall knight, was a typical authoritarian, fawning over his superiors and looking down on his subordinates.

It was precisely because he looked down on adventurers as being below him that he took a rude attitude towards Alana.

Normally, it would be an issue for a mere ordinary knight to take such an attitude towards a high-rank adventurer, but in the royal capital, there was a peculiar custom where the kingdom’s nobility held a slight advantage over the Adventurer’s Guild.

The place Hazel guided them to was the lord’s bedroom.

Though called a bedroom, it was more like a hotel suite, fully equipped not only with a bed but also a toilet, shower, and a simple kitchenette.

They supposedly had enough food stockpiled to hole up for about a month without issue, and regarding meals, it seemed they were being brought whatever they wished.

As of now, there appeared to be no inconvenience other than being unable to go outside.

Two guards stood on either side of the bedroom door.

Their attire, consisting of thick clothing over scale mail, gauntlets, and metal boots, was similar to the equipment worn by Giles, who conducted a plea for a severed neck, Kenneth, Leonard, and others.

This equipment was commonly seen on guards stationed close to the lord, like the personal guard within the knights, but the guards this time were of a different rank.

“Oh, the Royal Guards are actually deployed here?”

One glance at the emblem embroidered on their chests was enough to tell they were Royal Guards.

Perhaps this was a consideration to avoid provoking William by having incompetent nobles stand guard.

After all, it was not often that Royal Guards were tasked with duties away from the Royal Castle.

One man and one woman stood on the left and right of the door respectively, each wearing a saber at their waist and holding a short spear upright, ready.

In places with high ceilings and wide corridors like a noble’s mansion, it was possible to swing a short spear even indoors.

As Alana approached the bedroom, short spears were extended from both sides of the door, blocking her path.

“You cannot pass here,” the female soldier declared.

“My apologies, but I have an urgent matter for my father. If you cannot let me pass, could you at least call him out?”

“Margrave Sarris cannot be let out of the room.”

“Umu. Then how exactly am I supposed to speak with my father?”

“There’s no way you can speak with him, is there? Leave immediately.”

“Is that so…”

Alana sighed tiredly but immediately changed her expression and stared at the female soldier.

“As B-rank adventurer Alana, I declare that I have business beyond this point and will be passing through.”

“Didn’t I say you can’t!”

“What’s with you…”

“Hey!!”

Perhaps thinking she was being mocked, the female Royal Guard pointed her spearhead at Alana.

“Senior! Don’t get in my way!!”
